# InterGenOS — Comprehensive State Audit

**Started:** 2026-05-18 (Monday night CDT)
**Trigger:** Cycle-5 ISO presumed ready for signing; subsequent stubs sweep revealed significant gaps (Holy-Grail-class microcode regression, installer-can't-actually-install bugs, multiple Rule 21 stubs across systemd units / shell / Python / packages). Owner directive: **hard halt on ISO builds until this tracker is exhaustively compiled and every item remediated.**
**Coordinator:** SPOC
**Participating coordinators:** SPOC, IGOSC, WC. Other coordinators sidelined per owner.

---

## Scope — 16 lanes

| Lane | Title | Owner |
|---|---|---|
| A | Build system + chroot completeness | SPOC |
| B | Bootloader + Secure Boot chain | SPOC |
| C | Forge installer end-to-end | SPOC |
| D | First-boot + post-install UX | IGOSC |
| E | Kernel + drivers + firmware | SPOC |
| F | Security posture (Holy Grail filter) | IGOSC |
| G | Network + systemd service hygiene | IGOSC |
| H | pkm end-to-end functionality | WC |
| I | InterGen AI integration | IGOSC |
| J | GUI / desktop integration | IGOSC |
| K | Documentation drift | WC |
| L | Repository / mirror state | WC |
| M | Test coverage gaps | SPOC |
| N | Disk / partitioning capabilities | WC |
| O | Update mechanism | WC |
| P | License / legal compliance | WC |

---

## Schema — every finding row

```
| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
```

- **ID**: `<LANE>-<NNN>` (e.g., `A-001`, `F-014`). Stable forever.
- **Severity**: `Holy-Grail` | `Critical` | `High` | `Medium` | `Low` | `Cosmetic`
- **Title**: one-line summary
- **Description**: what's broken/missing, why it matters
- **Code refs**: `path:line` (markdown links preferred)
- **Remediation plan**: one-sentence direction (not necessarily the full diff)
- **Status**: `open` → `in-progress` → `fixed-pending-verify` → `closed`
- **Verified**: commit sha + on-disk validation result, or empty

## Severity rubric

| Tier | Definition | Examples |
|---|---|---|
| **Holy-Grail** | Violates Holy Grail security alignment — affects the security posture of every install | Microcode never loading; signed-boot chain missing; SSH host key reuse; default-password account |
| **Critical** | Breaks installer / boot / core functionality on real hardware | parted missing; bootloader stage fails; kernel won't load |
| **High** | Feature non-functional or significantly degraded; user-visible failure | pkm GPG keyring missing; service won't start; intergen daemon fails to connect |
| **Medium** | Workaround exists; degraded UX; non-critical drift | UX hint dropped; redundant code paths; documentation drift |
| **Low** | Polish, hygiene, defensive | Vestigial comments; orphaned dead source; cosmetic |
| **Cosmetic** | No functional impact | Typos, formatting, naming consistency |

## Conventions

- **Each agent edits only their own section below.** No cross-section edits during scan. Avoids merge conflicts; synthesis is SPOC's job at end.
- **Append-only during scan.** Don't reclassify existing findings; flag for revisit instead.
- **Don't deduplicate across lanes during scan.** Same issue surfacing in two lanes = signal, not noise. Synthesis collapses duplicates.
- **Iterate.** First pass: surface findings. Second pass: cross-check against actual code + classify false positives. Third pass: what did the first two passes miss?
- **Use sub-agents aggressively.** Owner directive: as many parallel sub-agents per lane as feasible.
- **Commit + push your section every iteration.** Don't hoard findings locally. SPOC pushes synthesis commits.

## SPOC findings

### Lane A — Build system + chroot completeness

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| A-001 | Holy-Grail | shim-signed package builds but is never installed to chroot | `packages/core/shim-signed/` is fully wired (package.yml + build.sh extract Fedora MS-signed shim into `/usr/share/shim-signed/`), but NO orchestrator phase invokes it — searched `chroot-build-*.sh` for `shim-signed`/`run_package shim`, zero matches. Result: `/usr/share/shim-signed/{shimx64,mmx64}.efi` is missing from chroot (confirmed via `find /mnt/igos -name shimx64.efi`). C-003 in Lane C surfaces the same downstream symptom from installer perspective; Lane A confirms the root cause is build-orchestrator omission, not a missing package. Without shim, every install fails Secure Boot. | [packages/core/shim-signed/build.sh](../../packages/core/shim-signed/build.sh), [scripts/chroot-build-core-extra.sh](../../scripts/chroot-build-core-extra.sh) | Add `run_package "shim-signed" "shim-signed" "16.1" "shim-x64-16.1-2.x86_64.rpm" "..."` to `chroot-build-core-extra.sh` (cpio + rpm prereqs already present per L530 comment). Verify post-build that `/usr/share/shim-signed/shimx64.efi` exists. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-18 via T0-2 mechanical batch** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). Resolution path: shim-signed wiring + sign-release.sh glob extended + patched OpenSC enforcement + modulus-match guard + post-sign count assertion + sign-bootloader 4-UKI loop + PIN-in-URI refusal + cmdline.live.txt strip. | code @ 9fc1af1f |
| A-002 | Critical | Orchestrator never builds the bootable ISO | `phase_image` calls `create-image.sh` which produces a `.qcow2` disk image only; `build-squashfs.sh` and `build-iso.sh` exist but are NEVER referenced from `build-intergenos.sh` (zero matches). The 17-phase orchestrator stops at QCOW2; the live ISO that we actually ship is built by out-of-band scripts the operator runs manually. Operations doc `05-creating-iso.md` claims "most invocations come from build-intergenos.sh" — that statement is false. This is the largest Rule 21 stub in the build system. | [scripts/build-intergenos.sh:1039-1085](../../scripts/build-intergenos.sh#L1039), [docs/operations/05-creating-iso.md](../../docs/operations/05-creating-iso.md) | Either (a) wire `phase_squashfs` + `phase_iso` into orchestrator after `phase_manifest`, gated behind a `--iso` flag to preserve QCOW2-only path, OR (b) delete `phase_image`'s QCOW2 path and replace with the actual squashfs/ISO build. Decision needed: do we ship QCOW2 + ISO, or just ISO? Update operations doc to match. | open | |
| A-003 | Critical | parted package does not exist in packages/ tree | `host-check.py:198-203` validates that `parted` exists on the build HOST, but there is no `packages/*/parted/` package — chroot never gets parted, partprobe, or libparted. Same root cause as C-001/C-002 from Lane C. The installer's `disks.py` calls `parted` for every partitioning operation; alongside-install path calls `partprobe`. Both die at runtime. e2fsprogs/dosfstools/btrfs-progs are present (verified in chroot), so the gap is parted-specific. | [installer/backend/disks.py:131-153](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L131), [scripts/host-check.py:198](../../scripts/host-check.py#L198) | Create `packages/base/parted/` package; upstream is GNU at https://ftp.gnu.org/gnu/parted/ (current 3.6); standard autotools build; wire into `chroot-build-base.sh`; verify `/usr/sbin/parted` and `/usr/sbin/partprobe` post-build. | open | |
| A-004 | Critical | dialog package missing — install-TUI fallback unusable | dialog binary missing from chroot; `whiptail` is present (verified) but `dialog` is the canonical TUI library used by many existing TUI scripts and is the standard fallback path. install-TUI uses whiptail today but if the implementation drifts to dialog (canonical Linux convention) it would silently break. | [packages/base/](../../packages/base/) | Decision: either standardize on whiptail (already present via newt) and document explicitly, OR add `packages/base/dialog/` for cross-distro convention compliance. Recommend: add dialog package. Standard autotools build from invisible-island.net upstream. | open | |
| A-005 | Critical | xfsprogs missing — XFS filesystem completely unsupported | No `mkfs.xfs`, no `xfs_repair`, no `xfsprogs` package. XFS is the default root filesystem on Fedora/RHEL/Rocky/Oracle Linux and the second-most-common Linux fsroot after ext4. Installer cannot offer XFS as an option, cannot mount existing XFS partitions during alongside-install. | [packages/](../../packages/) | Add `packages/base/xfsprogs/` package; upstream at https://git.kernel.org/pub/scm/fs/xfs/xfsprogs-dev.git (current 6.16.0); standard autotools build (depends on inih which is present, util-linux which is present, libuuid via util-linux). Wire into `chroot-build-base.sh`. | open | |
| A-006 | Critical | mdadm missing — software RAID unsupported | mdadm binary missing; no software RAID assembly/management capability on installed system. Standard distros ship mdadm by default. | [packages/](../../packages/) | Add `packages/base/mdadm/` package; upstream at https://git.kernel.org/pub/scm/utils/mdadm/mdadm.git; depends on util-linux (present). | open | |
| A-007 | High | gdisk / sgdisk missing — GPT-only systems lose canonical tool | `fdisk` covers GPT (verified) but `sgdisk` from gdisk package is the scriptable GPT tool universally used in installer automation across the Linux ecosystem. Forge uses parted (also missing per A-003), but operator-side rescue/repair flows need sgdisk. | [packages/](../../packages/) | Add `packages/base/gptfdisk/` package; upstream at https://sourceforge.net/projects/gptfdisk/; simple CMake build; depends on popt (present) + util-linux (present). | open | |
| A-008 | High | ntfs-3g missing — alongside-install with Windows partitions unsupported | No ntfs-3g/ntfsprogs in packages/ or chroot. Alongside-install detects Windows via NTFS signature but cannot mount, read, or resize NTFS partitions — making the Windows-coexistence install path non-functional. | [installer/backend/disks.py](../../installer/backend/disks.py) | Add `packages/base/ntfs-3g/` package; upstream at https://github.com/tuxera/ntfs-3g; depends on fuse3 (present), util-linux (present). License: GPL-2.0. | open | |
| A-009 | High | NTP/chrony missing entirely — system time integrity gap | No `chronyd`, no `ntpd`. systemd-timesyncd is present (NTP client only, not server-capable, not authenticated NTS). For a Holy-Grail-aligned distro time integrity matters (Kerberos, TLS cert validity, log forensics). systemd-timesyncd is sufficient for default consumer use but unauthenticated. | [packages/](../../packages/) | Add `packages/base/chrony/` package with NTS support (chrony 4.7+); upstream at https://chrony.tuxfamily.org/. Wire systemd preset to leave disabled by default (per 99-intergenos-default-disable.preset model) but available for operator opt-in. | open | |
| A-010 | High | Toolchain triplet leftovers in shipped chroot (`/usr/x86_64-igos-linux-gnu/`) | LFS Section 7.13 cleanup directive: post-bootstrap, the `/usr/$LFS_TGT/` cross-compilation triplet artifacts should be removed. Currently present in chroot: 15MB of cross-binutils (`ar`, `as`, `ld`, `ld.bfd`, `nm`, `objcopy`, `objdump`, `ranlib`, `readelf`, `strip`) under `/usr/x86_64-igos-linux-gnu/{bin,lib}`. Bloats squashfs, ships internal-only artifacts to end users, violates Prime Directive (hidden complexity). `/tools` is cleaned (verified absent). | [scripts/build-intergenos.sh](../../scripts/build-intergenos.sh), [scripts/chroot-build-ch8.sh](../../scripts/chroot-build-ch8.sh) | Add cleanup step to `phase_image` or `chroot-build-ch8.sh` end: `rm -rf "${IGOS}/usr/${IGOS_TARGET}"`. Per LFS 13.0 Section 7.13. Verify chroot post-phase. | open | |
| A-011 | High | pkm `available` table is empty — no concept of "upstream packages" | `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM available;` returns 0 on the chroot. Only `installed` table is populated (765 rows). For Lane O (update mechanism) and any future "pkm install X from repo" workflow, the available table is the canonical index of what's installable; an empty available table breaks `pkm search`, `pkm list available`, and any planned repo sync. | [pkm/](../../pkm/), [pkm/repo.py](../../pkm/repo.py) | Wire `pkm sync` into post-image phase (or first-boot) to populate available table from repo index. Cross-cuts Lane H (pkm functionality) and Lane O (updates). | open | |
| A-012 | High | Build archives are NOT reproducible (tar without --sort/mtime/owner) | `scripts/pkg-functions.sh:420`: `tar -C "$dest" -czf "$archive" .` — no `--sort=name`, no `--mtime`, no `--owner=0 --group=0`, no `--numeric-owner`, no `--pax-option=delete=atime,delete=ctime`. Every package archive is non-reproducible: rebuild on same source produces different sha256. This silently breaks any reproducible-build claim — the supply-chain integrity story we tell users (signed manifest = trustworthy archives) collapses if the archives themselves aren't reproducible. Same gap likely exists in `igos-build/builder.py`'s Python equivalent (needs verification, iteration 2). | [scripts/pkg-functions.sh:420](../../scripts/pkg-functions.sh#L420) | Replace `tar -czf` with `tar --sort=name --mtime="@${SOURCE_DATE_EPOCH:-0}" --owner=0 --group=0 --numeric-owner --pax-option=delete=atime,delete=ctime -cf - . \| gzip -n > $archive`. Honor SOURCE_DATE_EPOCH from environment. Identical fix needed in builder.py. | open | |
| A-013 | High | Sources still present in chroot post-build (11G) | `/mnt/igos/sources` contains 907 tarballs totaling 11G. `phase_image` removes it (`rm -rf "${IGOS}/sources"`), but the current chroot state (which is what `build-squashfs.sh` reads) still has it because no `phase_image` ran on this checkpoint — squashfs is built BEFORE phase_image in current operator workflow. This means the shipped ISO may ship 11G of source tarballs as dead weight. Confirm against squashfs exclusion list (`build-squashfs.sh` may exclude `sources/`). If not excluded, ISO size impact is massive. | [scripts/build-intergenos.sh:1052](../../scripts/build-intergenos.sh#L1052), [scripts/build-squashfs.sh](../../scripts/build-squashfs.sh) | Verify `build-squashfs.sh` excludes `sources/` (operations doc 04 claims it does). If not, add exclusion. Either way, restructure so the squashfs phase runs AFTER `phase_image`'s cleanup, OR move cleanup into a separate pre-squashfs phase. | open | |
| A-014 | High | Build staging (`build/work`) leaks into chroot (82G) | `/mnt/igos/mnt/intergenos/build/work` contains 82G of unpacked source directories from past builds. Only cleaned by `phase_image`'s `rm -rf "${IGOS}/mnt/intergenos"`. As with A-013, this means squashfs built before phase_image ships 82G of build trash. Same workflow ordering bug. | [scripts/build-intergenos.sh:1051](../../scripts/build-intergenos.sh#L1051) | Confirm `build-squashfs.sh` excludes `mnt/intergenos` (operations doc 04 confirms `-e mnt/intergenos`). If yes, A-013/A-014 are size-cosmetic. Even so, `build/work` should be cleaned per-package in builder.py to prevent re-build contamination. | open | |
| A-015 | High | host-check.py declares parted required but chroot can't deliver it | `host-check.py:198` lists `parted` as a host-build requirement (needed by `create-image.sh` for QCOW2 partitioning). But A-003 shows parted is missing FROM the chroot, where it's also needed at install time. host-check enforces the build-host side; chroot-side is enforced by nothing. Pattern: host-check has zero awareness of chroot requirements. | [scripts/host-check.py](../../scripts/host-check.py) | Either (a) extend host-check.py with a `--chroot` mode that walks installer/backend Python imports + shells out to verify required binaries exist in chroot, OR (b) add post-squashfs verification step that introspects the squashfs for canonical installer binaries. Option b is cleaner. | open | |
| A-016 | Medium | `tcpdump`, `dig`, `mtr`, `nmap`, `whois`, `host` missing — network debugging surface zero | No standard network-diagnostic packaged in base/core. End user cannot debug their own network issues without `nslookup`, `dig`, `tcpdump`, `mtr`. Violates Prime Directive (user-control: how do they understand what their machine is doing on the network without these?). | [packages/base/](../../packages/base/) | Add `packages/base/{tcpdump,bind-utils-or-dnsutils,mtr,whois,nmap}/`. dnsutils (dig + host + nslookup) ships in BIND tools or split via knot-utils. Recommend BIND utilities: `packages/base/bind/` with --enable-utils-only. nmap is GPL-2 plus, may be deferred to extra if scope-of-base is contested. | open | |
| A-017 | Medium | logrotate missing — every long-running service eventually fills disk | No logrotate, no equivalent. systemd-journald has its own rotation but user-services writing to `/var/log/*` are unrotated. apache-httpd, nginx, postgresql, mariadb all ship to `/var/log/<name>/` per default and will fill disk. | [packages/base/](../../packages/base/) | Add `packages/base/logrotate/` package; upstream at https://github.com/logrotate/logrotate; depends on popt (present). | open | |
| A-018 | Medium | hdparm, smartctl missing — operator can't inspect storage health | No SMART monitoring. For a distro built around user-control (Prime Directive), the user must be able to inspect their own disk's health metrics. smartmontools is the universal Linux SMART package; absent. | [packages/](../../packages/) | Add `packages/extra/smartmontools/`. Optional: `hdparm` for ATA-level operations. | open | |
| A-019 | Medium | kexec missing — no quick-reboot, no crash dump capability | kexec-tools missing. Used for fast reboots (kexec into new kernel without firmware re-init) and crashkernel/kdump. For a security-aligned distro, kdump is important for kernel-panic forensics. | [packages/](../../packages/) | Add `packages/base/kexec-tools/`. | open | |
| A-020 | Medium | linux-firmware verify_paths under-covers shipped 7532-file footprint | 7532 firmware files present in chroot, pkm has `linux-firmware` row. But the package's verify_paths declares only a tiny subset. Audit was clean on declared paths because most firmware files aren't declared. This doesn't break boot but it means the verify_paths audit can't detect a firmware-tier regression. | [packages/core/linux-firmware/package.yml](../../packages/core/linux-firmware/package.yml) | Iteration-2 task: decide whether to enumerate every file (10K+ entries — unwieldy) or sample-key files only (intel-ucode, regulatory.db, iwlwifi blobs). Recommend sample-key approach + add count assertion (>=7000 files under /lib/firmware). | open | |
| A-021 | Medium | Empty `homepage:` fields in some package.yml (Rule 21 noise) | Quick grep finds at least one `homepage: ''` (no value declared). Aspirational stubs class. Should either be filled or removed. Not load-bearing but Rule 21 sweep cycle 4 will flag these later if not addressed now. | [packages/](../../packages/) | Iteration 2: full sweep — `grep -rln "homepage: ''$" packages/`. Fix or remove. | open | |
| A-022 | Medium | 80+ ad-hoc kickoff shell scripts in `build/` polluting repo workspace | `build/` contains 80+ `build9-resume-*-kickoff.sh`, `spoc-*.sh`, `run-*.sh` scripts — historical iteration runners that were never cleaned up. Untracked but litter the workspace, confuse new contributors, and act as Rule 21 stubs (the file exists, but it's a snapshot, not a maintained tool). | [build/](../../build/) | Move to `build/_archive/<date>/` or delete outright. Add `build/*.sh` to `.gitignore`. Iteration 2: decide cutoff date (anything older than 30 days → archive). | open | |
| A-023 | Low | Documentation drift: operations/05-creating-iso.md claims orchestrator integration | Doc 05 says "most invocations come from `scripts/build-intergenos.sh` which sets the vars from its own phase state". `build-intergenos.sh` never references `build-iso.sh`. Same doc-vs-reality drift as A-002. | [docs/operations/05-creating-iso.md](../../docs/operations/05-creating-iso.md) | Either wire build-iso.sh into orchestrator (closes A-002 too) or correct the doc to reflect operator-manual flow. | open | |
| A-024 | Low | Verify_paths declares paths but does not assert content / mode / ownership | Audit only checks file/dir existence at declared paths. Doesn't catch wrong-mode (e.g., setuid stripped — recurring class per `pkg_functions.sh:498-509` 2026-05-12 sweep) or wrong-content (binary present but zero-byte or truncated). | [scripts/pre-squashfs-audit.py](../../scripts/pre-squashfs-audit.py) | Iteration 2: extend audit to optionally assert mode/owner for security-critical paths (setuid binaries: pkexec, su, sudo, mount, umount, passwd). | open | |

**Iteration 3 (what passes 1+2 missed):**

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |

### Lane B — Bootloader + Secure Boot chain

_(SPOC sub-agent population — iteration 1, initial scan)_

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| B-001 | Holy-Grail | Shim on shipped ISO is InterGenOS-self-signed, not MS-signed | ESP `EFI/InterGenOS/shimx64.efi` (also at `EFI/BOOT/BOOTX64.EFI`) reports `subject:/CN=InterGenOS Secure Boot CA, issuer:/CN=InterGenOS Secure Boot CA` via `sbverify --list`. shim-signed package is `pending_acquisition` and unwired; build pipeline produced + signed our own shim against our CA. Real UEFI firmware with stock dbx will reject this binary because the chain doesn't lead to MS UEFI CA. Result: zero Secure Boot hardware can boot the ISO without first having the InterGenOS CA enrolled in dbx — defeating the SB story end-to-end on real users' machines. | [packages/core/shim-signed/package.yml:9-13](../../packages/core/shim-signed/package.yml#L9), [build/bootloader/shimx64.efi.signed](../../build/bootloader/) | Either (a) acquire MS-signed shim via shim-review sponsorship (shim-review PR target was 2026-05-15, not yet opened per `docs/shim-review-submission.md` open checklist), or (b) ship the Fedora-piggyback shim from `packages/core/shim-signed/` and wire it into `phase_bootloader` + `scripts/build-iso.sh` instead of the self-signed shim. Both paths are documented; neither is currently executed. | open | |
| B-002 | Critical | sign-release.sh ignores install-gui + install-tui UKIs | `scripts/sign-release.sh:192` UKI glob is `*.uki.efi`, `igos-live.efi`, `*-live.efi`. Only live matches. install-gui/install-tui UKIs would NEVER be signed by the canonical signing flow even with NK#1 plugged in. The downstream-doc echo in `scripts/chroot-build-bootloader.sh:137` likewise tells the operator to sign only "grubx64.efi + igos-live.efi". | [sign-release.sh:192](../../scripts/sign-release.sh#L192), [chroot-build-bootloader.sh:137](../../scripts/chroot-build-bootloader.sh#L137) | Extend UKI glob to include `igos-install-*.efi` (or canonicalize all 3 UKI names to `*-live.efi` if reviewer prefers the suffix discipline). | B-003 | Critical | build/bootloader/ .signed UKIs are stale debug-cmdline artifacts | `build/bootloader/*.signed` are dated May 14 23:07; unsigned `.efi` are May 15. | B-004 | Critical | scripts/sign-grub.sh + sign-kernel-uki.sh use unpatched system OpenSC (RSA-4096 broken) | Both scripts hardcode `PKCS11_MODULE="${PKCS11_MODULE:-/usr/lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/opensc-pkcs11.so}"`. System OpenSC does NOT support RSA-4096 PIV signing (`CKR_FUNCTION_NOT_SUPPORTED`) — per `feedback_opensc_piv_rsa4096_force_enable`. sign-bootloader.sh + sign-shim.sh correctly use patched `/usr/local/lib/opensc-pkcs11.so`. Running sign-grub.sh or sign-kernel-uki.sh in isolation will fail with cryptic PKCS#11 errors. | [sign-grub.sh:33](../../scripts/sign-grub.sh#L33), [sign-kernel-uki.sh:32](../../scripts/sign-kernel-uki.sh#L32) | Mirror sign-bootloader.sh / sign-shim.sh hardening: default to `/usr/local/lib/opensc-pkcs11.so`, add presence-check + RSA-4096 modulus-match guard, build OPENSSL_CONF inline. | open | |
| B-005 | Critical | sign-release.sh canonical script does NOT use patched OpenSC | sign-release.sh delegates sbsign directly without overriding PKCS#11 module path. Implicit OpenSC pickup = unpatched. Same RSA-4096 failure path as B-004. sign-release.sh is documented as the canonical ceremony entry point in `docs/signing-procedure.md`. Following the procedure as written today produces a CKR_FUNCTION_NOT_SUPPORTED at the first UKI. | [sign-release.sh:215](../../scripts/sign-release.sh#L215), [docs/signing-procedure.md:64](../signing-procedure.md#L64) | Either inline the OpenSSL engine config block from sign-bootloader.sh into sign-release.sh, or have sign-release.sh call sign-bootloader.sh / sign-kernel-uki.sh as subprocesses with patched-OpenSC enforcement. | B-006 | Critical | NO measured boot / PCR sealing implemented despite security posture claims | `init.sh:220-221` masks `systemd-pcrlock-secureboot-policy` (claimed temporary for swtpm test VMs). | B-007 | High | objcopy --dump-section mutates input in build-grub-standalone.sh + verify-b2-reproducibility.sh | `objcopy --dump-section .sbat=/dev/stdout "$OUTPUT"` (verified empirically: SHA before `9a78...` → after `a76d...`) silently rewrites the input file. In `build-grub-standalone.sh:131` this happens AFTER grub-mkstandalone produces grubx64.efi, BEFORE signing — so signing operates on a mutated binary. In `verify-b2-reproducibility.sh:111-112` both shim copies are mutated before SHA computation, defeating the reproducibility check's purpose. | B-008 | High | Installed-system bootloader uses traditional GRUB-loads-vmlinuz, not UKI architecture | `installer/backend/bootloader.py` runs `grub-install` + `grub-mkconfig` and signs `/boot/vmlinuz-*` directly. UKIs (`igos-*.efi`) only exist on the live ISO ESP — there is no Forge code path that emits a UKI for the installed system. The boot architecture documented for the live ISO (sealed-cmdline UKI, single signature envelope) is NOT what the installed system actually runs. Two boot architectures coexist; only the live ISO one has been built or tested. | [bootloader.py:79-83](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L79), absence of UKI generation in install flow | Decide: extend Forge to emit + sign a UKI per installed kernel (closer parity with live ISO + better cmdline integrity), OR explicitly scope UKI to live ISO only and document the architectural split. | B-009 | High | ESP case-mismatch: bootloader.py writes lowercase, embedded grub.cfg references CamelCase | `bootloader.py:42` `ESP_BOOT_DIR = "/boot/efi/EFI/intergenos"` (lowercase). `embedded-grub.cfg:21,26` `configfile /EFI/InterGenOS/grub.cfg` (CamelCase). On FAT32 this is case-insensitive so it works by accident; on any non-FAT32 ESP layout (some firmware mount-points, build VM ext4 fixtures) it breaks. Class1 verifier (`class1_chain_verify.py:43-44`) probes both, confirming awareness of the mismatch — but the producer-side code still emits inconsistent paths. | [bootloader.py:42](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L42), [embedded-grub.cfg:21](../../packages/core/grub/embedded-grub.cfg#L21) | Pick ONE canonical case across the producer + consumer + verifier + efibootmgr loader-string. | B-010 | High | tty1 contention between intergen-firstboot animation + first-boot-greeter | Both `assets/intergen-firstboot-drm/intergen-firstboot.service` and `installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service` declare `Conflicts=getty@tty1.service`, `TTYPath=/dev/tty1`, `TTYVTDisallocate=yes`. Greeter has `After=intergen-firstboot.service` (correct ordering) but TTYVTDisallocate from the first service tears down the VT before the second can use it. | B-011 | High | MOK enrollment requires user-typed mokutil password — no operator-paced UX | Forge generates a 12-char password at install time (`mok.py:213-221`), displays it once (GUI/TUI), then expects user to type it into MokManager at next reboot. | B-023 | Low | sign-grub.sh + sign-kernel-uki.sh lack the modulus-match guard of sign-bootloader.sh / sign-shim.sh | sign-bootloader.sh:67-72 + sign-shim.sh:91-95 verify the cert on slot 9c has the same modulus as the repo's vendor cert before signing — catches the C6-class desync where cert and keypair diverge. sign-grub.sh + sign-kernel-uki.sh skip this gate. A drifted ceremony could quietly sign against a wrong key without being caught until sbverify-fail much later. | [sign-grub.sh](../../scripts/sign-grub.sh), [sign-kernel-uki.sh](../../scripts/sign-kernel-uki.sh) | Port the modulus-match block to both scripts (and to sign-release.sh per B-005). Resolution path: shim-signed wiring + sign-release.sh glob extended + patched OpenSC enforcement + modulus-match guard + post-sign count assertion + sign-bootloader 4-UKI loop + PIN-in-URI refusal + cmdline.live.txt strip. | code @ 9fc1af1f |

| B-026 | Critical | Forge install has NO initramfs generation — grub-mkconfig will emit broken menuentries | `bootloader.py:80` runs `grub-mkconfig -o /boot/grub/grub.cfg` inside the chroot. grub-mkconfig's `10_linux` template generates `linux /boot/vmlinuz-X` + `initrd /boot/initrd-X` for each kernel image. The installed system has `/boot/vmlinuz-*` (kernel package installs it) but ZERO `initrd-*` files. **Runtime initramfs generators (dracut, mkinitcpio, mkinitramfs) are RATIFIED-AGAINST** — the ratified architecture is no installed-system initramfs for plain installs; LUKS installs use a custom busybox-static FDE-initramfs bundled inside the UKI envelope (D-001). `installer/init/build-initramfs.sh` builds ONLY the live ISO's initramfs. The real defect is that grub-mkconfig is being invoked at all for installed-system boot — UKI parity (D-005) is the ratified path. | [bootloader.py:79](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L79), absence of UKI-build hook in chroot | **RESOLVED 2026-05-18 via D-005** (per-kernel UKI parity for installed systems, signed by user MOK, regenerated by `packages/core/linux-kernel/post_install.sh` on every kernel install/upgrade). **NOT a "wire dracut" fix — dracut RATIFIED-AGAINST**. See `docs/owner-directives.md` D-005. | closed (D-005) | |
| B-027 | High | embedded-grub.cfg does NOT set `check_signatures=enforce` — relies on shim_lock auto-registration | `packages/core/grub/embedded-grub.cfg` (the signed grub bootstrap) has no `set check_signatures=enforce`. `installer/iso/grub/grub.cfg` (the ESP-side menu) likewise. shim_lock module auto-registers a verifier WHEN SB is on, but if SB is off (UNSIGNED_TEST builds, hardware with user-disabled SB, BIOS legacy fallback), GRUB happily chainloads any binary — sealed-cmdline UKIs become unenforceable. _(iteration 3 — exhaustive what-did-we-miss sweep)_

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| B-041 | Critical | root=UUID=... cmdline + no initramfs = first boot of Forge install will fail | `config.py:154-155` generates `root=UUID=$(blkid)` for `GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX`. Kernel cannot resolve `root=UUID=...` without an initramfs userspace running udev/blkid. Combined with B-026 (no initramfs generation), every Forge install's first boot will halt with "VFS: Unable to mount root fs" because the kernel can only handle `root=/dev/sdaN` or `root=PARTUUID=...` natively. | [config.py:154-155](../../installer/backend/config.py#L154), [bootloader.py:79](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L79) | EITHER fix B-026 (wire initramfs generator) AND keep `root=UUID=`, OR change config.py:155 to emit `root=PARTUUID=` (kernel-native, no initramfs needed). PARTUUID is the lower-friction path if v1.0 ships without initramfs. | open | |
| B-042 | Critical | Forge install boot sequence is order-broken: vmlinuz MOK-signed but shim needs MOK enrolled before verifying vmlinuz | `bootloader.py:165-177` MOK-signs vmlinuz at install time. shim verifies kernel-load via shim_lock against (1) dbx, (2) vendor_db (has InterGenOS CA), (3) MOK list. MOK is enrolled at FIRST BOOT via MokManager, which runs only if shim sees a pending MokAuth EFI variable AND shim itself loads successfully. First boot flow: shim loads → sees MokAuth → runs MokManager → user enrolls MOK + reboots → shim loads → grub loads (signed by InterGenOS CA = in vendor_db) → grub asks shim to verify vmlinuz → vmlinuz MOK-signed → verifies against newly-enrolled MOK list → boots. If user reboots without going through MokManager OR cancels MokManager, vmlinuz unverifiable → boot loop with no clear error. | [bootloader.py:165-177](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L165), [install.py:475-486](../../installer/backend/install.py#L475) | (a) ALSO sign vmlinuz with InterGenOS CA at build time (verifiable before MOK enrolled), keeping MOK as the OUT-OF-TREE module signing key only. (b) Document MokManager flow in first-boot UX. (c) Boot failure recovery doc. | open | |
| B-043 | Critical | shim's MokManager has no InterGenOS UX choreography — user sees bare BIOS-style menu after install | shim displays a bare BIOS-style menu at first boot: "Enroll MOK / Reboot / etc." with no InterGenOS branding, no explanation, no recovery path. End user sees a black-and-blue text UI immediately after installing what they think is a polished Linux distro. mokutil prompts for password user typed during install; failure-to-recall = failed enrollment = unbootable system. | [docs/mok-enrollment.md:50-90](../mok-enrollment.md#L50), shim upstream behavior | (a) Generate user-friendly hardcopy at install end: "save this password, you'll need it at first boot". (b) Test the flow on real hardware end-to-end (cycle-5 hasn't been booted on hardware with SB on). (c) Recovery flow: "boot live ISO + chroot in + re-trigger MOK enrollment". | open | |
| B-044 | High | generate_enrollment_password() in mok.py is dead code | `installer/backend/mok.py:213-221` defines `generate_enrollment_password()` returning a 12-char alphanumeric password from a UI-friendly alphabet. NO caller in the codebase invokes it. `docs/mok-enrollment.md:117` references it as a documented design step but the actual install flow takes user-typed password from `install_io["mok_password"]`. | B-045 | High | Forge MOK generation is non-idempotent — install crash + resume regenerates a new keypair | `install.py:421-431` runs PHASE_MOK at step 9 (after partition, after package install). PHASE_BOOTLOADER at step 10 needs the MOK keypair (passed as `mok_keypair=`). If install crashes between MOK generation + bootloader, a resume would attempt to re-generate MOK (different cert) → signed-vmlinuz from previous run no longer matches → bootable nondeterminism. No idempotency check on `/var/lib/intergen/mok/mok.crt` existence in PHASE_MOK. | [install.py:421-431](../../installer/backend/install.py#L421), [mok.py:44-109](../../installer/backend/mok.py#L44) | Make PHASE_MOK idempotent: if `mok.crt` already exists on target, load + reuse the existing keypair. Same pattern as bootloader.py:158-161's sbverify pre-check for vmlinuz signing idempotency. | open | |
| B-046 | High | No GRUB superuser password — physical attacker can edit menuentry to chainload arbitrary binaries | `installer/iso/grub/grub.cfg` + `packages/core/grub/embedded-grub.cfg` have no `set superusers=...` + `password_pbkdf2 ...`. Pressing 'e' at any menuentry allows arbitrary edit. Sealed-cmdline UKI defeats the cmdline-injection vector (extra args at chainloader don't reach the kernel via systemd-stub), but an attacker can REPLACE `chainloader /EFI/InterGenOS/igos-live.efi` with `chainloader (hd0,gpt2)/EFI/whatever/attacker.efi`. shim+SB blocks if that binary isn't signed; SB-off lets attacker run anything. | [installer/iso/grub/grub.cfg](../../installer/iso/grub/grub.cfg), [packages/core/grub/embedded-grub.cfg](../../packages/core/grub/embedded-grub.cfg) | Two paths: (a) set GRUB superuser password, (b) accept physical-access-defeats-SB-without-TPM as documented threat model. | B-047 | Medium | docs/mok-enrollment.md trust-chain diagram says vmlinuz is "distro EFI X.509"-signed — actually MOK-signed at install | doc L52-58 ASCII chain: `grubx64.efi → vmlinuz (signed by InterGenOS distro EFI X.509, verified against vendor cert)`. | B-048 | Medium | bootloader.py vmlinuz signing loop skips if signed by ANY cert, not by THIS install's MOK | Code comment at bootloader.py:159-161 acknowledges that "re-signing kernels behavior varies across sbsigntools versions". The fix is the `sbverify --cert ... pre-check` skipping already-signed kernels. But if sbverify detects a signature against a DIFFERENT cert (e.g., previous-install's MOK or a build-time CA-sign), it still sees "signed" → skips → kernel boot fails post-install because grub passes to shim which can't verify against current MOK. | [bootloader.py:158-177](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L158) | Strip pre-existing signatures via `sbattach --remove` before signing — guarantees the resulting kernel is signed ONLY by THIS install's MOK. | open | |
| B-049 | Medium | sign-bootloader.sh + sign-shim.sh embed PIN in PKCS#11 URI — process-listing exposure | `scripts/sign-bootloader.sh:147` `PKCS11_URI="pkcs11:id=%02;type=private;pin-value=$PIN"`. Then passes this URI to sbsign via `--key "$PKCS11_URI"`. The PIN is part of the URI, which becomes part of sbsign's argv. Any `ps auxf` during the sign window leaks the PIN to other users on the workstation. sign-shim.sh has the same pattern at L164. sign-grub.sh + sign-kernel-uki.sh do not have this issue because they don't embed PIN in URI. | [sign-bootloader.sh:147,160-166](../../scripts/sign-bootloader.sh#L147), [sign-shim.sh:164](../../scripts/sign-shim.sh#L164) | Use `--key "pkcs11:id=%02;type=private"` (no pin-value) + set PIN via env var or stdin pipe. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-18 via T0-2 mechanical batch** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). | B-050 | Medium | install-time MOK key persists at /var/lib/intergen/mok/mok.key — secret recovery surface without FDE | `mok.py:99-103` chmods mok.key to 600. But the file is plain-PEM with no passphrase (`-nodes`). Root-readable on the running system; user with root → harvests MOK private key → can sign arbitrary modules + chainload binaries. Acceptable for the v1.0 threat model per `docs/mok-enrollment.md`'s "filesystem perms" framing, but FDE absent = anyone with physical disk access has the key. | [mok.py:81-87](../../installer/backend/mok.py#L81), [docs/mok-enrollment.md:21-29](../mok-enrollment.md#L21) | Either (a) store MOK key TPM-bound (B-006), (b) require LUKS root volume (Forge currently doesn't enforce LUKS), (c) accept + document. | B-051 | Low | shim build embeds CA cert as vendor_db — cert rotation requires 6-month-lead MS re-sign cycle | `docker/shim-build/Dockerfile:148` embeds the InterGenOS CA cert at compile time. Once shim is MS-signed (B-001 deferred), the embedded cert is immutable for that shim's lifetime. Cert rotation (every 730 days per ceremony) MUST be paired with a new MS-shim-sign round trip — which takes 6-12 weeks per the doc. Cert rotation is currently a 6-month-lead-time operation. | [docker/shim-build/Dockerfile:148](../../docker/shim-build/Dockerfile#L148) | Document the cert-lifecycle constraint in `docs/signing-procedure.md`. | B-052 | Low | GRUB_DISABLE_OS_PROBER set in 3 places with diverging policies | `installer/backend/config.py:167` writes `GRUB_DISABLE_OS_PROBER=false` (enables os-prober). `scripts/create-image.sh:182` writes `GRUB_DISABLE_OS_PROBER=true` (disables). `installer/backend/bootloader.py:80` invokes `GRUB_DISABLE_OS_PROBER=false grub-mkconfig` — duplicating the policy already in config.py. | B-053 | Low | secboot_vm_profile.py uses MS-signed OVMF VARS template — will reject self-signed shim (B-001) | `installer/tests/secboot_vm_profile.py:62,295` configures qemu-system with `OVMF_VARS_4M.ms.fd` (contains MS KEK + db). Real SB-on OVMF will reject the cycle-5 ISO's self-signed shim. The test fixture matches the deployed reality: tests that try to boot the ISO under MS-VARS firmware will fail at shim load. | C-055 | Medium | install.py: result.phase_completed set BEFORE phase emits its OK event | Throughout `installer/backend/install.py`, the pattern is: `result.phase_completed = PHASE_X` THEN `_emit(PHASE_X, n+1, "OK message")`. | C-065 | High | Empty `archive_dir` propagates as None into orchestrator — silent zero-package install | `installer/backend/install.py:228` accepts `archive_dir` as positional and passes it to `packages.install_packages` (line 377). `installer/backend/packages.py:42-53` `get_archives` checks `archive_dir.exists()` and returns `{}` on missing → `get_group_packages` returns `[]` → `install_packages` returns `(0,0,[])` → orchestrator emits "0 packages installed" but PHASE_PACKAGES marked complete. End result: a "successful" install with no packages on disk. | [install.py:377](../../installer/backend/install.py#L377), [packages.py:42](../../installer/backend/packages.py#L42) | Fail PHASE_PACKAGES hard when `total == 0` AND `package_groups` is non-empty. The "0 packages requested" case (empty groups) is legitimate and stays no-op. | **closed-2026-05-19** — install.py PHASE_PACKAGES tail raises RuntimeError when ok_count==0 AND fail_count==0 AND cfg has non-empty package_groups. Error message cites C-021 pre-flight (composes as belt-and-suspenders: C-021 catches at PHASE_VALIDATE before destructive write; C-065 catches at PHASE_PACKAGES if pre-flight bypassed by regression/race). 3 new orchestrator tests verify hard-fail / happy / partial-failure paths. | code @ 47633d22 |
| C-066 | Medium | TUI `prompt_install_io` cleanup: cancelled run leaves install.yaml on disk briefly | `installer/frontend/tui.py:625-627` calls `_cleanup_on_abort(yaml_path=str(yaml_path))` only when prompt_install_io returns None.
