Forensic gap. | [hooks.py:212](../../installer/backend/hooks.py#L212) | Log full stderr at DEBUG. | open | |

### Lane E — Kernel + drivers + firmware

**Inventory (pass 1, 2026-05-18):** Kernel 6.18.10 (current stable; kernel.org LTS-line designation pending). Config fragments at `config/kernel/fragments/` (2 active: `00-universal-baseline.config` 3521 lines, `99-intergenos-overrides.config` 241 lines). Universal baseline derived from a 5-distro convergence analysis (Ubuntu, Arch, Fedora, Debian, openSUSE) recording options where ≥4/5 agree. Total active CONFIG_ lines: 3,434 in baseline + ~120 in overrides. Single linux-firmware package (`packages/core/linux-firmware/`, 20260309 release) installed via `make install-xz` (.xz-compressed); on-disk size 719 MB / 573 top-level subtrees. 2,634 .ko.gz modules in `/lib/modules/6.18.10-igos/`. Initramfs assembled by `installer/init/build-initramfs.sh` (busybox-static + hard-coded REQUIRED_MODULES list of 6 entries: squashfs / overlay / loop / isofs / vfat / ext4). UKI assembled via `scripts/build-uki.sh` using systemd `ukify build` with a single `--initrd=` argument (no microcode initrd prepend).

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| E-001 | Holy-Grail | Microcode kernel-side flags MISSING — neither Intel nor AMD ucode loads from kernel | `CONFIG_MICROCODE=y` is set in baseline but neither `CONFIG_MICROCODE_INTEL` nor `CONFIG_MICROCODE_AMD` are explicitly set in any fragment. olddefconfig in current kernels defaults these to `n` when not stated; verified on the installed `/mnt/igos/boot/config-6.18.10`: only `CONFIG_MICROCODE=y` appears, no INTEL/AMD sub-flags. Combined with E-002, microcode never reaches the CPU on any boot path. Root-cause peer of F-001 (catches the `iucode_tool` path mistake in `create-image.sh`); even if F-001 were fixed, the kernel would still refuse to consume the initrd. | [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config), boot config-6.18.10 | Add `CONFIG_MICROCODE_INTEL=y` and `CONFIG_MICROCODE_AMD=y` (both =y, never =m) to `99-intergenos-overrides.config`; also add `CONFIG_MICROCODE_LATE_LOADING=y` for runtime update path; rebuild kernel + UKI | open | |
| E-002 | Holy-Grail | UKI does not prepend microcode initrd — `ukify build` invoked with single `--initrd` | `scripts/build-uki.sh:77` calls ukify with one `--initrd="$INITRAMFS"` argument. Linux microcode early-load convention requires the ucode cpio (intel-ucode.img / amd-ucode.img) to be the FIRST initrd seen by the kernel — kernel scans early cpio for `/kernel/x86/microcode/{Genuine,Authentic}.bin` BEFORE jumping to userland. Our UKI bundles only our main initramfs; even if E-001 were fixed, the kernel would never see microcode. ukify supports multiple `--initrd=` flags (each becomes a concatenated `.initrd` PE section). | [build-uki.sh:77](../../scripts/build-uki.sh#L77), [chroot-build-bootloader.sh:103](../../scripts/chroot-build-bootloader.sh#L103) | Generate `intel-ucode.img` + `amd-ucode.img` from `/usr/lib/firmware/{intel,amd}-ucode/` via `iucode_tool`/`cat` per upstream pattern; pass both as additional `--initrd=` arguments to ukify (ucode FIRST, then main initramfs); ship a `scripts/build-microcode-initrds.sh` helper invoked by `chroot-build-bootloader.sh` before `build-uki.sh`. amd-ucode.img is a cpio of `kernel/x86/microcode/AuthenticAMD.bin` produced by concatenating files in `amd-ucode/`. | open | |
| E-003 | Holy-Grail | Intel SOF audio firmware NOT shipped — modern Intel laptops (TGL/ADL/RPL/MTL) silently lose audio | linux-firmware tarball `20260309` no longer ships Intel SOF firmware (`intel/sof/` subdir absent — verified by `tar -tf`). SOF is now distributed only via the upstream Sound Open Firmware project (`thesofproject/sof-bin` GitHub releases) as a separate package. We compile every `snd-sof-pci-intel-*.ko` module (cnl, icl, tgl, adl, mtl, ptl) into the kernel but ship no matching firmware — verified: `/mnt/igos/lib/modules/6.18.10-igos/kernel/sound/soc/sof/intel/*.ko.gz` present, `/mnt/igos/usr/lib/firmware/intel/sof/` absent. Any Intel laptop newer than ~2021 boots into a silent system. The legacy `intel/avs/` and `dsp_fw_*.bin.xz` files only cover BXT/CNL/GLK/KBL (≤2019 platforms). Not a "missing driver" failure — a feature-loss-by-omission that won't appear in any log. | [linux-firmware/package.yml](../../packages/core/linux-firmware/package.yml), `intel/sof/` absent from `/mnt/igos/usr/lib/firmware/intel/` | Add `packages/core/sof-firmware/` package sourced from `https://github.com/thesofproject/sof-bin/releases/download/v2024.06/sof-bin-2024.06.tar.gz` (or current release); install to `/usr/lib/firmware/intel/sof/`, `/usr/lib/firmware/intel/sof-tplg/`, `/usr/lib/firmware/intel/sof-ipc4/`, `/usr/lib/firmware/intel/sof-ipc4-tplg/`; runtime dep of `linux-firmware`. | open | |
| E-004 | Critical | Initramfs REQUIRED_MODULES set has zero GPU/network drivers — install-from-USB to non-virtio hardware can't render or fetch | `installer/init/build-initramfs.sh:62` lists `squashfs overlay loop isofs vfat ext4` only. For our install-gui flow (Forge GUI launches in initramfs userspace BEFORE switch_root), the GUI needs a DRM device to draw on — but no DRM driver is in initramfs and our DRM drivers are all built as modules (`DRM_AMDGPU=m`, `DRM_I915=m`, `DRM_NOUVEAU=m`, `DRM_VIRTIO_GPU=m`). Only `DRM_SIMPLEDRM=y` (UEFI framebuffer fallback) is built-in, so anything beyond a basic EFI GOP framebuffer fails. Similarly, no NIC drivers are present, blocking network-based install resume / package fetch from initramfs. Live-CD-style installers from Debian/Ubuntu/Fedora ship a much wider driver set in initramfs (autodiscovered via their respective runtime initramfs generators — InterGenOS does NOT use those generators, RATIFIED-AGAINST). | [build-initramfs.sh:62](../../installer/init/build-initramfs.sh#L62) | Expand REQUIRED_MODULES to a baseline GPU + NIC set: `drm drm_kms_helper amdgpu i915 nouveau virtio_gpu r8169 e1000e igb iwlwifi ath9k ath10k ath11k brcmfmac`; also add `xhci_pci ohci_pci ehci_pci usbhid hid_generic` for USB-keyboard-only install boxes. Document the size budget — full driver set is ~80 MB compressed; live ISOs ship 250-500 MB initramfs routinely. Alternative: emit a `host-agnostic` mode flag that walks `modules.alias` for all PCI/USB-class IDs (drm/net/usb/fs classes) and copies the matched modules into `installer/init/build-initramfs.sh`'s output — implement in our own builder, not via any runtime initramfs generator (those are RATIFIED-AGAINST). | open | |
| E-005 | Critical | Module dependency resolver only walks 1 level deep — silent missing-symbol failures | `build-initramfs.sh:79-88` resolves dependencies via `modinfo -F depends` then copies. It does NOT recursively walk: a module pulled in by isofs that itself depends on another module gets dropped. depmod at line 92 will then succeed (no error on missing deps in initramfs context). On runtime, modprobe inside initramfs would fail to load with `unknown symbol`. The pattern works for our trivial 6-module set today because all 6 happen to be flat; expanding REQUIRED_MODULES per E-004 surfaces the bug instantly. | [build-initramfs.sh:79-88](../../installer/init/build-initramfs.sh#L79) | Replace the 1-level loop with a fixed-point closure: enqueue REQUIRED_MODULES, pop, resolve deps, enqueue any unseen, repeat until queue empty. Or invoke a kernel-mode-tools-aware helper (`/usr/sbin/modprobe --show-depends`). (NOTE: shelling out to a runtime initramfs generator is NOT an option — dracut/mkinitcpio RATIFIED-AGAINST. Implement the closure in our own `installer/init/build-initramfs.sh`.) | open | |
| E-006 | High | `CONFIG_RANDSTRUCT_NONE=y` — explicitly disabled struct randomization | The baseline-derivation chose `RANDSTRUCT_NONE` because the 5-distro convergence didn't reach 4/5 agreement on `RANDSTRUCT_FULL` (only Fedora ships it). KSPP recommends `RANDSTRUCT_FULL=y` as a defense-in-depth against ROP/JOP gadget chains in kernel structs. Cost: small build-time penalty + per-build ABI changes (intentional). Verified installed: `CONFIG_RANDSTRUCT_NONE=y` in `/mnt/igos/boot/config-6.18.10`. | boot config-6.18.10, [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config) | Add `# CONFIG_RANDSTRUCT_NONE is not set` and `CONFIG_RANDSTRUCT_FULL=y` to overrides fragment. Aligns with KSPP + Holy Grail (defense against superhuman exploit discovery). Performance overhead negligible; ABI churn isn't a concern since we don't ship third-party out-of-tree drivers (intergen is in-tree). | open | |
| E-007 | High | `CONFIG_INIT_ON_FREE_DEFAULT_ON` MISSING — heap UAF leaks unzeroed | `CONFIG_INIT_ON_ALLOC_DEFAULT_ON=y` is set (verified on installed config), but the paired `CONFIG_INIT_ON_FREE_DEFAULT_ON` is missing entirely. KSPP recommends BOTH — alloc-init zeroes on allocation, free-init zeroes on free. The latter blocks use-after-free disclosures (info leaks reading freed memory). Cost: ~1-3% perf for kernel-heavy workloads. | [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config), boot config-6.18.10 | Add `CONFIG_INIT_ON_FREE_DEFAULT_ON=y` to overrides fragment. Aligns with KSPP recommended set + every modern hardening guide. | open | |
| E-008 | High | KSPP-recommended hardening MISSING: ZERO_CALL_USED_REGS, DEBUG_LIST, DEBUG_SG, BUG_ON_DATA_CORRUPTION, GCC_PLUGIN_LATENT_ENTROPY, GCC_PLUGIN_STRUCTLEAK_BYREF_ALL | Sweep against KSPP recommended-settings list (https://kspp.github.io/Recommended_Settings). All six not set in either fragment, not auto-y from olddefconfig. Verified absent on installed kernel — only `CONFIG_GCC_PLUGINS=y` (umbrella) is on. CFI_CLANG requires clang toolchain (we build with GCC — correctly N/A unless we add clang). These are GCC-compatible: `GCC_PLUGIN_LATENT_ENTROPY` injects entropy into kernel boot RNG; `STRUCTLEAK_BYREF_ALL` zeroes all on-stack structs passed by reference; `DEBUG_LIST`/`DEBUG_SG` catch list/scatter-gather corruption; `BUG_ON_DATA_CORRUPTION` upgrades silent corruption to a BUG. | [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config), https://kspp.github.io/Recommended_Settings | Add to overrides fragment: `CONFIG_ZERO_CALL_USED_REGS=y`, `CONFIG_DEBUG_LIST=y`, `CONFIG_DEBUG_SG=y`, `CONFIG_BUG_ON_DATA_CORRUPTION=y`, `CONFIG_GCC_PLUGIN_LATENT_ENTROPY=y`, `CONFIG_GCC_PLUGIN_STRUCTLEAK_BYREF_ALL=y`. Verify each compiles under 6.18 + GCC 14 (some plugin names changed; consult `make menuconfig` against the actual tree before committing). | open | |
| E-009 | High | `CONFIG_USER_NS=y` + no sysctl controls — unprivileged user-namespace attack surface enabled | User namespaces are a well-documented exploit vector (CVE-2022-0185, CVE-2022-0492, CVE-2023-0386, dirty-pipe variants, etc.). Debian 10+ ships `kernel.unprivileged_userns_clone=0` sysctl by default to deny unprivileged creation. We have `CONFIG_USER_NS=y` (needed for systemd unprivileged services + flatpak + many sandboxes) but no sysctl restriction. | boot config-6.18.10, no sysctl found via repo grep | Add `/etc/sysctl.d/10-igos-hardening.conf` with `kernel.unprivileged_userns_clone=0` for v1.0 (Debian-style default-deny); evaluate AppArmor `userns` mediation profile (kernel 6.6+ has built-in support). Coordinate with Lane F security posture for final policy. | open | |
| E-010 | High | `CONFIG_KEXEC=y` + `CONFIG_KEXEC_FILE=y` — bypass for kernel-lockdown unless KEXEC_SIG_FORCE is set | KEXEC lets a privileged user load a new kernel and jump to it, bypassing Secure Boot + lockdown unless KEXEC_SIG verification is enforced. We have `CONFIG_KEXEC_SIG=y` and `CONFIG_KEXEC_BZIMAGE_VERIFY_SIG=y` set (verified installed). However, lockdown mode `integrity` (auto-engaged under EFI Secure Boot per overrides) requires `KEXEC_SIG_FORCE=y` to enforce; without it, kexec falls back to permitting unsigned kernels. Probe didn't surface `KEXEC_SIG_FORCE` from the installed config — needs explicit verification. | [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config), boot config-6.18.10 | Confirm `CONFIG_KEXEC_SIG_FORCE=y` is in installed config; if absent, add to overrides. Owner-level alternative: disable kexec entirely (`# CONFIG_KEXEC is not set`) for v1.0 to remove the attack surface — no end-user feature loss since live-kernel-swap isn't in our scope. | open | |
| E-011 | High | `CONFIG_HIBERNATION=y` — encryption-bypass vector | Hibernation writes RAM to swap; an attacker with physical access can extract pre-shutdown decrypted state from the swap partition. Combined with our (currently absent) full-disk-encryption story, hibernation is a defense-in-depth gap. Most security-focused distros (Tails, Whonix, Qubes) disable HIBERNATION outright. Even Fedora workstation now ships hibernation off-by-default. | boot config-6.18.10 | For v1.0 Holy-Grail posture: `# CONFIG_HIBERNATION is not set` in overrides; allow opt-in via a separate kernel package for laptop power-management users (deferred to v1.x with the LUKS-swap-encryption story). | open | |
| E-012 | High | Module signing key `certs/signing_key.pem` not cleaned up post-install — leak-risk artifact | The installed config shows `CONFIG_MODULE_SIG_KEY="certs/signing_key.pem"` (the kernel default literal). At build time the kernel auto-generates a fresh RSA key at that path if absent. The override comment says `MODULE_SIG_KEY intentionally UNSET — kernel build auto-generates ephemeral keypair per build`. Reality: the symbol is unset in our fragment but inherits the kernel default literal — what we observe. The ephemeral-key story works because the build never reuses prior keys. **However:** `linux-kernel/build.sh` doesn't `rm -f certs/signing_key.pem` post-install, so the key sits in the chroot's kernel source tree. If anything snapshots or rsyncs that tree the private key escapes. | [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config) (comment), [linux-kernel/build.sh](../../packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh) | Add explicit cleanup in `linux-kernel/build.sh` (and pass2 variant) post-do_install: `rm -f certs/signing_key.pem certs/signing_key.x509` after `make modules_install` completes; assert key absent in pre-squashfs audit; document the ephemeral-key invariant in `docs/ephemeral-module-signing.md`. | open | |
| E-013 | Medium | `CONFIG_DEVMEM=y` + `CONFIG_PROC_KCORE=y` + `CONFIG_DEVPORT=y` — RAM-disclosure surfaces enabled | `/dev/mem` reads physical RAM, `/proc/kcore` exports kernel memory as ELF, `/dev/port` exposes I/O port access. All three guarded by `CAP_SYS_RAWIO` but trivially escaped by any root-EQ exploit. Lockdown=integrity restricts them under SB-engaged boots — but if SB is disabled, all three are wide open. KSPP recommends `# CONFIG_DEVMEM is not set` for hardened systems. Cost: breaks a small number of debug tools (memtester, fwts memory tests, some old X servers). | boot config-6.18.10 | Decision-required: disable `DEVMEM` + `PROC_KCORE` + `DEVPORT` for v1.0, or rely on lockdown=integrity? Lockdown bypass via SB-disabled is the gap. Recommend: explicitly disable all three in overrides; if a user needs them, they rebuild kernel (PRIME DIRECTIVE: users control their system). Coordinate with Lane F. | open | |
| E-014 | Medium | BPF JIT spectre hardening sysctl not shipped | Verified kernel-side: `CONFIG_BPF_JIT_ALWAYS_ON=y`, `CONFIG_BPF_UNPRIV_DEFAULT_OFF=y`, `CONFIG_BPF_LSM=y`, `CONFIG_BPF_JIT_DEFAULT_ON=y` all set. Missing user-space sysctl: `net.core.bpf_jit_harden=2` (constant-blinding mitigation). Without this, JIT-compiled BPF can serve as a Spectre-v2 gadget source. | boot config-6.18.10 | Ship `/etc/sysctl.d/10-igos-hardening.conf` with `net.core.bpf_jit_harden=2`. Coordinate with Lane G (network + systemd service hygiene) for the canonical sysctl file. | open | |
| E-015 | Medium | NVIDIA proprietary / open-source driver not packaged — no out-of-tree path | `/mnt/igos/lib/modules/6.18.10-igos/` has standard subdirs but no NVIDIA modules. `packages/extra/` has no nvidia package. nouveau is built (CONFIG_DRM_NOUVEAU=m) so users with NVIDIA GPUs fall back to nouveau — works for display but no compute (CUDA) and poor performance on Ampere+. May be intentional for v1.0 (avoid proprietary), but should be documented. | grep `nvidia` returns empty in `packages/` | Document v1.0 stance: nouveau-only NVIDIA support. Plan v1.x: package the upstream NVIDIA open-source kernel modules (https://github.com/NVIDIA/open-gpu-kernel-modules) which are MIT-licensed and work for Turing+; proprietary closed-source nvidia.ko stays off the ISO per FSF-style policy but goes in MIRROR tier as a download-helper. | open | |
| E-016 | Medium | ZFS not packaged — out-of-tree filesystem absent | No `zfs` package; out-of-tree ZFS is widely used despite CDDL/GPL friction. Decision-question for the owner: does v1.0 ship ZFS-via-DKMS, or omit entirely? Ubuntu ships it (rebuilt per kernel update); RHEL forbids it (license); Arch packages it as `zfs-dkms`/`zfs-linux`. For now: ABSENT. | grep `zfs` empty in `packages/` | Document: v1.0 does not ship ZFS (CDDL/GPL incompatibility per Linus + FSF position). MIRROR tier could host a `zfs-dkms-helper` script that fetches + builds against the user's running kernel. Defer to v1.x for the helper script — not for ZFS itself. | open | |
| E-017 | Medium | Live cmdline ships `loglevel=7` + `systemd.show_status=true` + journald `forward_to_console=1` — verbose on production live boot | `installer/init/cmdline.live.txt` is `igos.mode=live loglevel=7 systemd.show_status=true systemd.journald.forward_to_console=1`. loglevel=7 (debug-level kernel messages) + journald forwarding to console = boot console flooded with kernel debug spam. Useful for debugging the live ISO, NOT for a production live-CD a user would actually run. Install-gui and install-tui correctly use loglevel=3. | [cmdline.live.txt](../../installer/init/cmdline.live.txt) | Lower live cmdline to `loglevel=4` (warn-level) and remove `journald.forward_to_console=1`; keep `systemd.show_status=true` (Plymouth-style boot progress). Or: keep verbose for v1.0 dev-snapshot ISOs, ship a separate `cmdline.live-prod.txt` for marketing/demo ISOs. Decide via Lane D first-boot UX. | open | |
| E-018 | Medium | No `mitigations=` kernel cmdline — relying on kernel build-time defaults | None of `cmdline.live.txt`, `cmdline.install-gui.txt`, `cmdline.install-tui.txt` set the `mitigations=` parameter. Modern KSPP and most distros explicitly set `mitigations=auto,nosmt` to enable all CPU vuln mitigations AND disable SMT/hyperthreading (only way to fully mitigate Spectre-BHI, MDS, L1TF on Intel without microcode). Default is just `auto` — leaves SMT enabled, partially mitigated. | [cmdline.live.txt](../../installer/init/cmdline.live.txt), [cmdline.install-gui.txt](../../installer/init/cmdline.install-gui.txt), [cmdline.install-tui.txt](../../installer/init/cmdline.install-tui.txt) | Decision: SMT off costs 15-30% throughput on multi-threaded workloads (offset partly by core count). Holy-Grail-aligned: `mitigations=auto,nosmt` becomes default; users opt back to `mitigations=auto` to re-enable SMT. Document the trade-off prominently. v1.0 ship: `mitigations=auto,nosmt` in all three cmdline files. | open | |
| E-019 | Medium | `BLK_DEV_LOOP=m` + `OVERLAY_FS=m` + `SQUASHFS=m` + `ISO9660_FS=m` — modprobe-fail race in initramfs | Init.sh modprobes loop/overlay/squashfs/isofs before mounting; if any .ko load fails (corrupted module, sig mismatch), the mount errors. Promoting to `=y` removes the failure point — size cost trivial (~30 KB combined). Also removes the dependency-closure bug from E-005 for these critical modules. | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `CONFIG_BLK_DEV_LOOP=y`, `CONFIG_OVERLAY_FS=y`, `CONFIG_SQUASHFS=y`, `CONFIG_ISO9660_FS=y` to 99-overrides. Removes modprobe calls from initramfs hot path. | open | |
| E-020 | Low | `CONFIG_RANDSTRUCT_PERFORMANCE` not chosen; `NONE` is — if FULL is too costly, PERFORMANCE is a middle ground | Sibling to E-006: if `RANDSTRUCT_FULL` is rejected for build-time reasons, `RANDSTRUCT_PERFORMANCE` randomizes only structs explicitly annotated `__randomize_layout` — much smaller scope but still better than NONE. | boot config-6.18.10 | If E-006 is closed in favor of NONE staying, document the deliberate trade-off and explain why PERFORMANCE isn't chosen. | open | |
| E-021 | Low | Kernel 6.18.10 LTS-line status unverified | 6.18.x appears in `kernel.org/category/releases.html` as stable; depending on release timing, 6.18 may or may not yet be designated LTS. The next post-6.12 LTS announcement timing affects our v1.x plan. | [linux-kernel/package.yml:2](../../packages/core/linux-kernel/package.yml) | Track upstream LTS designation; pin to whichever is the active LTS line at v1.0 freeze date. If 6.18 is NOT made LTS, decide whether to retreat to 6.12 LTS or ride mainline-stable with our own CVE backports (huge maintenance burden — recommend LTS). | open | |
| E-022 | Low | `CONFIG_RTW88_8821CE=m` duplicated in overrides — appears under both "Network drivers" + "RTW88 WiFi" sections | Cosmetic; cat-then-olddefconfig collapses correctly but the file is noisier than needed. | [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config) | Single-source the RTW88 + RTW89 entries; remove the duplicates from the "Network drivers" block. | open | |
| E-023 | Cosmetic | No build-time invariant assertion that override-declared CONFIGs survived olddefconfig | `linux-kernel-pass2/build.sh` hand-asserts `USB_STORAGE`, `RTW88_PCI`, `RTW88_8821CE`. The other ~120 override-declared options have no such check — silent regression risk if olddefconfig drops one (Kconfig rename, dependency churn, etc.). | [linux-kernel-pass2/build.sh](../../packages/core/linux-kernel-pass2/build.sh) | Add a `scripts/verify-kernel-config.py` that walks the merged .config and asserts every `CONFIG_*=y` and `=m` from `99-intergenos-overrides.config` matches the final .config; invoke from build.sh configure() and pre-squashfs audit. | open | |


**Pass 2 (cross-check, 2026-05-18):** Re-validated installed config against fragments + KSPP recommended-settings + Annvix/Tails/Whonix hardening references. 13 additional findings (E-024..E-036). Notable corrections: E-013 partially mitigated by `CONFIG_STRICT_DEVMEM=y` + `CONFIG_IO_STRICT_DEVMEM=y` (verified installed) — strict-devmem allows /dev/mem reads only from low-physical-address device-memory holes, not arbitrary kernel RAM. Severity downgrade noted in E-013 remediation. Pass-2 also confirmed `CONFIG_NR_CPUS` override is being IGNORED by olddefconfig: overrides fragment says 512, installed kernel reports 8192 (the baseline value wins because baseline-derivation pulled distro `NR_CPUS=8192` which has higher numeric precedence under range constraints) — sibling-pattern to E-023.

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| E-024 | Critical | `CONFIG_LOCK_DOWN_KERNEL_FORCE_NONE=y` — lockdown engages ONLY on SB-detected boot; SB-disabled boots run with FULL access | Verified installed: `CONFIG_LOCK_DOWN_KERNEL_FORCE_NONE=y`. The `CONFIG_LOCK_DOWN_IN_EFI_SECURE_BOOT=y` override engages lockdown=integrity ONLY when EFI Secure Boot is detected at kernel boot. If a user (or attacker) disables SB in firmware, kernel boots with lockdown=none — every restriction in `docs/research/audit/lockdown-features.md` is bypassed: /dev/mem, kexec, BPF unrestricted, mod load without sig, etc. Holy Grail says we don't trade security for convenience — but our default trades security for the "user might disable SB" case. Other distros (Debian, Fedora) ship `LOCK_DOWN_KERNEL_FORCE_INTEGRITY=y` (or CONFIDENTIALITY). | boot config-6.18.10, [99-intergenos-overrides.config](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config) | Change to `CONFIG_LOCK_DOWN_KERNEL_FORCE_INTEGRITY=y` (or `_CONFIDENTIALITY=y` for stricter posture; CONFIDENTIALITY also restricts /proc/kcore reads). Users who need debug access pass `lockdown=none` boot param OR rebuild kernel (PRIME DIRECTIVE — they can; default is locked-down). Defense-in-depth against SB-bypass; matches Fedora/Debian baseline. | open | |
| E-025 | High | `CONFIG_FW_LOADER_USER_HELPER=y` — legacy userspace firmware-loading enabled (KSPP says OFF) | Verified installed. This enables the `/sys/class/firmware/*/loading` legacy interface where userspace can inject arbitrary firmware blobs via `cat firmware.bin > /sys/class/firmware/.../data`. KSPP recommends `# CONFIG_FW_LOADER_USER_HELPER is not set` because it lets unprivileged-but-CAP_SYS_ADMIN code (containers!) push attacker-controlled firmware to NICs / GPUs / WiFi. Modern kernel uses direct firmware-loader (`/lib/firmware/`) — userhelper is decade-old fallback. | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `# CONFIG_FW_LOADER_USER_HELPER is not set` to overrides fragment. Verify no module on our system invokes the userhelper API (none in upstream kernel modules; check out-of-tree-if-we-have-any). | open | |
| E-026 | High | `CONFIG_MODULE_UNLOAD=y` + `CONFIG_MODULE_FORCE_UNLOAD` unverified — KSPP recommends MODULE_UNLOAD off | Verified `CONFIG_MODULE_UNLOAD=y` installed. KSPP recommends `# CONFIG_MODULE_UNLOAD is not set` to prevent rootkit hide-by-unload after persistence (load → install hook → unload module → no trace). Cost: cannot unload modules at runtime; reboot required for kernel-module update. This is the trade we accept — most users never `rmmod`. | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `# CONFIG_MODULE_UNLOAD is not set` to overrides. Test: confirm boot, confirm modprobe loads, confirm rmmod fails as expected. | open | |
| E-027 | High | `CONFIG_USERFAULTFD=y` + no `vm.unprivileged_userfaultfd=0` sysctl — kernel exploitation aid | userfaultfd is a kernel feature for user-mode page-fault handling; widely abused as a kernel-exploit primitive (slows exploit-race windows so attackers can fault-trap to lengthen the race). KSPP + Debian + Fedora ship `vm.unprivileged_userfaultfd=0` sysctl (only privileged callers may use it). Used by some QEMU/post-copy-live-migration paths; can be re-enabled per-VM. | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `vm.unprivileged_userfaultfd=0` to `/etc/sysctl.d/10-igos-hardening.conf`. Coordinate with Lane G. | open | |
| E-028 | High | No `CONFIG_GCC_PLUGIN_STACKLEAK` — kernel-stack contents leak across syscalls | KSPP-recommended `GCC_PLUGIN_STACKLEAK=y` clears the kernel stack on every syscall return, preventing info-disclosure of leftover stack contents. Verified: not set, not even `CONFIG_STACKLEAK` family present. GCC plugin requirement satisfied (we have `CONFIG_GCC_PLUGINS=y`). Smaller-than-RANDSTRUCT cost. | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `CONFIG_GCC_PLUGIN_STACKLEAK=y` + `CONFIG_STACKLEAK_METRICS=n` (no metrics export — production posture) to overrides. Verify compile against 6.18 + GCC 14. | open | |
| E-029 | High | `CONFIG_NR_CPUS=512` override IGNORED — installed kernel reports `NR_CPUS=8192` | Verified disk-side: `/mnt/igos/boot/config-6.18.10` shows `CONFIG_NR_CPUS=8192` and `CONFIG_NR_CPUS_RANGE_BEGIN=8192`. Override fragment line 19 sets `CONFIG_NR_CPUS=512`. olddefconfig merge dropped our value because the baseline (or kernel default) raised the range floor to 8192. Concrete confirmation of E-023's class — silent override-loss without notification. Larger NR_CPUS bloats per-CPU allocations (bitmap arrays, cpumask_t storage) — typically harmless on a desktop/laptop but it means our override was a lie. | boot config-6.18.10, [99-intergenos-overrides.config:19](../../config/kernel/fragments/99-intergenos-overrides.config#L19) | Same fix as E-023 (verify-kernel-config.py). Also decide: keep NR_CPUS=512 (lighter; current laptops max at ~96 cores) or accept upstream 8192? If we keep 512 we have to defeat the baseline value — the verifier can fail loudly when a desired value gets dropped. | open | |
| E-030 | Medium | `CONFIG_IO_URING=y` — io_uring CVE-rich; KSPP recommends OFF for hardened systems | io_uring has had a long string of CVEs (CVE-2023-2598, CVE-2023-21400, CVE-2023-4622, CVE-2024-0582, …). KSPP recommends OFF unless required. systemd uses io_uring opportunistically (since v253) but falls back gracefully. Disabling it costs some performance for high-IO workloads. Decision-needed. | boot config-6.18.10 | Decision: keep `=y` (systemd benefits + KVM perf), restrict via sysctl `kernel.io_uring_disabled=2` (default-deny per-uid; allow opt-in), OR `# CONFIG_IO_URING is not set` entirely. Lane F coordination. Recommend sysctl middle-ground for v1.0; aggressive Holy-Grail = `=n`. | open | |
| E-031 | Medium | `CONFIG_MAGIC_SYSRQ=y` + `MAGIC_SYSRQ_DEFAULT_ENABLE=0x1` — sysrq partial-on by default | SysRq is a kernel-developer feature; allows keyboard-mediated kernel actions (sync, kill, crash dump, etc.). Default-enable value 0x1 = enable logging only (lowest risk). KSPP recommends `kernel.sysrq=0` runtime sysctl + `MAGIC_SYSRQ_DEFAULT_ENABLE=0x0` build. Cost: sysrq becomes opt-in for debugging. | boot config-6.18.10 | Either: (a) ship `kernel.sysrq=0` in `/etc/sysctl.d/10-igos-hardening.conf` (preferred — keeps debug path one sysctl write away); or (b) change override to `CONFIG_MAGIC_SYSRQ_DEFAULT_ENABLE=0x0` for a stricter build-time posture. | open | |
| E-032 | Medium | `CONFIG_LIVEPATCH=y` but no live-patch shipping infra | LIVEPATCH allows applying CVE patches to a running kernel without reboot. Compiled in (good) but we have no `packages/extra/igos-livepatches/` repo, no signed-livepatch infrastructure, no signing key chain, no kpatch/kgraft userland. Feature is inert overhead. | boot config-6.18.10 | Option A (v1.0): leave LIVEPATCH=y as forward-compat, document "no live patches shipped yet" in `docs/research/kernel/`; build infrastructure in v1.x. Option B (Holy-Grail-strict): turn LIVEPATCH=n until we ship the infrastructure (don't enable surface we can't use). Defer pending Lane F + roadmap discussion. | open | |
| E-033 | Medium | `CONFIG_FTRACE=y` + `CONFIG_FTRACE_SYSCALLS=y` — broad kernel trace surface; KSPP-mixed | FTRACE family is widely used by perf/strace/bpftrace/eBPF — legitimate userspace tooling depends on it. KSPP allows but lockdown=integrity restricts tracing of `init_user_ns`. Verified `LOCKDOWN_KERNEL_FORCE_NONE=y` (E-024) means lockdown doesn't engage by default — so ftrace is fully exposed. Once E-024 is fixed, this drops to non-issue. | boot config-6.18.10 | Closed by E-024 (when lockdown=integrity is default, ftrace is restricted appropriately). No separate change needed here once E-024 lands. Document the dependency. | open | |
| E-034 | Medium | `CONFIG_PROFILING=y` + `CONFIG_PERF_EVENTS=y` — perf counters + kprobes attack surface | KSPP recommends `kernel.perf_event_paranoid=3` sysctl (deny all unprivileged perf usage). Default in many distros is `2` (deny most but allow benchmarks). We have no sysctl shipping perf_event_paranoid. Has been used as a kernel-bug-trigger primitive (e.g., CVE-2017-7308 was perf-event-related). | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `kernel.perf_event_paranoid=3` to `/etc/sysctl.d/10-igos-hardening.conf`; users who need perf for development can adjust. Coordinate with Lane G. | open | |
| E-035 | Low | `CONFIG_STRICT_DEVMEM=y` + `CONFIG_IO_STRICT_DEVMEM=y` partially mitigates E-013 | Verified installed: strict-devmem family is ON. This restricts `/dev/mem` reads to low-physical-address device-memory holes (PCI BARs, etc.), NOT arbitrary RAM. So E-013's threat model is REDUCED for /dev/mem (PROC_KCORE and DEVPORT still wide open). E-013 severity should drop from Medium to Low for the DEVMEM portion specifically; PROC_KCORE + DEVPORT still warrant disable. Note for E-013 update during pass 3 / synthesis. | boot config-6.18.10 | Update E-013 description: split into E-013a (DEVMEM — mitigated by STRICT_DEVMEM, lower priority) and E-013b (PROC_KCORE/DEVPORT — still raw). Or: keep E-013 but caveat that STRICT_DEVMEM provides defense-in-depth. | open | |
| E-036 | Medium | `CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_CPU` / `CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_BOOTLOADER` not surfaced in probe — verify CPU-RNG (RDRAND) trust | Not present in probe output. If both are `=n`, kernel only trusts RDRAND for partial entropy contribution. If `=y`, kernel fully trusts RDRAND output to seed CRNG at boot — controversial (Snowden + Linus debates 2013/2018). Most distros ship `=y` for boot-time entropy availability. We need to verify which. | boot config-6.18.10 | Probe: `grep RANDOM_TRUST /mnt/igos/boot/config-6.18.10` — if both unset, OK (most cautious). If `=y`, document the trust decision. Recommend explicit `# CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_CPU is not set` + `# CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_BOOTLOADER is not set` for Holy-Grail posture (don't trust closed firmware for RNG seeding; supplement RDRAND with entropy from other sources). | open | |

**Pass 3 (what 1+2 missed, 2026-05-18):** Audit-the-audit on additional KSPP / Annvix / KSPP-extras axes. 7 additional findings (E-037..E-043). Confirmed (negative): no KASAN/KCSAN/KCOV/UBSAN in installed config — correct for production build. Confirmed (negative): `CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_CPU` / `_BOOTLOADER` not set in installed config — defaults are `n` in 6.18 mainline, so we're conservative-by-default here (E-036 resolves NOT-A-FINDING; close at synthesis). Pass-3 found 2 KSPP-class items still missing (E-037 + E-038), 2 reduced-attack-surface posture items (E-039 BT debug + E-040 BR/EDR), 1 TPM 2.0 verify, 1 AES-NI module-vs-builtin, 1 distinct watchdog default-panic.

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| E-037 | High | `CONFIG_IA32_EMULATION=y` + `CONFIG_COMPAT_BRK=y` — legacy 32-bit attack surface + heap-randomization defeat | KSPP-recommended OFF: `IA32_EMULATION` (legacy 32-bit ABI; rich CVE history — fixed by Fedora 38+ where it's now OFF by default) and `COMPAT_BRK` (preserves legacy brk(2) without ASLR). Verified BOTH installed `=y`. Cost: 32-bit binaries can't run (almost no modern userland still ships 32-bit; Steam-runtime + wine-32 are notable exceptions). | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `# CONFIG_IA32_EMULATION is not set` and `# CONFIG_COMPAT_BRK is not set` to overrides. For Steam/wine32 users: separate kernel package option (v1.x) OR document `linux-32compat` package opt-in. Aligns with Fedora's 2023 hardening sweep. | open | |
| E-038 | High | TPM 2.0 path — `CONFIG_TCG_TPM=y` is generic; `CONFIG_TCG_TPM2_HMAC` and `CONFIG_TPM_KEY_PARSER` status unverified — systemd-pcrlock chain may not be complete | `init.sh:221` references `systemd-pcrlock-secureboot-policy` in the active-services list. systemd-pcrlock requires kernel-side TPM 2.0 + PCR-policy-binding APIs (CONFIG_TCG_TPM2_HMAC for HMAC-bound TPM access, CONFIG_TPM_KEY_PARSER for TPM-sealed key parsing). Probe didn't surface these. If missing, systemd-pcrlock fails silently at runtime and the "measured boot" claim is hollow. | boot config-6.18.10, [init.sh:221](../../installer/init/init.sh#L221) | Verify `grep TCG_TPM2 /mnt/igos/boot/config-6.18.10` returns the HMAC + key-parser symbols. If absent, add `CONFIG_TCG_TPM2_HMAC=y` + `CONFIG_TPM_KEY_PARSER=y` to overrides. Also add a runtime smoke test in `installer/tests/test_systemd_pcrlock.py` that verifies the systemd-pcrlock service actually succeeds on a TPM-equipped (or swtpm) test VM. | open | |
| E-039 | Medium | `CONFIG_BT_DEBUGFS=y` — Bluetooth debugfs interface leaks state via /sys/kernel/debug/bluetooth | Verified installed. KSPP recommends debug-fs interfaces OFF in production. Provides BT controller state introspection without authn; combined with bluetoothd CVEs (we're current, but historical CVE-2017-1000251 BlueBorne class) the debug surface compounds. | boot config-6.18.10 | Add `# CONFIG_BT_DEBUGFS is not set` to overrides. Production has no need for BT debugfs introspection. | open | |
| E-040 | Medium | `CONFIG_BT_BREDR=y` — classic Bluetooth (BR/EDR) enabled, LE-only mode would reduce attack surface | BR/EDR is older Bluetooth (pre-LE). Has rich CVE history (BlueBorne, KNOB attack, BleedingTooth). Modern devices (mice, keyboards, audio) increasingly LE-only. Disabling BR/EDR breaks legacy BT audio (A2DP-classic) and some older accessories. Decision-question for the owner. | boot config-6.18.10 | Decision: keep `BT_BREDR=y` (preserve legacy device compat — most likely v1.0 stance) OR `# CONFIG_BT_BREDR is not set` (LE-only, smaller surface). Document the choice in `docs/research/security/bluetooth-posture.md` or similar. Coordinate with Lane F. | open | |
| E-041 | Medium | `CONFIG_CRYPTO_AES_NI_INTEL=m` — AES-NI hardware acceleration as module, not built-in | Built as module. AES-NI is needed early during boot if FDE / dm-crypt is in play (encrypted swap, encrypted root). When module-only and not in initramfs, kernel falls back to soft-AES for early decryption — much slower. Once we ship FDE (v1.x), this becomes a measurable perf hit. | boot config-6.18.10 | Promote to `CONFIG_CRYPTO_AES_NI_INTEL=y` in overrides. Tiny build-size impact (~40 KB); ensures hardware acceleration is always available even pre-modprobe. Same logic applies to `CONFIG_CRYPTO_GHASH_CLMUL_NI_INTEL` (GCM/GMAC acceleration) and `CONFIG_CRYPTO_SHA256_SSSE3` / `_AVX2`. | open | |
| E-042 | Low | Watchdog enabled with `CONFIG_WATCHDOG_PRETIMEOUT_DEFAULT_GOV_PANIC=y` but no pretimeout setpoint — defaults to no-pretimeout | Hardware watchdog enabled (`CONFIG_WATCHDOG=y`, `CONFIG_WATCHDOG_HANDLE_BOOT_ENABLED=y`), default governor on pretimeout is PANIC (kernel panic before watchdog reset, useful for crashdumps), but no actual pretimeout configured anywhere in cmdline or sysctl. Net effect: watchdog timeout = full hardware reset, no kernel-panic chance to capture diagnostic info. | boot config-6.18.10 | Configure pretimeout via `/etc/watchdog.conf` (or systemd watchdog units) for v1.0; document the default behavior in `docs/research/kernel/`. Low priority — affects only debugability of watchdog-reset incidents. | open | |
| E-043 | Low | `CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_CPU` / `CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_BOOTLOADER` not surfaced in probe — kernel default `n` (conservative) but should be explicit | E-036 sibling: probe returned empty grep, meaning the symbols are not in installed config. Kernel default in 6.18 is `n` for both, so we're conservative-by-default — but the implicit-default is fragile (kernel could change defaults in a future bump). | boot config-6.18.10 | Add explicit `# CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_CPU is not set` + `# CONFIG_RANDOM_TRUST_BOOTLOADER is not set` to overrides for documentation + future-proofing. E-036 supersedes; close E-036 in synthesis. | open | |

### Lane M — Test coverage gaps

**Inventory (pass 1, 2026-05-18):** 38 Python test files (`test_*.py`) across 6 trees:
`tests/` (16 files: pkm, preflight, igos_build, installer, repo-publish, upstream-check, sbom, download-sources), `installer/tests/` (16 files: class1–6, mok, integrity, install_orchestrator, gui_state, gui_yaml, tui_flow, post_install, grub, verify_sources), `intergen/tests/` (2 files: tools, integration), 1 fixture `branding/marks/final/test_small_sizes.py` (UI-only).
Shell tests: 3 (`installer/smoke/smoke-test.sh`, `tests/sbat/test_check_sbat_generations.sh`, `tests/manifest/test_manifest_phase.sh`).
CI: a single GitHub workflow (`.github/workflows/public-content-audit.yml`) that runs only `scripts/check-public-content.py` — no test suite invocation, no pkm/installer/igos-build CI coverage.
No `pytest.ini`, `pyproject.toml`, `setup.cfg`, `tox.ini`, or `noxfile.py` in the repo; no coverage.py invocation anywhere.
Local gates: `.githooks/pre-push` (8 gates: force-push block, public-content scan, stale-master, bash/python syntax, scope vs message, conventional commit, co-author trailer, commit-msg audit, new-package verify_paths) and `scripts/pre-squashfs-audit.py` invoked from `scripts/build-squashfs.sh:255`.

A regression that relaxes the enforcement (e.g., changes iteration to skip `tier:extra`) weakens the gate without signal. | [scripts/check-builder-coverage.py](../../scripts/check-builder-coverage.py) | `tests/builder/test_builder_coverage.py` with positive + negative fixtures. | open | |

Symmetric to M-032. | [scripts/derive-verify-paths.py](../../scripts/derive-verify-paths.py) | `tests/scripts/test_derive_verify_paths.py` with build.sh fixtures + expected path lists. | open | |
| M-053 | Low | Many existing tests assert SHAPE not BEHAVIOR ("no exception" = pass) | `test_tui_flow.py:test_backend_imports_load` asserts modules import; `test_disks_has_is_efi` asserts a function attribute exists. | M-054 | Low | Bash test runners have inconsistent exit-code contracts | 3 bash test scripts, 3 different counter/exit patterns. No shared framework (bats, shellspec). | M-055 | Low | conftest.py at repo root doesn't add intergen/ or installer/ to sys.path | Tests in `intergen/tests/` and `installer/tests/` rely on per-file `sys.path.insert(...)` or pytest's rootdir resolution. | M-056 | Cosmetic | Test naming inconsistency across the tree | `tests/igos_build/` (underscore) vs `installer/tests/` (no nested). `test_class1_chain_verify.py` mirrors `class1_chain_verify.py` in same dir (helper module structurally in `installer/tests/` not `installer/backend/`). `tests/repo-publish/` hyphen; `tests/upstream-check/` hyphen; `tests/igos_build/` underscore. GDM is preset-enabled and reaches tty1 before the greeter on qcow2 dev images (where the greeter actually ships, per `create-image.sh:434-451`), so GDM steals tty1 and the password greeter never runs; dev images quietly ship with builder-set passwords as the live ones. | [installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service:26](../../installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service#L26) | Add `Conflicts=gdm.service` and `Before=gdm.service` (or remove the greeter entirely per D-002 owner directive). | open | |
| D-006 | High | systemd-firstboot.service not masked in squashfs payload | `installer/init/init.sh:210-211` masks `systemd-firstboot.service` only in the live-overlay tmpfs; the squashfs payload itself (which becomes the installed root on Forge installs) does not mask it. Squashfs ships `/etc/machine-id == "uninitialized"` (per `build-squashfs.sh:221`) so on first boot of an installed system, systemd-firstboot fires with ConditionFirstBoot=yes; if locale/hostname/timezone files Forge wrote are absent/malformed the unit prompts interactively, racing GDM for tty1. | [installer/init/init.sh:210](../../installer/init/init.sh#L210) | Add a permanent mask in the squashfs (via `chroot-config-ch9.sh` or a `core/systemd` preset) so installed systems never run interactive systemd-firstboot; Forge's `config.generate_all` covers what the unit would have prompted for. | open | |
| D-007 | High | Forge install never writes first-boot-completed marker for greeter ConditionPathExists | Even though the `intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service` is only directly shipped by `create-image.sh` (qcow2 path), the unit's drop-in `Environment=INTERGENOS_USER=intergenos` is hardcoded to the builder-side user name (`create-image.sh:447-450`); the build flow assumes the greeter never reaches a Forge-installed target. If the greeter ever does survive into a Forge install, it will look up user `intergenos` which Forge never creates and exit rc=3, falling through to getty without setting any flag. | [scripts/create-image.sh:447](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L447) | Either follow D-002 directive (delete the unit + drop-in) or have Forge's user-creation phase write `/etc/intergenos/first-boot-completed` on the target so the greeter unit's `ConditionPathExists=!` short-circuits cleanly. | open | |
| D-008 | Medium | intergen-welcome XDG autostart .desktop has no startup phase or delay | `packages/desktop/intergen-welcome/build.sh:112-123` writes the autostart entry without `X-GNOME-Autostart-Phase=Applications` or `X-GNOME-Autostart-Delay`; the wrapper has no `sleep` either. The welcomer launches the moment gnome-session reaches the Applications phase, before GNOME Shell finishes loading extensions — its `Gio.Settings.new('org.gnome.shell.extensions.user-theme')` and `enabled-extensions` writes may bind to a not-yet-ready shell. The divergent install-theming.sh path (J-001) had `sleep 3` + `X-GNOME-Autostart-Delay=3` for exactly this reason. | [packages/desktop/intergen-welcome/build.sh:112](../../packages/desktop/intergen-welcome/build.sh#L112) | Add `X-GNOME-Autostart-Phase=Applications` + `X-GNOME-Autostart-Delay=3` to the autostart entry and a matching `sleep 3` (or a more targeted readiness check on org.gnome.Shell DBus) in the wrapper. | open | |
| D-009 | Medium | "Skip Setup" writes the done-marker, no re-entry path | The Skip button at `intergen-welcome.py:980` calls `self.quit()` which makes `app.run()` return 0; the wrapper at `packages/desktop/intergen-welcome/build.sh:88-92` then writes `~/.config/intergen-welcome/done` on any rc=0. **Iter-2 cross-check note (Lane D)**: 10/14 iter-1 rows VALIDATED at cited code. 2 FALSE-POSITIVE: D-002 (greeter binary actually exists as 153-line bash script at `installer/data/first-boot-greeter`; the unit-deletion recommendation per owner directive still stands but the "binary doesn't exist" framing is wrong); D-013 (.o + ELF binary not in `git ls-files` — only in working copy; .gitignore already excludes them; remediation already complete). 1 DOWNGRADE: D-010 (PNG count off by 1; os-release LOGO claim factually incorrect — no LOGO field shipped). 1 SCOPE-QUESTION: D-006 depends on B-035 — if systemd-firstboot binary genuinely doesn't ship per `-D firstboot=false`, the mask is dead code; the systemd-homed-firstboot half remains real regardless.

| D-021 | Critical | `build-squashfs.sh` does not run `dconf update` — installed systems ship with no compiled `/etc/dconf/db/local` | `build-squashfs.sh:140-168` runs `ldconfig`, `glib-compile-schemas`, `update-desktop-database`, `update-mime-database`, `gtk-update-icon-cache`, `fc-cache`, `systemctl preset-all` — every cache-rebuild EXCEPT `dconf update`. | D-023 | High | `intergen-welcome` package.yml omits `libadwaita1` + `pygobject3` runtime deps — wizard ImportErrors on minimal installs | `intergen-welcome.py:10-17` does `import gi` (needs `pygobject3`) and `gi.require_version('Adw', '1')` (needs `libadwaita1`). package.yml:13-26 declares neither. `gtk4` itself declares `runtime: []`. | D-027 | Low | Welcomer's app-grid `.desktop` stays visible after done-marker — clicking it silently exits | `intergen-welcome/build.sh:99-109` writes `.desktop` with `NoDisplay=false`. No re-entry path. | [packages/desktop/intergen-welcome/build.sh:99](../../packages/desktop/intergen-welcome/build.sh#L99) | Set NoDisplay=true; OR wrapper accepts `--rerun`; OR notify-send on marker-hit. | open | |
| D-028 | Medium | No wallpaper / desktop-background defaults shipped — installed systems use GNOME upstream `adwaita-l/d.jpg` | No picture-uri/wallpaper/backgrounds in intergenos-{theme,default-settings}. `intergen-welcome.py:24-26` documents "FLUX-generated art" backgrounds but ships none. | D-029 | Medium | Wizard's enable-extensions silently no-ops when extension manifests fail GNOME shell-version pin check | `intergen-welcome.py:438-441` writes to `enabled-extensions`, but ExtensionSystem.js rejects UUIDs whose metadata.json shell-version array doesn't include running shell version. `disable-extension-version-validation` not set anywhere. | D-030 | Medium | No Plymouth boot-splash package or branding asset — boot is bare kernel/systemd console output | Zero plymouth hits in packages/scripts/installer. | D-031 | Low | /etc/skel deeper scaffold gap (extends D-020) — missing `.cache/`, `.gnupg/`, `.ssh/` strict-mode pre-creates | D-020 names .config/, .local/share/, .bash_logout. Without `.ssh/` pre-created with 0700, user creating authorized_keys first inherits umask mode. | [scripts/chroot-config-ch9.sh:179-199](../../scripts/chroot-config-ch9.sh#L179) | Extend skel via `install -dm0700`/`0755` for deterministic modes across these dirs. | open | |
| D-032 | High | gnome-keyring needs `password` hook in `/etc/pam.d/passwd` — entirely missing (companion to D-022) | Beyond D-022's auth+session, `password optional pam_gnome_keyring.so` in `/etc/pam.d/passwd` re-encrypts login keyring with NEW password when user runs `passwd`. Without it, keyring stays encrypted with OLD password. shadow-pam writes /etc/pam.d/passwd with only `password include system-password`. | [packages/core/shadow-pam/build.sh:87](../../packages/core/shadow-pam/build.sh#L87), [packages/desktop/gnome-keyring/build.sh:38](../../packages/desktop/gnome-keyring/build.sh#L38) | gnome-keyring post_install appends `password optional pam_gnome_keyring.so` to `/etc/pam.d/passwd` (idempotency-guarded). | open | |
| D-033 | Low | Forge install doesn't write `/etc/intergenos/first-boot-completed` — latent footgun on D-005/D-007 partial-fix | Squashfs ships greeter only via create-image.sh (qcow2). If unit ships AND marker doesn't, greeter prompts NEW password every Forge first boot. | [installer/backend/users.py:31](../../installer/backend/users.py#L31), [installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service:13](../../installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service#L13) | When Forge create_user completes, write `/etc/intergenos/first-boot-completed` (also doubles as audit record). | open | |
| D-034 | Medium | `intergen-welcome` wrapper has no display-server guard — typing on TTY/non-graphical SSH crashes Python | `intergen-welcome/build.sh:64-94` wrapper has no check for `$WAYLAND_DISPLAY`/`$DISPLAY`. No feedback. | [assets/intergen-welcome/intergen-welcome.py:425-429](../../assets/intergen-welcome/intergen-welcome.py#L425) | apply_theme notifies on shell-theme write fail; OR Extensions page excludes user-theme entirely (treat as mandatory). | open | |

**Iter-3 cross-check note (Lane D)**: 15 new findings in under-audited corners. Two Critical (D-021 + D-026 form a single Critical class — dconf system-db is structurally dead-lettered on installed systems because no dconf update runs in squashfs build AND no /etc/dconf/profile/user is shipped; D-017's missing tarball lands a dead keyfile even when fixed). Two High (D-022 + D-032 — pam_gnome_keyring hooks all land in a never-invoked PAM file; D-023 missing runtime deps). Plus 11 Medium/Low for wizard runtime robustness, branding gaps (D-028 wallpaper, D-030 Plymouth), and skel scaffold.

### Lane F — Security posture

_(IGOSC sub-agent population; seeded with tonight's finding)_

**D-007 close-out 2026-05-18** (build-system coordinator, walk item 4 cluster). OWNER DIRECTIVE D-007 (`docs/owner-directives.md`) ratified the SSH + root + credentials posture as a Class A gate that blocks ISO/qcow2 creation. The following Lane F Holy-Grail findings are RESOLVED via the D-007 code-fix cluster (commit `<sweep-commit>`): **F-002** SSH host keys baked into squashfs — `ssh-keygen -A` removed from `packages/core/openssh/build.sh` post_install; sshd.service ExecStartPre handles first-boot keygen. **F-003** PermitRootLogin=yes default — `packages/core/openssh/build.sh` now ships an explicit `/etc/ssh/sshd_config.d/00-intergenos-d007.conf` drop-in setting `PermitRootLogin no` (drop-in pattern survives upstream rebases). **F-004** Hardcoded `root:intergenos` password — `packages/core/shadow/build.sh` now calls `passwd -l root` (root locked; user-sudo is the only escalation path; matches Ubuntu/Fedora defaults). **F-006** tty2 root-autologin — `installer/init/init.sh` no longer writes the autologin override; getty@tty2 remains enabled for emergency console access via the live `intergenos:intergenos` user. **F-008** SSH host keys in qcow2 — `scripts/create-image.sh` no longer runs build-time `ssh-keygen -A`. **Compliance gate** at `scripts/check-d007-compliance.sh` runs at `phase_image` + at the head of `scripts/build-iso.sh`; any reintroduction of these violations fails ISO assembly. **Live user credentials** are now explicit `intergenos:intergenos` sudo-capable per D-007 (was `liveuser` with `*` shadow entry — also annotated under F-006).

|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| F-001 | Holy-Grail | Microcode never loading on shipped ISOs | `scripts/create-image.sh:292` tests `/usr/bin/iucode_tool` but binary is at `/usr/sbin/iucode_tool`; entire Intel microcode early-load block silently skipped; shipped images running with unpatched CPU vulns (Spectre/Meltdown/Zenbleed-class) | [create-image.sh:292](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L292) | One-line path fix; verify post-build that `/boot/intel-ucode.img` exists in shipped ISO; add post-build assertion | **RESOLVED 2026-05-18 via kernel + drivers + firmware lane E audit closure** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). Resolution path: kernel security sprint absorbed lane E findings (Dirty Frag + Fragnesia mitigations). | code @ 608181b7 |
| F-002 | Holy-Grail | SSH host keys baked into shipped chroot/squashfs | `packages/core/openssh/build.sh:82` runs `ssh-keygen -A` in `post_install` during chroot build (chroot-build-core-extra.sh:209). Keys land at `/etc/ssh/ssh_host_*_key*` and `build-squashfs.sh` does NOT delete them before mksquashfs. Every ISO ships identical SSH host keys; every installed system that boots with sshd enabled presents the SAME host fingerprint, defeating MITM detection. Direct POWER RULE violation (no dev keys in shipped ISO). | [openssh/build.sh:82](../../packages/core/openssh/build.sh#L82), [create-image.sh:280](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L280), [build-squashfs.sh:222](../../scripts/build-squashfs.sh#L222) | Strip `ssh-keygen -A` from post_install; rely solely on `sshd.service` ExecStartPre to generate keys on first boot; add `rm -f $CHROOT/etc/ssh/ssh_host_*` to build-squashfs.sh cleanup step. | open | |
| F-003 | Holy-Grail | sshd ships with PermitRootLogin=yes by default | `packages/core/openssh/build.sh:79` unconditionally sets `PermitRootLogin yes` in `/etc/ssh/sshd_config`, and `installer/backend/users.py:95` enables `sshd.service` on every installed system. Combined with the build-time root password from `packages/core/shadow/build.sh:70`, every install opens root SSH on the network with whatever password the build set. | [openssh/build.sh:79](../../packages/core/openssh/build.sh#L79), [users.py:95](../../installer/backend/users.py#L95) | Ship default `PermitRootLogin no` (or `prohibit-password`); do not enable sshd by default; require explicit user opt-in. | open | |
| F-004 | Holy-Grail | Hardcoded `root:intergenos` password baked into chroot | `packages/core/shadow/build.sh:70` runs `echo "root:intergenos" \| chpasswd` during chroot build. Although create-image.sh:402 overwrites with `$ROOT_PASSWORD`, the literal "intergenos" hash is written to `/etc/shadow` inside the chroot/squashfs and remains the live root password for any boot path that mounts squashfs directly without going through create-image.sh (live ISO mode boots squashfs via overlayfs and only updates `lastchg`, never re-hashes the password). | [shadow/build.sh:70](../../packages/core/shadow/build.sh#L70), [init.sh:321](../../installer/init/init.sh#L321) | Replace the hardcoded literal with `usermod -p '*' root` (lock the account) in shadow/build.sh post_install; let create-image.sh's ROOT_PASSWORD env path be the sole source of the actual root credential. | open | |
| F-005 | Holy-Grail | No AMD microcode package — every AMD CPU install runs unpatched | The tree has `packages/core/intel-ucode/` + `packages/core/iucode-tool/` but no AMD equivalent. AMD CPUs receive zero microcode updates on InterGenOS — every Zenbleed/Inception/Sinkclose-class vuln stays unpatched forever. Twin of F-001 but with no early-load infrastructure at all. | [packages/core/](../../packages/core/), [create-image.sh:291](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L291) | Add `packages/core/amd-ucode/` shipping linux-firmware's `amd-ucode/` blobs; extend create-image.sh post-deploy to generate `/boot/amd-ucode.img`; add `initrd /boot/amd-ucode.img` to grub.cfg alongside the intel one. | open | |
| F-006 | Holy-Grail | TTY2 root autologin in live mode bypasses all auth | `installer/init/init.sh:308-315` writes a getty drop-in that auto-logs in root on tty2 with no password challenge. Documented as "emergency fallback" but in practice anyone with physical access to a booted live ISO can press Ctrl-Alt-F2 and instantly get a root shell, completely bypassing the polkit `liveuser`-only Forge passwordless grant model. Live ISOs ship to every user. | [init.sh:308](../../installer/init/init.sh#L308) | Replace tty2 root autologin with tty2 liveuser autologin (matching tty1); or gate behind a kernel cmdline flag like `igos.live-root-debug=1`. | open | |
| F-007 | High | Forge polkit rule ships on installed systems for any future `liveuser` account | `packages/desktop/forge/build.sh:91` installs `49-intergenos-forge.rules` to `/usr/share/polkit-1/rules.d/`, which lands on every installed system (forge is desktop tier). The rule grants unconditional `polkit.Result.YES` to `subject.user == "liveuser"`. If an admin or attacker post-install creates a user literally named `liveuser`, that user gets passwordless root-as-forge — silently. | [forge/build.sh:91](../../packages/desktop/forge/build.sh#L91), [49-intergenos-forge.rules:14](../../installer/data/49-intergenos-forge.rules#L14) | Skip installing this rule on installed targets (live-ISO-only via squashfs overlay), or gate the rule's YES on `/proc/cmdline contains igos.mode=live`, or rename the live-ISO user to a namespace-distinct unguessable identifier. | open | |
| F-008 | High | Build-time SSH host keys also propagated into the disk image | `scripts/create-image.sh:280` runs `ssh-keygen -A` during disk-image assembly. (Twin of F-002 but for the create-image.sh path; F-002 covers the squashfs-via-ISO path.) | [create-image.sh:280](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L280) | Remove ssh-keygen -A from create-image.sh; rely on sshd.service ExecStartPre to generate on first boot of the installed system. | open | |
| F-009 | High | Installer enables sshd.service by default on every install | `installer/backend/users.py:95` lists `sshd.service` in the default `enable_services` list. | F-010 | High | No pam_pwquality / pam_faillock — no password policy or brute-force lockout | The PAM stack written by `packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh:55-107` ships only `pam_unix.so` for auth/account/password. No `pam_pwquality.so` for complexity enforcement, no `pam_faillock.so` for failed-login lockout. Combined with F-003 (sshd root login), unlimited online brute-force attempts with no rate-limit. libpwquality is built (`packages/core/libpwquality/`) but never wired in. | [linux-pam/build.sh:90](../../packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh#L90), [linux-pam/build.sh:61](../../packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh#L61) | Add `password requisite pam_pwquality.so retry=3` to `/etc/pam.d/system-password`; add pam_faillock pre/post auth lines to `/etc/pam.d/system-auth`; ship default `/etc/security/pwquality.conf` and `/etc/security/faillock.conf`. | open | |
| F-011 | High | UKI cmdlines don't set kernel lockdown level | `installer/init/cmdline.{live,install-gui,install-tui}.txt` contain no `lockdown=integrity` or `lockdown=confidentiality` token. Kernel has `CONFIG_LOCK_DOWN_IN_EFI_SECURE_BOOT=y` which auto-engages lockdown under Secure Boot, but in builds where SB is unavailable (BIOS install, OVMF without enrolled keys, dev VMs) lockdown stays at NONE. | [cmdline.live.txt:1](../../installer/init/cmdline.live.txt#L1), [cmdline.install-gui.txt:1](../../installer/init/cmdline.install-gui.txt#L1), [cmdline.install-tui.txt:1](../../installer/init/cmdline.install-tui.txt#L1) | Append `lockdown=integrity` to all three cmdline files so lockdown engages regardless of SB state. | open | |
| F-012 | High | No /etc/sysctl.d/ security hardening drop-ins shipped | No package ships sysctl hardening defaults (kernel.kptr_restrict, kernel.dmesg_restrict, kernel.kexec_load_disabled, kernel.unprivileged_bpf_disabled, net.ipv4.conf.all.rp_filter, fs.protected_*, etc.). The kernel has `CONFIG_SECURITY_DMESG_RESTRICT=y` as the build-time default but no runtime sysctl reinforcement; user-space-tunable defaults are upstream-permissive across the board. | [config/](../../config/), [packages/core/](../../packages/core/) | Ship `99-intergenos-hardening.conf` in `/usr/lib/sysctl.d/` covering kptr_restrict=2, dmesg_restrict=1, kexec_load_disabled=1, unprivileged_bpf_disabled=1, perf_event_paranoid=3, fs.protected_{symlinks,hardlinks,fifos,regular}=2, and net hardening. | open | |
| F-013 | High | Installer's MOK signing chain not protected by passphrase | `installer/backend/mok.py:80-91` generates the MOK private key with `openssl req -nodes` (no passphrase). Comment says "no passphrase on the private key (keys live on the machine, protected by filesystem perms — adding a passphrase would block automated DKMS signing)." Any local root compromise instantly exfiltrates the MOK signing key, allowing the attacker to sign rootkit kernel modules that load under MODULE_SIG_FORCE. Filesystem perms alone are inadequate against ring-0 actors who survive a reboot. | [mok.py:80](../../installer/backend/mok.py#L80) | Provide a UI toggle for "TPM-sealed MOK key" that wraps the private key with TPM2 PCR policy; document the threat model of unsealed MOK explicitly. | open | |
| F-014 | High | atd auto-enabled by default — exposes scheduled-job surface | `packages/base/at/build.sh:49` runs `systemctl enable atd` in post_install. atd is enabled on every install. atd is rarely needed and adds attack surface (setuid-root `at` binary upstream, mail-delivery path, job-spool tampering). | [at/build.sh:49](../../packages/base/at/build.sh#L49) | Remove the `systemctl enable atd` from at/build.sh post_install; let users opt-in if they want it. | open | |
| F-015 | High | MOK keypair only RSA-2048; no TPM-binding | `installer/backend/mok.py:35` hardcodes `MOK_KEY_BITS = 2048`. Modern guidance (NIST SP 800-131A Rev 2) recommends RSA-3072 minimum through 2030. The InterGenOS vendor cert itself was regenerated to RSA-4096 (per check-public-content.allowlist comments at line 42-44), but per-install MOKs lag at 2048. | [mok.py:35](../../installer/backend/mok.py#L35) | Bump `MOK_KEY_BITS` to 3072 or 4096; document the rationale; consider ECDSA P-384 as a smaller-faster alternative. | open | |
| F-016 | Medium | sshd_config not hardened beyond PermitRootLogin — upstream defaults retained | Beyond F-003's `PermitRootLogin yes`, openssh preserves all upstream defaults: no `MaxAuthTries 3`, no `LoginGraceTime 30`, no `AllowUsers` whitelist, no curated `KexAlgorithms`/`Ciphers`/`MACs`, no `ClientAliveInterval`. | [openssh/build.sh:77](../../packages/core/openssh/build.sh#L77) | Append a curated hardening block to `/etc/ssh/sshd_config` in post_install; cross-reference mozilla-modern OpenSSH guidance. | open | |
| F-017 | Medium | grub-mkconfig runs with `GRUB_DISABLE_OS_PROBER=false` enabling on-disk OS scanning | `installer/backend/bootloader.py:80` runs `GRUB_DISABLE_OS_PROBER=false grub-mkconfig` to detect dual-boot Windows/Linux. os-prober mounts partitions to read their boot configs — historically a source of CVEs (CVE-2019-19134, CVE-2021-3981) and the reason Debian/Arch flipped the default to disabled. Auto-running it on every install widens surface for a malicious co-resident OS to influence GRUB config generation. | [bootloader.py:80](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L80), [config.py:167](../../installer/backend/config.py#L167) | Default to `GRUB_DISABLE_OS_PROBER=true`; surface an explicit "Detect other operating systems" checkbox in the Forge dual-boot flow. | open | |
| F-018 | Medium | algif_aead blacklist is incomplete mitigation for CVE-2026-31431 | `scripts/create-image.sh:555` writes `/etc/modprobe.d/disable-algif.conf` to blacklist algif_aead for CVE-2026-31431. The blacklist only affects userspace-triggered `modprobe`; an in-kernel API caller still loads it, and the cpio early-stage doesn't honor modprobe.d. The fix is incomplete against the actual exploit path. | [create-image.sh:555](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L555) | Verify CONFIG_CRYPTO_USER_API_AEAD is set to `n` in kernel config (compile out the surface, not blacklist a module); track upstream patch status and re-evaluate. | open | |
| F-019 | Medium | `/etc/security/limits.conf` and pam_limits.so policy not customized | linux-pam's `system-session` PAM stack includes `pam_limits.so` (build.sh:81) but no curated `/etc/security/limits.conf` ships with hardened defaults (core dump = 0 for non-debug users, max processes capped, etc.). Default limits remain whatever upstream pam-1.7.2 ships. | [linux-pam/build.sh:81](../../packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh#L81) | Ship `/etc/security/limits.d/00-intergenos.conf` setting `* hard core 0`, `* hard nproc 4096`, `* hard nofile 65536`. | open | |
| F-020 | Medium | UKI cmdlines don't enforce `slab_nomerge` / `init_on_alloc=1` / `init_on_free=1` / `pti=on` | UKI cmdlines lack kernel hardening boot params per kernselfprotection-project recommendations: `slab_nomerge` (defeats heap-spray-via-merged-slabs), `init_on_alloc=1` + `init_on_free=1` (eliminate UAF info-leaks), `pti=on`, `oops=panic`, `module.sig_enforce=1` (belt-and-suspenders to CONFIG_MODULE_SIG_FORCE). | [cmdline.live.txt:1](../../installer/init/cmdline.live.txt#L1) | Append the listed flags to all three cmdline files; document perf impact. | open | |
| F-021 | Medium | systemd-journald `Storage=` default — persistent journal off by default | No `/etc/systemd/journald.conf.d/` drop-in is shipped. Default systemd journald `Storage=auto` means `/var/log/journal` is non-persistent unless the directory exists; security events (login attempts, audit traces) evaporate at reboot. | [packages/core/systemd/](../../packages/core/systemd/), [config/systemd/](../../config/systemd/) | Ship `/etc/systemd/journald.conf.d/00-intergenos-persistent.conf` with `Storage=persistent`, `Compress=yes`, `SystemMaxUse=2G`, `MaxRetentionSec=90day`; mkdir `/var/log/journal` in chroot-config-ch9.sh. | open | |
| F-022 | Medium | No /etc/skel default umask / dotfile hardening | /etc/skel (chroot-config-ch9.sh:181) ships .bashrc + .bash_profile but no `umask 027` (private-by-default file creation) and no `.ssh/` with 0700 perms pre-created. New users default to upstream umask 022 (world-readable file creation), spilling into editor backups, downloaded archives, etc. | [chroot-config-ch9.sh:181](../../scripts/chroot-config-ch9.sh#L181) | Add `umask 027` to /etc/skel/.bash_profile; create empty /etc/skel/.ssh/ with mode 0700. | open | |
| F-023 | Medium | `lastchg=19800` in live shadow + installer-set root has aging disabled | `installer/init/init.sh:253` writes `liveuser:*:19800:0:99999:7:::` (max 99999 days = effectively never), and `installer/backend/users.py:30` runs `passwd -x 99999` for root which disables password aging entirely. No `chage` policy is applied to the created user. | [init.sh:253](../../installer/init/init.sh#L253), [users.py:30](../../installer/backend/users.py#L30) | Either ship sensible `chage` defaults (max 365 days, warn 14 days) OR document explicitly that InterGenOS does not enforce password aging by design. | open | |
| F-024 | Medium | shim's vendor MOK enrollment posture undocumented; mokutil pre-enroll missing | shim-signed (packages/core/shim-signed/build.sh:33) extracts shimx64.efi + mmx64.efi from the Fedora RPM. There's no automated MOK pre-enrollment into shim's vendor-db at build time. Installed-system kernel/GRUB signed by the per-install MOK is verified by MokManager-enrolled keys only, NOT by the InterGenOS root of trust. If MOK enrollment fails or is skipped, the chain falls back to "trust whatever loads," defeating the security promise. | [shim-signed/build.sh:33](../../packages/core/shim-signed/build.sh#L33), [docker/shim-build/vendor-cert/](../../docker/shim-build/vendor-cert/) | Replace shim-signed (Fedora extract) with a true InterGenOS shim built via shim-review (vendor-cert section pre-populated with intergenos-secure-boot-ca.der), OR document that the current posture is "MOK-enrollment-or-bust" with no fallback root of trust. | open | |
| F-025 | Medium | `tester` user created in shadow post_install — ships to every install | `packages/core/shadow/build.sh:75-77` creates a `tester` user during package build. Comment says it's for LFS test-suite use, but the user persists into the shipped chroot/squashfs. Account has no password set (locked), but it's a free-uid login surface and a name to scan for. | [shadow/build.sh:75](../../packages/core/shadow/build.sh#L75) | Move `tester` user creation into a build-only script that the chroot-build phase invokes; userdel the `tester` account in build-squashfs.sh cleanup before mksquashfs. | open | |
| F-026 | Low | MOK enrollment: no documented recovery / verification post-install | The installer's mok.py runs `mokutil --import` to queue enrollment but never sanity-checks at first boot that enrollment actually completed. | F-049 | High | `intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service` runs as root with zero hardening — first-boot UX parses password input | Greeter ExecStart=`/usr/libexec/intergenos/first-boot-greeter` runs as root, no User=, no NoNewPrivileges, no SystemCall filter, no ProtectSystem. Bug in tty parsing (or binary-path race) is straight LPE before any login. | [installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service:35](../../installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service#L35) | Add `ProtectSystem=strict`, `ReadWritePaths=/etc /var/lib/intergen /etc/intergenos`, `ProtectHome=read-only`, `CapabilityBoundingSet=CAP_CHOWN CAP_SETUID CAP_SETGID CAP_DAC_OVERRIDE`, `RestrictAddressFamilies=AF_UNIX`, `SystemCallFilter=@system-service`. | **PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-05-20 via Item 4 medium hardening commit (cross-coordinator-concur'd: installed-system coordinator 12:25:58Z proposal + Windows-host coordinator 12:31:42Z BLOCKER + MINOR + build-system coordinator 16:19:19Z full-concur).** 3 documented deviations from the F-049 literal recommendation: (1) ProtectSystem downgraded from =strict-class to =true because password-tool writes credential database at /etc + PAM modules touch /etc/security configuration files + libpwquality reads /etc/pwquality; (2) CapabilityBoundingSet uses CAP_CHOWN + CAP_DAC_OVERRIDE + CAP_FOWNER + CAP_AUDIT_WRITE instead of the F-049 literal CAP_CHOWN + CAP_SETUID + CAP_SETGID + CAP_DAC_OVERRIDE — CAP_AUDIT_WRITE preserves first-boot password event audit trail (high-value forensics), CAP_FOWNER covers password-tool file ownership ops, SETUID + SETGID not needed since greeter runs as root throughout; (3) RestrictAddressFamilies adds AF_NETLINK to AF_UNIX because libaudit opens NETLINK_AUDIT socket for the audit events CAP_AUDIT_WRITE enables. Full ReadWritePaths omitted since ProtectSystem=true keeps /etc writable without explicit enumeration. Resolution path: `installer/data/intergenos-first-boot-greeter.service` [Service] section now ships 19 medium-hardening directives — NoNewPrivileges=yes + ProtectSystem=true (downgraded from =strict-class because greeter writes credential database + flag at /etc; ProtectSystem=full or =strict would mount /etc read-only and fail all 3 writes per Windows-host coordinator BLOCKER + build-system coordinator verification) + ProtectHome=yes + ProtectKernel{Tunables,Modules,Logs}=yes + ProtectClock=yes + ProtectControlGroups=yes + ProtectHostname=yes + PrivateTmp=yes + RestrictAddressFamilies=AF_UNIX AF_NETLINK (AF_NETLINK added per Windows-host coordinator MINOR + build-system coordinator concur — libaudit opens NETLINK_AUDIT socket for PAM USER_CHAUTHTOK/USER_AUTH events; AF_UNIX-only would cause silent degradation and CAP_AUDIT_WRITE would become inert) + RestrictNamespaces=yes + RestrictRealtime=yes + RestrictSUIDSGID=yes + LockPersonality=yes + SystemCallArchitectures=native + SystemCallFilter=@system-service (literal @-prefix syscall-group token per systemd.exec(5) predefined-syscall-groups) + CapabilityBoundingSet=CAP_CHOWN CAP_DAC_OVERRIDE CAP_FOWNER CAP_AUDIT_WRITE (4-cap minimum matching password-tool + libaudit access pattern) + MemoryDenyWriteExecute=yes. Stale `After=intergen-firstboot.service` ordering line atomic-bundle-removed in same commit per audit-multi-wiring-single-commit POWER rule (firstboot rewrite uses per-user autostart .desktop chain on first GDM login, not a systemd unit). F-049 surgical-hardening exemption shape anticipated by 63c2edb5. | code @ bb43a724 |
| F-050 | High | sshd.service has `KillMode=process` AND `Restart=on-failure` — orphan child sessions survive daemon kill but daemon never restarts on clean exit | `config/systemd/sshd.service:38,41`. KillMode=process leaves child sessions; Restart=on-failure means clean `sshd -D` exit doesn't trigger restart. With `ExecStartPre=ssh-keygen -A`, a rotated host-key flow `systemctl restart sshd` after host-key removal silently does NOT regen keys if previous daemon exited cleanly. Behavior is unit-state-dependent and not user-obvious. | [config/systemd/sshd.service:35-42](../../config/systemd/sshd.service#L35) | Change to `KillMode=mixed` (main+children) and `Restart=always`; ExecStartPre key-gen always re-tests. | open | |
| F-051 | Medium | UKI cmdlines lack `vsyscall=none`, `audit=1`, `audit_backlog_limit=8192`, `pti=on` enforcement | F-020 noted slab_nomerge/init_on_alloc/init_on_free/pti=on absent. Adjacent: no `audit=1` means kernel audit subsystem starts disabled — AVC denials don't reliably reach userspace audit log without it. No `audit_backlog_limit` means default-1024 backlog drops events under load. No `vsyscall=none` (cross-ref F-046). | [installer/init/cmdline.live.txt:1](../../installer/init/cmdline.live.txt#L1) | Append `audit=1 audit_backlog_limit=8192 vsyscall=none pti=on` to all three cmdline files. | open | |
| F-052 | Medium | `pam_env.so` referenced in 4 PAM stacks but `/etc/security/pam_env.conf` and `/etc/environment` never shipped — silent no-op, config-bomb regression vector | `shadow-pam/build.sh:75,104` + `linux-pam/build.sh:80` + `sudo/build.sh:48` all include `session required pam_env.so`. pam_env reads `/etc/security/pam_env.conf` and `/etc/environment`. Neither file ships. Default-empty = no-op (acceptable), but `required` directive means syntax error in admin-dropped pam_env.conf locks out all sessions. Companion to F-044. | [packages/core/shadow-pam/build.sh:75](../../packages/core/shadow-pam/build.sh#L75), [packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh:80](../../packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh#L80) | Ship empty `/etc/environment` + commented-out `/etc/security/pam_env.conf.template`; downgrade `required` to `optional`. | open | |
| F-053 | Medium | `pam_loginuid.so` placed AFTER `pam_limits.so` in /etc/pam.d/system-session/systemd-user — auditing loginuid set after session-tracked modules fire | linux-pam/build.sh:80-87 ordering: pam_env → pam_limits → pam_keyinit → pam_systemd; loginuid (in some stacks via shadow-pam) follows limits not precedes. Upstream-systemd-shipped stack places `pam_loginuid.so` first so audit/session-tracked modules see the correct loginuid. | [packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh:76-87](../../packages/core/linux-pam/build.sh#L76) | Reorder `pam_loginuid.so` to come BEFORE pam_env/pam_limits in /etc/pam.d/systemd-user; align with upstream-systemd stack. | open | |
| F-054 | Medium | `CONFIG_KPROBES=y` enabled in production kernel — root can attach dynamic probes to any kernel function | `config/kernel/fragments/00-universal-baseline.config:362`. | F-055 | Medium | `CONFIG_USERFAULTFD=y` without `vm.unprivileged_userfaultfd=0` sysctl — known exploit primitive for kernel UAF use-after-free races | `config/kernel/fragments/00-universal-baseline.config:2679`. userfaultfd has long exploit history (Project-Zero kernel chains, Dirty-Pipe-class). Modern kernels gate via `vm.unprivileged_userfaultfd` sysctl. Even if default=0, no /etc/sysctl.d/ override enforces it (F-012). | [config/kernel/fragments/00-universal-baseline.config:2679](../../config/kernel/fragments/00-universal-baseline.config#L2679) | Either compile out OR ship `/etc/sysctl.d/99-intergenos-hardening.conf` with `vm.unprivileged_userfaultfd = 0`, `kernel.unprivileged_userns_clone = 0`. | open | |
| F-056 | Medium | systemd-resolved + systemd-timesync ship upstream-defaults (no LLMNR=no, no NTS, no DoT enforcement) | F-029 covered resolved DNSSEC/DoT. No `LLMNR=no` (known spoofing vector — Responder.py target). systemd-timesyncd ships with no Servers= override + no NTS — defaults to ntp.org pool over UDP-123 cleartext. | [installer/backend/users.py:93](../../installer/backend/users.py#L93), [scripts/create-image.sh:331](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L331) | Extend resolved.conf.d/ with `LLMNR=no`, `DNSSEC=allow-downgrade`, `DNSOverTLS=opportunistic`; ship timesyncd.conf with `Servers=time.cloudflare.com time1.google.com`. | open | |
| F-057 | Medium | No systemd-coredump.conf override — kernel coredumps land at `/var/lib/systemd/coredump/`, group-readable | systemd ships `Storage=external` + `Compress=yes` defaults; coredumps land at `/var/lib/systemd/coredump/`, mode 0640 root:systemd-coredump. Non-privileged member of `systemd-coredump` group can read them. | F-058 | Low | sudo `Defaults` lack `env_reset`, `mail_badpass`, `use_pty`, `logfile=` — no forensic trail / no PATH hardening | `sudo/build.sh:39` ships only `Defaults secure_path="/usr/sbin:/usr/bin"`. **Iter-3 cross-check note (Lane F)**: 24 new findings (F-035..F-058). **Five new Holy-Grail-class**: F-035/F-036 (install-theming.sh's nftables block clobbers canonical package's config AND service AND bypasses preset → SSH brute-force window open from boot 1), F-037 (live UKI cmdline ships KERN_DEBUG-level + journal-to-console = info leak on every public-facing release artifact), F-038 (intergen.service runs as root with ZERO hardening — strictly less sandboxed than nginx), F-039 (AppArmor profiles ship but no orchestrator transitions them to complain mode — defense theater for the 4 custom profiles). **Five new Critical**: F-040 DEBUG_FS_ALLOW_ALL, F-041 MAGIC_SYSRQ_SERIAL, F-042 sudoers.d perms/visudo, F-043 PROC_KCORE+DEVMEM, F-044 pam_access required without config. Plus 8 High (F-045..F-050 kernel hardening configs + sshd unit semantics) and 6 Medium/Low (cmdline gaps, PAM config-bombs, coredump policy). Cross-lane: F-035/F-036 ↔ G-005 (canonical package policy=accept) ↔ J-021 (the same install-theming.sh write clobber). F-038/F-048/F-049 form a service-hardening-gap class — three highly-privileged services run with zero hardening.

### Lane G — Network + systemd service hygiene

_(IGOSC sub-agent population; seeded)_

| G-002 | High | mariadb /run/mysqld vs /run/mariadb path mismatch | Service declares `ReadWritePaths=/run/mysqld`; package's own tmpfiles.d creates `/run/mariadb`; unit will fail at start | [mariadb.service:41](../../packages/extra/mariadb/mariadb.service#L41) | Pick one path; align both sides | open | |
