| G-004 | Holy-Grail | SSH host keys baked into squashfs — every install shares keys (twin of F-002) | `core/openssh/build.sh:82` runs `ssh-keygen -A` in post_install during chroot build, baking ed25519/rsa/ecdsa host keys into the chroot; `create-image.sh:280` regenerates again in the qcow2 image flow. `build-squashfs.sh` has NO host-key reset before mksquashfs — the live ISO ships with the build-host's keys, and every installed system from that ISO shares the same SSH host fingerprints. MITM-trivial across the fleet. | [openssh/build.sh:82](../../packages/core/openssh/build.sh#L82), [create-image.sh:280](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L280), [build-squashfs.sh:217](../../scripts/build-squashfs.sh#L217) | Add `rm -f /etc/ssh/ssh_host_*_key*` to build-squashfs.sh cleanup block (next to machine-id reset); ship a sshd-keygen.service oneshot wired Before=sshd.service to regenerate per-install at first boot. | open | |
| G-005 | Holy-Grail | nftables default ruleset is policy=accept on every chain | `nftables.conf:17,27,31` declares input/forward/output with `policy accept`; only ct-state-invalid drop + loopback-trust as filters. Comment claims "permissive default — Operators tighten to default-drop." But `90-nftables.preset` markets this as a "default-deny baseline." Shipped posture is wide-open firewall on every install — anyone on the LAN can reach every service that the operator later enables. Holy-Grail security alignment requires deny-by-default with explicit allow rules. | [nftables.conf:17](../../packages/core/nftables/nftables.conf#L17), [90-nftables.preset:4](../../packages/core/nftables/90-nftables.preset#L4) | Flip input + forward chains to `policy drop`; ship explicit `accept` for loopback, established/related, and the minimum service surface (sshd if enabled). Align preset comment to actual behavior. | open | |
| G-006 | High | Dual network managers enabled in qcow2 image path | `create-image.sh:369-374` enables `systemd-networkd.service` and `systemd-resolved.service` via target.wants/ symlinks. The squashfs has NM enabled; the disk image flow re-enables networkd on top, so the installed system from the image has both managers fighting for interfaces. Indeterminate DHCP / DNS behavior on first boot. | [create-image.sh:369](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L369), [networkmanager/build.sh:60](../../packages/desktop/networkmanager/build.sh#L60) | Pick one (NetworkManager per the desktop-tier choice); delete the systemd-networkd enable block from create-image.sh, and stop writing `/etc/systemd/network/10-dhcp.network` (consumed only by networkd). | open | |

Live ISO boots with no /etc/resolv.conf; DNS broken until NetworkManager (which writes the file itself) finishes the DHCP path — or systemd-resolved is asked nicely. | G-015 | Medium | D-Bus activation file for intergen bypasses systemd unit (no SystemdService=) | `intergen/build.sh:117-121` ships `/usr/share/dbus-1/services/com.intergenos.InterGen.service` with `Name=com.intergenos.InterGen` and `Exec=/usr/bin/intergen daemon` but no `SystemdService=intergen.service`. D-Bus activation will spawn intergen daemon as the bus user's child, not via systemd — bypassing the systemd unit's user-level integration, restart policy, journal capture. | [intergen/build.sh:117](../../packages/ai/intergen/build.sh#L117) | Add `SystemdService=intergen.service` line; also add `User=` field per current freedesktop spec for system-bus activation. | open | |
| G-016 | Medium | influxdb/memcached EnvironmentFile= with no leading dash → unit fails on missing file | `influxdb.service:10` declares `EnvironmentFile=/etc/influxdb/influxdb.env` and `memcached.service:20` declares `EnvironmentFile=/etc/sysconfig/memcached`. | G-017 | Medium | nginx ReadWritePaths=/run (entire tmpfs) is overly broad | nginx.service:44 declares `ReadWritePaths=/var/log/nginx /var/cache/nginx /run` — the whole /run, not /run/nginx. Bypasses the namespace-isolation point: nginx workers get write access to dbus sockets, systemd's runtime state, every other service's runtime files. Should be `/run/nginx`. PIDFile=/run/nginx.pid (line 20) is also at the top of /run, not under /run/nginx. | [nginx.service:20](../../packages/extra/nginx/nginx.service#L20), [nginx.service:44](../../packages/extra/nginx/nginx.service#L44) | Add tmpfiles.d entry for /run/nginx, move PIDFile to /run/nginx/nginx.pid, tighten ReadWritePaths to /run/nginx. | open | |
| G-018 | Medium | intergen-firstboot.service has no Restart=, ExecStartPost writes flag without verifying dir | `intergen-firstboot.service:11-12` runs `/usr/bin/intergen-firstboot` then `ExecStartPost=/usr/bin/touch /var/lib/intergen/.firstboot-done`. No `mkdir -p /var/lib/intergen` first — if the dir doesn't exist (firstboot animation package ships separately per D-001 and may not be installed), touch fails and ExecStartPost fails. Also no Restart= directive, no failure-action — unit just silently fails. | [intergen-firstboot.service:11](../../assets/intergen-firstboot-drm/intergen-firstboot.service#L11) | Add `StateDirectory=intergen` to auto-create /var/lib/intergen with correct mode; OR add `ExecStartPre=/usr/bin/mkdir -p /var/lib/intergen`. | open | |
| G-019 | Medium | igos-live-dconf-compile.service DefaultDependencies=no but doesn't pull basic.target | init.sh:348-363 writes a oneshot unit with `DefaultDependencies=no` and only `After=local-fs.target`. Without DefaultDependencies, the unit doesn't get standard ordering. `dconf update` may fire before /tmp is even tmpfs-mounted. Tolerable because dconf is read-mostly, but breaks the "DefaultDependencies=no must compensate with explicit deps" rule. | [init.sh:351](../../installer/init/init.sh#L351) | Either drop DefaultDependencies=no (default chain is fine for this unit), or add `Requires=sysinit.target` and `After=sysinit.target`. | open | |
| G-020 | Medium | systemd-firstboot.service masked in init.sh but never built — phantom mask | systemd `core/systemd/build.sh:32` and `desktop/systemd-pass2/build.sh:29` both pass `-D firstboot=false` — `systemd-firstboot.service` is not produced. init.sh:210 masks the phantom unit. No effect, but parallel to G-003. Likewise `systemd-homed-firstboot.service` at line 211: homed=disabled in pass1, homed=enabled in pass2 — homed-firstboot may or may not exist depending on pass-2 timing. | [init.sh:210](../../installer/init/init.sh#L210), [systemd/build.sh:32](../../packages/core/systemd/build.sh#L32) | Either drop the masks (unbuilt = nothing to mask), or build with `firstboot=true` so the masks have a target. | open | |
| G-021 | Medium | sshd_config sets PermitRootLogin=yes — Holy-Grail-adjacent (twin of F-003) | `openssh/build.sh:79` runs `sed -i 's/^#PermitRootLogin prohibit-password/PermitRootLogin yes/' /etc/ssh/sshd_config` in post_install. Combined with G-004 (shared host keys) and the create-image.sh forced ROOT_PASSWORD policy, every installed system ships with root-SSH-login over network enabled. Defense-in-depth violation. | [openssh/build.sh:79](../../packages/core/openssh/build.sh#L79) | Change to `PermitRootLogin prohibit-password` (the upstream default) or `PermitRootLogin no` if no admin keys are pre-staged. | open | |
| G-022 | Low | Server services use After=network.target instead of After=network-online.target | etcd/haproxy/influxdb/memcached/valkey/postgresql/mariadb/nginx/apache-httpd/caddy/lighttpd all `After=network.target` only. network.target signifies "network stack initialized" not "interface is up." Defaults bind to 127.0.0.1 so safe, but operators who edit configs to bind 0.0.0.0 hit startup races where the bind() fails because no interface is up yet. | [etcd.service:3](../../packages/extra/etcd/etcd.service#L3), [postgresql.service:15](../../packages/extra/postgresql/postgresql.service#L15) | Add `Wants=network-online.target` and `After=network-online.target` to each service; or document explicitly that operators changing bind-address must also `systemctl edit` the unit to add the dep. | open | |
| G-023 | Low | forge-tui.service has circular Wants/WantedBy on multi-user.target | forge-tui.service:4-5 has `After=multi-user.target` and `Wants=multi-user.target`, then [Install] WantedBy=multi-user.target (line 32). Wants= in [Unit] section toward a target the unit is also wanted by is circular dependency — systemd resolves it by ignoring one direction, but the unit author clearly meant `After=basic.target Wants=basic.target` (or just `WantedBy=multi-user.target` alone). | [forge-tui.service:4](../../installer/data/forge-tui.service#L4) | Drop `Wants=multi-user.target` from [Unit] section; WantedBy= alone covers ordering. | open | |
| G-024 | Low | sshd.service ships zero hardening flags | `config/systemd/sshd.service:14-15` deliberately omits ProtectSystem/ProtectKernel* per comment ("SSH spawns user sessions inheriting mount namespace"). Comment is wrong for the daemon itself — Debian/Fedora ship sshd.service with ProtectSystem=full etc. Result: sshd has no hardening of any kind, while every server in /extra has full baseline. | [sshd.service:14](../../config/systemd/sshd.service#L14) | Add at least `ProtectSystem=full`, `ProtectKernelTunables=yes`, `ProtectKernelModules=yes`, `ProtectControlGroups=yes`, `RestrictRealtime=yes`, `RestrictSUIDSGID=yes` (PAM needs namespaces + IPC for user sessions, so leave those alone). | open | |
| G-025 | Low | init.sh masks `atopgpu.service` but it's a real upstream unit | atop's upstream Makefile installs both `atop.service` and `atopgpu.service` into /usr/lib/systemd/system. The atop package itself doesn't enable atopgpu (opt-in for GPU monitoring); 99-default-disable preset already covers that. The init.sh mask at line 220 is redundant/dead. Not phantom in the G-003 sense (the unit exists) but pointless. | [init.sh:220](../../installer/init/init.sh#L220), [atop/build.sh:13](../../packages/base/atop/build.sh#L13) | Drop the atopgpu mask; preset-disable already handles it. | open | |
| G-026 | Low | nftables.service: Wants/Before=network-pre.target but no PartOf= | nftables.service:4-5 has the standard `Wants=network-pre.target Before=network-pre.target` pair; missing `PartOf=network-pre.target` means restart of network-pre doesn't propagate to nftables. Minor for a static-ruleset firewall but inconsistent with how upstream nftables.service has evolved. | [nftables.service:4](../../packages/core/nftables/nftables.service#L4) | Add `PartOf=network-pre.target`. | open | |
| G-027 | Low | OpenSSH sshd.service has both RuntimeDirectory=sshd AND tmpfiles.d/sshd.conf — redundant | `openssh/build.sh:48-50` installs a tmpfiles.d entry creating `/run/sshd`; `config/systemd/sshd.service:45` also declares `RuntimeDirectory=sshd`. Both work — but only one is needed. With both, dir created at boot AND at every restart. Choose one. (Counter-example to G-001: this service has it right + redundant, while 7 others have nothing.) | [openssh/build.sh:48](../../packages/core/openssh/build.sh#L48), [sshd.service:45](../../config/systemd/sshd.service#L45) | Drop the tmpfiles.d/sshd.conf install (RuntimeDirectory= alone is canonical for non-shared sockets). | open | |
| G-028 | Cosmetic | Server packages declare ReadWritePaths under /var/log/<svc> but build.sh creates them mode 750 owned by root | Build.sh of etcd/haproxy/influxdb/memcached/valkey/postgresql/mariadb/nginx/apache-httpd/lighttpd uses `install -d -m 750 $DESTDIR/var/log/<svc>` at build (root-owned). post_install then chowns to the service user — but only if post_install actually runs against the installed system. Net: ownership occasionally drifts to root after a pkm reinstall, causing the service to fail to write logs. | [etcd/build.sh:62](../../packages/extra/etcd/build.sh#L62) | Move dir-create + chown to a tmpfiles.d entry per service: `d /var/log/<svc> 0750 <user> <group> - -` — fires deterministically at every boot. | open | |
| G-029 | Medium | /etc/systemd/network/10-dhcp.network written twice with divergent parameters | chroot-config-ch9.sh:38-50 writes the file with `DHCP=ipv4` + `[DHCPv4]` UseDNS/UseDomains. create-image.sh:378-384 writes the SAME path in the mounted image with `DHCP=yes` (IPv4+IPv6 dual). The qcow2 image path overwrites whatever chroot-config-ch9 wrote — two different DHCP intents. Since NetworkManager owns the stack (G-006), both dead config; if networkd ever re-engages, behavior depends on which writer ran last. | [chroot-config-ch9.sh:38](../../scripts/chroot-config-ch9.sh#L38), [create-image.sh:378](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L378) | Pick one writer (or delete both per G-012); align DHCP mode. | open | |
| G-030 | Low | No StartLimitBurst / StartLimitIntervalSec on any /extra service | None of the 11 server units declare `StartLimitBurst=` or `StartLimitIntervalSec=`. When G-009 is closed (adding `Restart=on-failure` to postgres/memcached/haproxy/nginx), restart loops are unbounded. | [packages/extra/*/*.service](../../packages/extra/) | Add `StartLimitBurst=5` + `StartLimitIntervalSec=10min` to [Unit] section of each server unit. | open | |
| G-031 | Medium | G-022 remediation would hang boot — NetworkManager-wait-online explicitly disabled | networkmanager-pass1/build.sh:62 and networkmanager/build.sh:69 both `systemctl disable NetworkManager-wait-online.service`. So network-online.target is never satisfied at boot. If operators (or G-022's remediation) add `After=network-online.target`, boot hangs at the network-online.target wait. Ordering trap. | [networkmanager-pass1/build.sh:62](../../packages/core/networkmanager-pass1/build.sh#L62), [networkmanager/build.sh:69](../../packages/desktop/networkmanager/build.sh#L69) | Either re-enable NM-wait-online (accept boot-with-no-link delay) or document explicitly that server bind-on-0.0.0.0 operators must not add the dep. | open | |
| G-032 | Low | forge-tui.service ordering loop: After=multi-user.target + Before=getty@tty1.service | forge-tui.service:4 `After=multi-user.target` AND line 14 `Before=getty@tty1.service`. getty@tty1.service is pulled in via multi-user.target's wants set. systemd will silently resolve one direction. Compounds G-023's same-target circularity. | [forge-tui.service:4](../../installer/data/forge-tui.service#L4), [forge-tui.service:14](../../installer/data/forge-tui.service#L14) | Use `After=basic.target` (or drop After= entirely); keep Conflicts=getty@tty1.service + Before=getty@tty1.service. | open | |
| G-033 | Medium | post_install systemctl daemon-reload / enable commands silently failed in chroot | Every package in /extra runs `systemctl daemon-reload`/`systemctl enable` with `2>/dev/null \|\| true`. In chroot (no dbus, no PID-1 systemd), these uniformly fail and are swallowed. Actual unit-enable comes from chroot-config-ch9.sh:507 + build-squashfs.sh:177 `systemctl preset-all` — per-package enables are dead. | [etcd/build.sh:78-83](../../packages/extra/etcd/build.sh#L78), [postgresql/build.sh:135-140](../../packages/extra/postgresql/build.sh#L135) | Delete the `systemctl enable` calls from /extra build.sh files; document preset-driven model. | open | |

**Iter-2 cross-check note (Lane G)**: 26/28 iter-1 rows VALIDATED. 1 FALSE-POSITIVE: G-002 (mariadb path-mismatch framing wrong — there's no tmpfiles.d for `/run/mariadb` at all; issue is identical to G-001, just an 8th missing-tmpfiles.d package — merge into G-001's class). 1 partial-FP cosmetic: G-028 (half packages — haproxy/memcached/postgresql/nginx — use correct `install -dm755 -o <user>` pattern; finding's universal claim overstated). G-004 (SSH host keys) and G-005 (nftables policy=accept) Holy-Grail-class re-verified exactly. G-021 (PermitRootLogin=yes) twin of F-003 — consistent. **Important warning**: G-031 documents a TRAP — naive `After=network-online.target` remediation on G-022 hangs boot indefinitely because NM-wait-online is disabled by design.

| G-034 | High | `lighttpd.service` is `Type=forking` with no `PIDFile=` — systemd cannot track main PID | `lighttpd.service:6` declares Type=forking but no PIDFile=. systemd-style guidance: forking services MUST set PIDFile=. `ExecReload=/bin/kill -HUP $MAINPID` may signal wrong process; KillMode=control-group keeps stop working but reload unreliable. nginx correctly sets `PIDFile=/run/nginx.pid` — inconsistent class. | [lighttpd.service:6](../../packages/extra/lighttpd/lighttpd.service#L6) | Switch to `Type=simple` with `lighttpd -D` (foreground) — preferred — or add `PIDFile=/run/lighttpd/lighttpd.pid` + tmpfiles.d entry. | open | |

Asymmetric drift vs sed for PermitRootLogin. | [openssh/build.sh:78](../../packages/core/openssh/build.sh#L78) | Replace `echo >>` with grep-guard: `grep -q '^UsePAM ' /etc/ssh/sshd_config \|\| echo "UsePAM yes" >>`; or ship `/etc/ssh/sshd_config.d/10-intergenos.conf` drop-in. | open | |

**Iter-3 cross-check note (Lane G)**: 17 new findings (G-034..G-050). The dominant theme is **negative space**: things that should ship but don't — no NM.conf, no logind.conf, no oomd.conf (G-039 — service enabled but inert without policy), no system.conf, no .slice files. G-036 surfaces a **booby-trap** mirroring G-031: nftables ExecStop=flush ruleset becomes a momentary firewall-bypass the instant G-005 is fixed (both must land together). G-042 surfaces a **dead remediation** (update-pki.timer killed by G-033 + 99-default-disable catch-all). G-035 surfaces **idempotency drift accumulator** (UsePAM appended on every reinstall). G-038/G-039/G-040/G-041 form a single coherent unit — oomd needs accounting needs slices, all currently absent.

### Lane I — InterGen AI integration

_(IGOSC sub-agent population; seeded)_

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| I-001 | Low | intergen/data/intergen.service is orphan dead code | Package build.sh generates its own inline replacement; source file misleading | [intergen/data/intergen.service](../../intergen/data/intergen.service) | Delete the orphan; build.sh inline is authoritative | open | |
| I-002 | Low | intergen/data/com.intergenos.InterGen.service same orphan class | Same as I-001 | [intergen/data/com.intergenos.InterGen.service](../../intergen/data/com.intergenos.InterGen.service) | Delete the orphan | open | |
| I-003 | Medium | ai/intergen verify_paths undercount | Declares 2 paths; build.sh installs ~10 (CLI wrapper, config, systemd user unit, dbus service, state dirs) | [packages/ai/intergen/package.yml](../../packages/ai/intergen/package.yml) | Extend verify_paths to cover load-bearing entry points | open | |
| I-004 | Critical | dbus_daemon main() never enters a main loop | `main()` calls `start_service()`, logs status, and falls off the end; no `GLib.MainLoop().run()`, no `signal.pause()`. Process exits immediately. systemd `Type=dbus` will wait for the bus-name acquisition, then see the process die → unit marked failed. The literal comment `# In production, the D-Bus main loop would run here.` confirms it's an unfinished skeleton. The CLI fallthrough at `cli.py:90-96` spawns a transient direct session each `ask`, masking the missing daemon. | [intergen/dbus_daemon.py:515](../../intergen/dbus_daemon.py#L515) | Add `from gi.repository import GLib; GLib.MainLoop().run()` after `start_service()` and call `loop.quit()` from the shutdown handler. | open | |
| I-005 | Holy-Grail | Model SHA256 verification is TOFU (no pinned hashes) | `MODEL_CATALOG` declares `sha256=""` for all three tier models and the embedding model. `verify_model()` line 217-222 records the computed hash on first download and returns True ("No expected hash — recording"). Any MITM, compromised HF mirror, or model-repo rug-pull is accepted blindly, then locked in as "trusted". The download path at line 124 only checks the hash if `model.sha256` is non-empty. Violates Holy-Grail supply chain rule for any artifact loaded into the model runtime. | [intergen/model_manager.py:30-67](../../intergen/model_manager.py#L30), [intergen/model_manager.py:217](../../intergen/model_manager.py#L217) | Populate sha256 fields with pinned, audited values for each released model build; reject downloads on empty manifest hash; never auto-trust on first download. | **STRUCTURALLY RESOLVED 2026-05-20 via T0-4-D unified commit (operator-PIV-signed `intergen/data/models-manifest.json` + armored detached `.asc` produced via `gpg --detach-sign --armor`; consumer `_load_pins` reads pinned SHA256 set; `verify_model` fail-closed against empty manifest; TOFU branch removed).** Resolution path: `intergen/data/models-manifest.json` (3 entries: Qwen3.5-2B + Qwen3.5-9B + nomic-embed-text-v1.5 per operator-decided Option A scope 2026-05-20) ships to `/usr/share/intergen/models-manifest.json` via `packages/ai/intergen/build.sh` Step 5; consumer integration via Steps 3+4 `model_manager` refactor + `dbus_daemon` `INTERGEN_MODEL_PATH` -> `verify_arbitrary_path` wiring; tests at Step 6 (5/5 PASS). | I-006 | High | User-service daemon writes to root-owned paths | build.sh installs `intergen.service` as a systemd **user** unit at `/usr/lib/systemd/user/intergen.service` and `systemctl --global enable`s it for every user. | I-007 | Medium | Two divergent shell-safety classifiers in same package | `intergen/safety.py` and `intergen/tools/run_command.py` independently classify shell commands and disagree on real cases: `mount`/`umount` are BLOCKED in safety.py but AUTO in run_command.py; `sudo` is BLOCKED in safety.py but CONFIRM in run_command.py; `chmod`/`chown` are BLOCKED in safety.py but CONFIRM in run_command.py; `parted` is BLOCKED in both (intergen would refuse the installer's own partitioner). Only run_command.py is wired in via `RunCommandTool.classify_safety`; safety.py is dead code waiting to mislead the next maintainer. | [intergen/safety.py:91-128](../../intergen/safety.py#L91), [intergen/tools/run_command.py:26-67](../../intergen/tools/run_command.py#L26) | Pick one classifier; delete the other; add a unit test that asserts a single canonical policy. | open | |
| I-008 | Medium | intergen-welcome surfaces no intergen functionality | The 991-line GTK welcome wizard has a "Meet InterGen" page but zero references to `intergen daemon`, `intergen ask`, `intergen setup`, the `com.intergenos.InterGen` D-Bus name, llama-server, or `/usr/bin/intergen`. **Iter-2 cross-check note (Lane I)**: 16/16 iter-1 rows VALIDATED. Two Critical claims — I-004 (dbus_daemon main() never enters main loop; literal comment "In production, the D-Bus main loop would run here." at line 517 confirms unfinished skeleton) and I-005 (MODEL_CATALOG sha256="" with TOFU verify_model) — reproduced verbatim at cited lines. Voice POWER-RULE compliance confirmed: router.py:4 explicit "No voice" comment. Notable iter-2 elevation: **I-023 (High)** — `sudo` in CONFIRM_COMMANDS effectively gives the model a one-click root door once user confirms; safety classifier is structurally weaker than I-007 alone communicates. Subsumed-by-fix chain: I-018, I-019, I-021 close when I-004/I-006 close.

| I-027 | Holy-Grail | `SafetyTier.CONFIRM` is never enforced — every CONFIRM tool executes immediately, no user gate | `tool_registry.execute()` checks ONLY `safety == SafetyTier.BLOCKED` and silently proceeds for CONFIRM. No callback, no prompt, no PolicyKit dialog, no IPC pause. Every "confirm" tool — write_file (always CONFIRM), manage_packages install/remove, manage_services start/stop/enable, run_command for CONFIRM_COMMANDS — runs the moment the LLM emits the tool call. User-facing copy ("require user confirmation") is a fiction. A prompt-injected web_search result that says "write to ~/.bashrc" goes straight to disk. | [intergen/tool_registry.py:99-115](../../intergen/tool_registry.py#L99) | Wire confirmation callback: tool registry returns PENDING for CONFIRM-tier and emits D-Bus signal `ConfirmationRequired(call_id, tool, args)`; only proceed on matching `Confirm(call_id)`. Until that exists, treat CONFIRM as BLOCKED. | I-031 | High | `events.jsonl` logs first 80 chars of every LLM response + tool-call source to disk, world-readable on fallback path | `router.py:874-887` EventLogger emits `message=f"{source}: {result.text[:80]}"` per turn. `mcp_client.py:296-313` audit log writes argument values for every MCP call. | I-032 | High | Per-user daemon model has NO file-locking around `/var/lib/intergen/models/` or llama-server port 8080 — two simultaneous user logins race | Two users log in via GDM in parallel; both `intergen.service --user` instances initialize: each spawns `LlamaManager.start(model_path, port=8080)`. | I-033 | High | `MCPServerConfig.command` accepts arbitrary binary path with NO trust-tier gate before subprocess execution; UNTRUSTED is default | `mcp_client._MCPServerConnection.connect()` (158-166) does `subprocess.Popen([self.config.command] + self.config.args)` with NO validation that command is in any allow-list, NO refusal-by-default for `trust_tier == UNTRUSTED`. Tool DESCRIPTIONS validated via SentinelGuard but never gates SPAWNING. A `mcp.d/*.yml` planted at `/etc/intergen/mcp.d/evil.yml` (via supply-chain) would auto-spawn `subprocess.Popen(["/tmp/evil"])` on every daemon start. | I-034 | High | `write_file.execute()` writes BEFORE generating the diff and BEFORE any confirmation — file is already overwritten when user sees "diff for review" | `write_file.py:91-129`: function generates diff for display, then unconditionally calls `path.write_text(content)` at line 129. Schema's `safety_tier=SafetyTier.CONFIRM` (66) and description's promise of "generates unified diff so user can review before confirming" (38) both lies — by the time diff is returned, write is done. Per I-027 CONFIRM doesn't gate, so even LLM emitting tool call already executes write. | [intergen/tools/write_file.py:91-148](../../intergen/tools/write_file.py#L91) | Reorder: stash proposed write to temp path until registry-level CONFIRM gate (I-027 fix) returns approval; only then `path.write_text`. | I-035 | High | `manage_services.py:121-122` silently prepends `sudo` to CONFIRM actions — passwordless sudo (F-004 wheel NOPASSWD default) gives uncontested root via LLM-emitted calls | When `action in CONFIRM_ACTIONS` and not user_mode, cmd is rewritten as `["sudo", "systemctl", "stop|disable|mask|...", service]` and executed via subprocess.run. No `sudo -n`, no pkexec, no PolicyKit. On a system where install lane (F-004) makes default user passwordless-sudo, the LLM can: `manage_services(action="mask", service="dbus")` → systemd dies → next reboot fails. Combined with I-027 and I-030, this is RCE-equivalent. | [intergen/tools/manage_services.py:121-127](../../intergen/tools/manage_services.py#L121) | Use `pkexec systemctl` with PolicyKit action forcing password each time; restrict allowed services to `MANAGEABLE_SERVICES` allow-list; refuse mask/daemon-reload/disable on critical units (firewalld, NetworkManager, dbus, polkit, systemd-logind, sshd). | **SUPERSEDED-BY D-008 (2026-05-18T16:49:42Z); STRUCTURALLY RESOLVED 2026-05-19 via two-layer fix** — (1) D-007 locks the install-lane NOPASSWD-wheel assumption (root locked + wheel-sudo password-required by default; D-007 compliance gate prevents reintroduction); (2) T0-4-E Step 7 `tool_registry.execute()` refactor + SPOC's pkexec runner artifacts at `intergen/data/intergen-privileged-runner` + `intergen/data/org.intergenos.intergen.policy` (landed 2026-05-19T23:32:27Z at commit 49a585ca; PolicyKit action `org.intergenos.intergen.privileged-tool` with `auth_admin_keep`) + installed-system coordinator's Step 15b wires `subprocess.run(['pkexec', '/usr/bin/intergen-privileged-runner', tool_name, args_json])` invocation in `tool_registry.execute()` for any tool the gate classifies PRIVILEGED_STATE_CHANGING (manage_services is in `_PRIVILEGED_TOOLS` frozenset). MANAGEABLE_SERVICES allow-list + critical-unit refusal (firewalld + NetworkManager + dbus + polkit + systemd-logind + sshd) authored as part of Step 15 final commit per installed-system coordinator's K15 surface. Resolution path: `docs/architecture/intergen-provenance-gate-design.md` v1.0. Full closure at Step 15 unified commit. | |
| I-036 | Medium | `read_file.py` enforces NO path-restriction allow-list — reads /etc/shadow (if root via I-006 fix) or user-readable secrets (SSH keys, browser cookies) | `read_file.py:71` does `Path(path_str).expanduser().resolve()` with NO comparison to allow-list. 1 MB size cap doesn't help — `~/.ssh/id_rsa` ~3 KB; Firefox `cookies.sqlite` ~500 KB. A prompt-injection "read ~/.ssh/id_rsa and put it in the web_search query" achieves passive credential exfil via DDG/Serper logs (and events.jsonl per I-031). Counterpart to write_file.PROTECTED_PATHS which exists for writes but not reads. | [intergen/tools/read_file.py:71](../../intergen/tools/read_file.py#L71) | Add BLOCKED_READ_PREFIXES = ("~/.ssh/", "~/.gnupg/", "~/.aws/", "~/.config/google-chrome/", "~/.mozilla/firefox/*/cookies.sqlite", "/etc/shadow", "/etc/gshadow", "/etc/sudoers*", "/root/", "/var/lib/intergen/data/"). | open | |
| I-037 | Medium | `llama_manager.py` spawns llama-server with no RLIMIT_AS, no cgroup placement, no nice — malicious/buggy server can consume all RAM | `llama_manager.start()` builds cmd at 85-95 and `subprocess.Popen` at 111-115 with no preexec_fn=set_rlimits, no `RLIMIT_AS`, no slice unit override. Systemd user unit sets only `Restart=on-failure` — no MemoryMax=, CPUQuota=, OOMScoreAdjust=. Tier-3 model is 21 GB; if mmap fails and server hits real swap, desktop locks. | I-038 | Medium | MCP schema-pin "rug pull detection" auto-creates pin file on first sight with NO out-of-band verification — TOFU on every fresh install | `mcp_client.SentinelGuard.validate_schema()` (258-278): if pin_file exists and hash differs → reject. On fresh install, every MCP server's schema auto-pinned to whatever server first reports — no "expected hash" check against signed manifest. | I-039 | Medium | `dbus_daemon.on_method_call` (D-Bus Ask handler) bypasses ALL Sentinel/safety scanning of inbound messages — only enforces 4 KB size cap | `dbus_daemon.py:418-470` validates message size only (433). | I-040 | Medium | `analyze_file.py` hardcodes `LLM_ENDPOINT = "http://127.0.0.1:8080/v1/chat/completions"` — escapes LLMRouter config + ignores INTERGEN_* overrides, cloud-escalation routing | `analyze_file.py:28` module-level constant. | I-041 | Low | `_BLOCKED_PATTERNS` in run_command.py defeated by shell-substitution variants — `rm -Rf /`, `rm -fr /`, `\rm -rf /`, base64-decoded | `run_command.py:52` pattern `\brm\s+(-[a-zA-Z]*f[a-zA-Z]*\s+)?/\s*$` (line-anchored) trivially defeated by `rm -rf / # comment`, `rm -rf /*`, `rm -rf "/"`, `\rm -rf /` (backslash escapes alias), `echo cm0gLXJmIC8=\|base64 -d\|sh`. | I-042 | Low | `cli.py daemon` subcommand and CLI direct-ask both bind EventLogger/MemoryManager to disk paths with no opt-out — even `intergen ask --once` writes events.jsonl | Per cli.py:90-96, CLI fallback creates a transient session each ask; each session imports EventLogger and writes routed turn to events log. | I-043 | Low | `Memory.db_path` defaults to `/var/lib/intergen/data/memory.db` (root-owned) — per-user daemon falls back silently with no warning that facts aren't shared/persisted across daemon-fail-and-restart | `dbus_daemon.py:311-312`: `db_path = self._config.get("memory.db_path", "/var/lib/intergen/data/memory.db")`. **Iter-3 cross-check note (Lane I)**: 17 new findings (I-027..I-043). **FIVE NEW HOLY-GRAIL** elevations the prior passes missed: I-027 (SafetyTier.CONFIRM is structurally not enforced anywhere — entire "two-tier safety with user confirmation" model is fiction; this is the keystone Lane-I finding, making I-007/I-022/I-023/I-034/I-035 downstream symptoms of a single architectural absence); I-028 (INTERGEN_* env-var blanket loop accepts ANY config key — strictly worse than I-016 — full LLM-traffic redirection one env-var away); I-029 (safety.py's BLOCKED taxonomy is imported but never invoked — dead code that misleads code reviewers); I-030 (D-Bus session-bus methods have ZERO per-caller authorization — any process in user's session can Ask() the daemon and ride I-027 to arbitrary tool dispatch); I-035 (manage_services auto-`sudo`s on CONFIRM with passwordless wheel-sudo from install lane — structural root-equivalence for the LLM). Voice POWER-RULE re-confirmed CLEAN. No telemetry/phone-home (SERPER_API_KEY only opt-in outbound). Iter-1/2 documented individual symptom rows; iter-3 surfaced the underlying architectural absences that produce them.

**Iter-3 cross-check note (Lane J)**: 14 new findings (J-025..J-038). Heavily weighted toward "what's NOT shipped" — the installer/installed-system path is the consistent gap. **J-025 (High)** is the headline: the three gschema override files defining the curated InterGenOS desktop are copied only by `create-image.sh` for the live ISO; no package ships them, installer never copies them, so every installed system boots into vanilla GNOME 49 with none of the InterGenOS branding/color/dock/banner. This subsumes J-001..J-010's "live-vs-install divergence" theme into a single root cause. **J-026 (High)** locale-binary gap. **J-027 (High)** broken-dock-pin. J-028+J-029 internal contradictions between override files. J-030..J-034 "not shipped" gaps (xdg-user-dirs, mimeapps.list, GDM greeter dconf, extension shell-version validation, portals.conf). J-035..J-038 defaults-not-set for IME, sound theme, accessibility, HiDPI. **Cross-lane signal**: J-025 + J-026 + J-027 collectively mean a freshly installed (vs. live-booted) InterGenOS does NOT match the screenshots/specs — orthogonal-axis regression no Lane D/F/G/I row touches.

## WC findings

### Lane H — pkm end-to-end functionality

_(WC iter-3 complete 2026-05-18 ~03:30 CDT — iter-1 17 + iter-2 4 (H-018..H-021) + iter-3 12 (H-022..H-033) = 33 findings total; iter-3 surfaced 1 Holy-Grail (H-022 tar path-traversal) + 2 Critical (H-023 concurrency-lock, H-024 helper-env-passthrough); exhaustive)_

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| H-001 | High | pkm GPG keyring missing | `pkm/repo.py:74` GPG_KEYRING=/etc/pkm/trusted.gpg; doesn't exist in chroot; pkm update fails | [pkm/repo.py:74](../../pkm/repo.py#L74) | Generated as side effect of signing ceremony; verify exists post-ceremony and during install | **RESOLVED 2026-05-19 via intergenos-keyring package** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). Resolution path: ship /etc/pkm/trusted.gpg + GPG trust anchor + pre-flight verifier integration. | code @ ed4cfa2a |
| H-002 | Holy-Grail | repos.conf format mismatch silently nullifies shipped repo config | `pkm/repo.py:148` parses `/etc/pkm/repos.conf` with `json.load()`, but `packages/core/pkm/build.sh:35-46` writes an INI-style `[intergenos-current]` stanza. On every install the JSONDecodeError is silently caught and the loader falls back to the in-source `DEFAULT_REPOS` dict pointing at `https://repo.intergenos.org/x86_64/current` — a hostname that does not match the actual published mirror at `intergenstudios.com`. Result: ALL pkm fetches go to the wrong URL, every signature check fails closed (no GPG keyring), `pkm update` reports network error, and the user has zero indication that their shipped config was ignored. Cross-ref O-004 and L-004 — same root cause surfaced from three lanes. | [pkm/repo.py:143](../../pkm/repo.py#L143), [packages/core/pkm/build.sh:35](../../packages/core/pkm/build.sh#L35) | Settle on one format. Either parse INI with `configparser` in `_load_repos`, or have build.sh emit JSON. Surface parse errors to stderr instead of swallowing — silent fallback to wrong URL is the Holy-Grail violation. | open | |
| H-003 | Holy-Grail | `--archive-trust=strict` (default) requires reachable repo, breaking offline trust posture | `pkm/cli.py:182-190` rejects every `pkm install --archive PATH` invocation when `repo.get_package(name)` returns nothing or the index is unreachable, because `repo_match` stays False. The shipped repo config is broken (H-002) and even with a working mirror, an air-gapped install of a locally-signed archive cannot succeed without explicitly downgrading to `--archive-trust=loose`. The strict mode in effect tells users "trust requires the network," which inverts the local-first / offline-capable posture. `--archive-trust=loose` only prints a warning — there's no path to "trust this archive because I verified it via independent channel" short of swapping trust modes. | [pkm/cli.py:169](../../pkm/cli.py#L169), [pkm/cli.py:187](../../pkm/cli.py#L187) | Add a third trust mode `manifest` that verifies against a co-located `.sha256` or `.sig` file alongside the archive, or accept signed BSD-manifest verification (matches `installer/backend/integrity.py`). Document that strict requires repo sync; default to loose+warning when no repo configured. | open | |
| H-004 | Critical | installer never records package dependencies → reverse-dep safety check is dead | `pkm/installer.py` calls `add_installed` + `add_files` + `log_operation` but NEVER calls `db.add_depends()`. The `depends` table exists in the schema (`pkm/database.py:76-82`) and `add_depends()` is implemented (line 363), but no code path in the install flow invokes it. Consequences: (1) `pkm depends <pkg>` always returns "no tracked dependencies"; (2) `pkm info` "Dependencies" section is always empty; (3) `pkm remove`'s reverse-dependency safety check at `remover.py:31-37` never trips, meaning users can `pkm remove glibc` without `--force` and silently destroy their system; (4) `pkm depends --reverse` always returns "no packages depend on it"; (5) `cli.cmd_install` repo-fetch path calls `repo.resolve_dependencies()` which produces a correct install ORDER but the resolved deps are never persisted. | [pkm/installer.py:196](../../pkm/installer.py#L196), [pkm/database.py:363](../../pkm/database.py#L363), [pkm/remover.py:30](../../pkm/remover.py#L30) | In installer.install(), parse `depends:` from `pkg.get("depends", [])` (when repo-sourced) or from a DEPENDS header in the staged manifest (when archive-sourced), then call `self.db.add_depends(pkg_id, [(d, "runtime") for d in deps], commit=False)` inside the atomic transaction at line 218. | open | |
| H-005 | High | smoke-test invokes non-existent `pkm query` subcommand | `installer/smoke/checks/pkm.sh:39` runs `pkm query "$marker"` and treats non-zero exit as missing marker. The pkm CLI has no `query` subcommand (only install/install-helper/remove/list/update/upgrade/search/info/files/provides/verify/depends/history/import per `pkm/cli.py:22-95`). Every fresh install will report `FAIL pkm/query: marker package 'glibc-core' not in DB — install incomplete?` even on a fully successful install. The closest equivalent is `pkm info glibc-core` or `pkm list installed`. | [installer/smoke/checks/pkm.sh:37](../../installer/smoke/checks/pkm.sh#L37), [pkm/cli.py:22](../../pkm/cli.py#L22) | Either rename the smoke check to `pkm info` (returns 0 when installed) or add a `query` alias subcommand in cli.py that wraps `cmd_info`. | open | |
| H-006 | High | `pkm verify` with no args and no `--all` returns exit 0 — masks integrity failures in smoke test | `pkm/cli.py:448-451`: when neither `--all` nor a package name is supplied, the command prints `Usage: ...` and returns. The default exit code is 0. The smoke check (`installer/smoke/checks/pkm.sh:27`) runs `pkm verify --fast` with no positional arg; rc=0 always lands the case-0 PASS branch. A corrupted package on disk would never be reported by the smoke test. | [pkm/cli.py:448](../../pkm/cli.py#L448), [installer/smoke/checks/pkm.sh:25](../../installer/smoke/checks/pkm.sh#L25) | Make bare `pkm verify` (no args, no --all) implicitly mean `--all` (matches user intent), OR exit 2 when invoked without an argument. Update smoke-test to pass `--all`. | open | |
| H-007 | High | install helper path never registers files or dependencies | `pkm/installer.py:430-456` (`_run_helper`) calls `add_installed()` and `log_operation()` but NEVER calls `add_files()` or `add_depends()`. Helpers (chrome, vscode, edge, brave, discord, spotify, claude-code) deposit files into `/opt/google/chrome`, `/usr/bin/google-chrome` etc, but pkm has zero record of those files. Consequences: (1) `pkm files chrome` returns "no tracked files"; (2) `pkm verify chrome` reports `total: 0 OK` even when chrome has been deleted; (3) `pkm remove chrome` does NOT remove the files — only the DB row, leaving orphaned binaries in `/opt`; (4) `pkm provides /usr/bin/google-chrome` returns no owner. Helper installs are effectively untracked, defeating the whole purpose of the package manager for the extra-tier. | [pkm/installer.py:446](../../pkm/installer.py#L446), [packages/extra/chrome-helper/build.sh:23](../../packages/extra/chrome-helper/build.sh#L23) | Helpers should write a manifest-style listing of installed files to a known path (e.g., `/var/lib/igos/helpers/<name>.files`); pkm reads it on success and calls `add_files()` to register them. Alternative: helpers emit a JSON manifest to stdout that pkm captures. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-19 via ffmpeg-nonfree-helper migration** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). Resolution path: P-015 ffmpeg redistributable default + fdk-aac dep drop + opt-in helper package. | code @ 5aa2f95c |
| H-008 | High | installer never populates tier/description/license/build_date metadata | `pkm/installer.py:198-201` calls `add_installed()` with only name + version + install_method + archive_path. The schema columns `tier`, `description`, `license`, `build_date` (`pkm/database.py:45-62`) are always NULL post-install. Consequences: (1) `pkm info <pkg>` shows no tier/description/license; (2) `pkm list --tier core` filter returns ZERO packages because the tier column is NULL for everything; (3) `pkm search <term>` against description is dead because description is NULL. The data exists in `package.yml` and the repo index JSON but is dropped on the floor. | [pkm/installer.py:196](../../pkm/installer.py#L196), [pkm/database.py:177](../../pkm/database.py#L177) | When repo-sourced, populate from `pkg.get("tier"/"description"/"license"/"build_date")`. When archive-sourced, parse `.PKGINFO` from the archive (the function `_parse_pkginfo` already exists in `pkm/repo.py:519`) and pass into `add_installed`. | open | |
| H-009 | High | database.py line 246 uses `sys.stderr` without importing sys | `pkm/database.py:246` is `print(f"  WARNING: ...", file=sys.stderr)` but the module has no `import sys` (verified: `sys` does not appear in the module's imports at lines 7-12). | H-022 | Holy-Grail | tar extraction uses subprocess `tar` with no path-traversal protection — archive with `../` member escapes staging | `pkm/installer.py:101-105` extracts archives via `subprocess.run(["tar", "-xzf", ...])` to staging, then again at lines 160-165 to `self.root` (the live filesystem). GNU tar does not reject `../` members by default. `--no-same-owner` / `--no-same-permissions` flags address ownership but not traversal. A malicious or corrupted `.igos.tar.gz` (e.g., attacker who bypasses sig verification via H-002/L-015, or any `--archive-trust=loose` install) writes arbitrary files OUTSIDE staging and OUTSIDE self.root. Supersedes file-list audit at lines 116-123 walks staging and sees nothing of escaped files, so they go unrecorded in the DB and remain post-install. Iter-1/2 audited supersede transaction + sig flow but did not audit the extraction primitive itself. Python 3.12+ added `tarfile.data_filter` precisely to close this — pkm shells out instead, bypassing the protection. | [pkm/installer.py:101](../../pkm/installer.py#L101), [pkm/installer.py:160](../../pkm/installer.py#L160) | Switch to `tarfile.open(...).extractall(path=..., filter="data")` (Python 3.14 hardened filter). At minimum add `--anchored --no-wildcards-match-slash` to tar argv + pre-scan archive to reject members matching `^/` or containing `/../`. Reject symlink members whose target escapes install root. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW (Holy-Grail) |
| H-023 | Critical | No process-level lock — concurrent `pkm install` invocations race on SQLite WAL + filesystem deploy | `pkm/database.py:120-126` opens SQLite with `journal_mode=WAL` but takes no advisory lock on `/var/lock/pkm.lock`. Two simultaneous `pkm install pkgA` + `pkm install pkgB` invocations (e.g., user in two terminals, or systemd-timer auto-update racing with interactive use) each open their own connection, BEGIN their own transaction, and tar-extract into self.root concurrently. SQLite WAL handles DB-level concurrency safely — but BEGIN at installer.py:196 is held during DB-write phase, NOT during FS deploy at lines 160-165. Two installs with overlapping files interleave at FS level with no coordination, then both attempt to register the same path; second's add_files silently transfers ownership via INSERT OR REPLACE. Supersedes invariant breaks. Iter-1/2 audited single-thread atomicity but not multi-process concurrency. | [pkm/database.py:123](../../pkm/database.py#L123), [pkm/installer.py:196](../../pkm/installer.py#L196), [pkm/cli.py:101](../../pkm/cli.py#L101) | Acquire `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` on `/var/lock/pkm.lock` at top of cmd_install/cmd_remove/cmd_upgrade/cmd_install_helper before opening DB. Document pkm is single-writer per-system. Add busy-wait with `pkm is already running (pid X) — retry in a moment` message. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| H-024 | Critical | Helper installer runs with FULL inherited environment — PATH/LD_PRELOAD/proxy injection lets malicious shell env compromise root install | `pkm/installer.py:439-442` runs helpers via `subprocess.run([str(helper_path)], env=os.environ.copy())`. Helpers like `igos-install-chrome` do `wget`, `cp`, `ln` as root because user ran `sudo pkm install-helper chrome`. Full env inherited including PATH, LD_PRELOAD, LD_LIBRARY_PATH, http_proxy, https_proxy, HTTPS_PROXY, GNUPGHOME. Attacker who controls non-root user env then convinces user to `sudo -E pkm install-helper chrome` (or via sudoers rules preserving env) can: (a) inject PATH=/tmp/evil-bin:$PATH so helper's wget/tar/cp calls go to attacker binaries running as root; (b) inject https_proxy to MITM the Google download (helpers use wget -q with no cert pinning); (c) inject LD_PRELOAD=/tmp/evil.so to compromise every subprocess. Combined with H-007 (helpers register nothing in DB), malicious helper-spawned process has free reign and pkm has zero record. | [pkm/installer.py:441](../../pkm/installer.py#L441), [packages/extra/chrome-helper/build.sh:51](../../packages/extra/chrome-helper/build.sh#L51) | Strip env to minimal allowlist (PATH=/usr/bin:/bin, HOME=/root, LANG, TERM) before spawning. Drop LD_PRELOAD/LD_LIBRARY_PATH/all `*_proxy` vars unconditionally. Use `subprocess.run([helper_path], env={...})` with explicit dict. Pin TLS roots in `wget` calls inside helpers (`--ca-certificate=`). | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| H-025 | High | `_download` has no retry, no resume, no Content-Length check — single TCP RST loses entire install batch | `pkm/repo.py:221-228` is one-shot `urllib.request.urlopen(...timeout=30)` + `shutil.copyfileobj`. No retry on transient errors (connection reset, 503, EAGAIN, slow-mirror partial read). No Range resume. No Content-Length validation (server closing mid-stream produces truncated file that fails SHA256 on next round, costing entire batch). 30-second timeout is per-connection-attempt, not per-byte — stalled mirror (Cloudflare 524 patterns) keeps connection open with no data, timeout never fires until kernel keepalive expires (~2hr default). For real upgrade run downloading 50+ archives, single mirror hiccup aborts entire `cmd_upgrade` loop with no recovery state. Iter-1/2's H-019 caught no-rollback issue but not underlying download fragility that causes the rollback gap to matter. | [pkm/repo.py:221](../../pkm/repo.py#L221), [pkm/cli.py:313](../../pkm/cli.py#L313) | Wrap `_download` in retry-with-backoff (3 attempts, exponential, jitter). Add Content-Length validation pre/post-copy. Add per-byte read timeout via socket.setdefaulttimeout + socket-level keepalive. Implement resume via Range header when partial file present + `.part` extension convention. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| H-026 | High | Recursive dependency cycle hits Python recursion limit silently — no cycle detection | `pkm/repo.py:381-405` does plain recursion via inner `resolve(pkg_name)` with `visited` set. `visited` prevents re-visiting a name but NOT cycle detection — A→B→A returns early because A is in visited. Works for direct 2-cycles. BUT: A→B→C→A early-return — Python stack consumed but no error. For pathological inputs (attacker-crafted index with deeply-nested cycles, or genuine bug where dep arrays generated by upstream tools point at themselves through chains of 1000+ names), this hits `RecursionError`. Worse: cycle still RESOLVES SUCCESSFULLY because visited absorbs the loop — but with WRONG install order (P appears in `to_install` BEFORE its actual transitive deps if those deps closed a cycle and were skipped at append-time). | [pkm/repo.py:385](../../pkm/repo.py#L385), [pkm/repo.py:399](../../pkm/repo.py#L399) | Add explicit cycle detection: track `in_progress` set; if name re-enters while still in_progress, raise `DependencyCycleError(chain)`. | H-027 | High | No `Ctrl-C` / SIGINT handling — KeyboardInterrupt mid-deploy leaves staging + half-extracted root + uncommitted SQLite transaction | `pkm/installer.py:95-241` uses `tempfile.mkdtemp` in try/finally with `shutil.rmtree(staging, ignore_errors=True)` — but try/finally catches `Exception`, not `BaseException`. KeyboardInterrupt inherits BaseException, so SIGINT triggers finally — good for tmpdir cleanup. HOWEVER: if SIGINT lands between line 160 (`tar -xzf ... -C self.root`) and line 196 (`db.conn.execute("BEGIN")`), live root has been written but no DB transaction was opened. ### Lane K — Documentation drift

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

| K-026 | Medium | getting-started.md presents install path as TUI-only; init.sh routes to install-gui OR install-tui as parallel first-class modes | docs/getting-started.md:47 — "The system will boot into the **Forge Installer** TUI (Text User Interface)." ### Lane L — Repository / mirror state

_(WC iter-3 complete 2026-05-18 ~03:30 CDT — iter-1 14 (1 FP L-014) + iter-2 4 (L-015..L-018) + iter-3 14 (L-019..L-032) = 31 net findings; iter-3 surfaced 2 Holy-Grail (L-019 anti-rollback / replay attack, L-020 schema-version-refusal absent) + 2 Critical (L-021 TOCTOU verify-vs-extract, L-022 disaster-recovery gap) + 5 High; exhaustive)_

**Mirror-sweep 2026-05-18 close-out** (build-system coordinator, post-walk item 2.5). The following Lane L findings are RESOLVED by the corrective sweep at commit `<sweep-commit>` (see commit body): **L-003** (was "no DNS record for repo.intergenos.org" — DNS live since 2026-05-11; scan-memory-first failure on the audit side); **L-004** (`packages/core/pkm/build.sh:42-44` URL fixed to `repo.intergenos.org`); **L-005** (`mirror-publish.sh` deleted; `publish-repo.sh` confirmed canonical and matches ratified VPS state); **L-006** (Apache snippet was for the rejected hostname — `repo.intergenos.org` has its own cPanel subdomain vhost; snippet deleted as moot); **L-002** (master-fingerprint hardcoding in `mirror-publish.sh:23` + `design.md:147` removed via deletion + rewrite — design.md now describes the subkey-on-NK topology correctly); **L-009** (atomic-promote conflict — rewritten `design.md` aligns with `publish-repo.sh`'s symlink-swap); **L-011** (`docs/architecture/public-hosting-plan.md` and `docs/architecture/reproducible-builds-design.md` were correct all along — the conflict was on the `design.md` side, now resolved). **K-012** (mirror design master-ref staleness) also RESOLVED by rewrite. The hostname was ratified DAY-0 (operator-direct, 2026-05-11); `intergenos.org` registrar-locked 5 years; infrastructure (DNS + LE R12 cert + SSH + docroot) live since 2026-05-11. The audit findings that flagged the hostname as "unknown/conflicted" reflected scan-memory-first failures rather than real ambiguity — the corrective sweep brings the docs/scripts into alignment with the ratified state rather than re-deciding it.

| L-001 | Holy-Grail | Signed-mirror story is theatre — zero packages have been signed or published | The "signed end-to-end mirror" narrative permeates user-facing docs (security-defaults.md:43, package-management.md:8, getting-started.md:63, repository-trust.md:11, README.md:149/161, VISION.md:296, CHANGELOG.md:22) yet there is no evidence in the repo or commit history that ANY package has ever been signed and published. No `InterGenOS.db*` artifact exists anywhere in tree, no `*.igos.tar.gz` or `*.sig` exists, no commit mentions a first-publish event having occurred. `docs/operational/first-publish-runbook.md:4` states verbatim "The procedure described here has never been exercised end-to-end." User-facing docs nonetheless market the mirror as operational. Violates Holy Grail rule #1 (no security trade-offs for convenience) and rule #9 (update infrastructure must be trustworthy — claiming a trustworthy mirror exists when none does is a credibility-loss-on-day-one trap). Cross-ref P-001. | [docs/users/security-defaults.md:43](../../docs/users/security-defaults.md#L43), [README.md:161](../../README.md#L161), [docs/operational/first-publish-runbook.md:4](../../docs/operational/first-publish-runbook.md#L4) | Either (a) gate every "signed mirror" claim behind a "post first-publish" banner identical to first-publish-runbook.md's status line, or (b) execute the first publish before next ISO ships. | L-002 | Holy-Grail | mirror-publish.sh signs with the OFFLINE MASTER fingerprint instead of a signing subkey | `scripts/mirror-publish.sh:23` hardcodes `GPG_KEY_FP=5597A3E0587B253006D0DD7B8C50826182083050` as the default `--local-user` for `gpg --detach-sign` at line 139-142. That fingerprint is the **master key** (per `docs/signing-key.md:18`), which lives offline on Drive #3 in a fireproof safe (per `docs/shim-review-submission.md:433`). Per the signing-key.md hierarchy table line 92-97, the master "Certifies the signing subkeys, signs rollover announcements" — **it is not supposed to sign release artifacts**. The signing subkeys [S1]/[S2]/[S3]/[S4] (D7AA641D... etc., on Nitrokey hardware) are what sign indexes. The companion `docs/mirror/design.md:147` repeats the same wrong fingerprint and §3 line 91 calls it the "master pubkey" inside the trust chain — design conflates the master with the on-card signing subkey. By contrast `scripts/publish-repo.sh:33-36` and `pkm/release-keys.json` correctly use D7AA641D/81DD223F. Operationally: running mirror-publish.sh as written would either fail (master key not on the NK#1 PIV slot 9c — that slot holds the EFI X.509 cert, not the GPG master) or, worse, require exhuming the offline master to satisfy the script — collapsing the offline-root posture. | [scripts/mirror-publish.sh:23](../../scripts/mirror-publish.sh#L23), [scripts/mirror-publish.sh:139](../../scripts/mirror-publish.sh#L139), [docs/mirror/design.md:147](../../docs/mirror/design.md#L147), [docs/signing-key.md:20](../../docs/signing-key.md#L20) | Change mirror-publish.sh default GPG_KEY_FP to the [S1] subkey fingerprint `D7AA641D81ACD690C5AD865E7276E14DD8886BFE` (matches publish-repo.sh + release-keys.json); update design.md §3 trust-model + §4 step 3 to reflect subkey-on-NK signing flow, not master-key signing; mirror-publish.sh:149 should also document the touch-policy on the NK signing slot (not PIV slot 9c, which is X.509 for EFI binaries). | open | |
| L-003 | Critical | `pkm/repo.py` default URL points at a non-existent host | `pkm/repo.py:78` ships `https://repo.intergenos.org/x86_64/current` as the `DEFAULT_REPOS` URL. A fresh install whose `/etc/pkm/repos.conf` is absent or unreadable falls through to this default and `pkm sync` immediately fails on DNS resolution. | L-009 | Medium | Mirror-design conflict between symlink-swap (publish-repo.sh) and directory-rename (mirror-publish.sh) | publish-repo.sh:166-175 promotes via `ln -sfn` + `mv -T` (rename-the-symlink pattern); mirror-publish.sh promote command (lines 179-188) renames the directory itself (`mv current _previous/...` then `mv staging/x86_64 current`). design.md:67-72 explicitly argues against symlink-swap ("the swap window can race with mid-request reads on Apache + sendfile"). The two scripts therefore embody mutually-incompatible promote contracts; whichever script ran last on a given mirror determines whether `current/` is a symlink or a directory, and the other script will misbehave on the next run (publish-repo.sh's `readlink -f LIVE/current` returns the dir path, then `ln -sfn` replaces a directory with a symlink — recoverable but messy). | [scripts/publish-repo.sh:172-175](../../scripts/publish-repo.sh#L172), [scripts/mirror-publish.sh:181-188](../../scripts/mirror-publish.sh#L181), [docs/mirror/design.md:67](../../docs/mirror/design.md#L67) | Tied to L-005 (one canonical workflow); whichever survives carries the canonical promote-shape. | L-015 | Holy-Grail | Shipped `/etc/pkm/repos.conf` is INI-format but `pkm/repo.py` parses it as JSON — every shipped install silently falls through to DEFAULT_REPOS | `pkm/repo.py:143-151` `_load_repos()` does `json.load(f)` on `/etc/pkm/repos.conf`. The shipped file at `packages/core/pkm/build.sh:35-46` is INI (`[intergenos-current]\nurl = ...`). On every install, the JSON parser raises `JSONDecodeError`, bare `except (json.JSONDecodeError, OSError): pass` swallows it, falls through to `DEFAULT_REPOS` (the `repo.intergenos.org` URL — see L-003). User has **no working override path**: any custom `/etc/pkm/repos.conf` in the documented INI format is also silently ignored. Holy-Grail because (a) removes user control over mirror configuration without any visible signal — Prime Directive violation; (b) the only effective config path is the hardcoded DEFAULT_REPOS URL (L-003); even L-003/L-004 dual-fix only fixes half — the INI parser must also exist before the shipped INI file is honored. Makes L-004 effectively a no-op at runtime (shipped wrong URL is ignored), which is *worse* — broken config silently goes away while broken default takes over. **This finding upshifts L-004 to Holy-Grail at synthesis.** Cross-ref H-002 / O-004. | [pkm/repo.py:143-151](../../pkm/repo.py#L143), [packages/core/pkm/build.sh:42-46](../../packages/core/pkm/build.sh#L42) | Either (a) implement INI parser in `_load_repos()` matching shipped format + design.md §6 spec, OR (b) change the shipped file to JSON matching DEFAULT_REPOS shape. Option (a) is design.md-aligned. Add `pkm config check` subcommand that loud-fails when /etc/pkm/repos.conf exists but cannot be parsed (instead of silent fallthrough). | open | iter-2 @ b3eb6318: NEW (Holy-Grail) |
| L-016 | High | Mirror layout incompatible between runbook (`/packages/<pkg>`) and pkm client (flat `/<filename>`) | `docs/operational/first-publish-runbook.md:79-93` specifies mirror layout as `/x86_64/InterGenOS.db` + `/x86_64/packages/<pkg>-<version>.igos.tar.gz` (nested packages/ subdir). `pkm/repo.py:327-328` `download_package()` constructs URL as `{repo_url}/{filename}` where filename is bare basename (line 449: `meta["filename"] = pkg_file.name`). | L-019 | Holy-Grail | No anti-rollback / freshness check on signed index — replay attack lets attacker pin clients to an old vulnerable snapshot | `pkm/repo.py:99` reads `generated` from index but never compares it against a previously-seen value. `_ensure_synced()` at line 288-309 trusts whatever cached index is on disk after re-verifying the signature only. An attacker who intercepts TLS (or controls a malicious mirror operator running the documented "preserve exact directory structure" instruction from docs/repository-trust.md:62-67) can serve a previously-validly-signed *old* InterGenOS.db containing known-vulnerable package versions — signature is genuine, SHA256s are genuine, but user gets outdated stack with CVEs. Standard mitigation in apt/dnf is "Valid-Until" headers + monotonic-timestamp pinning in local state. Neither exists. INDEX_MAX_AGE = 3600 at pkm/repo.py:85 is defined but never referenced. Holy-Grail because (a) attacker needs no key compromise, (b) trust chain reports "Good signature" the whole time hiding the downgrade, (c) violates Rule #1. | [pkm/repo.py:85](../../pkm/repo.py#L85), [pkm/repo.py:99](../../pkm/repo.py#L99), [pkm/repo.py:288-309](../../pkm/repo.py#L288), [docs/repository-trust.md:62-67](../../docs/repository-trust.md#L62) | Persist `last_seen_generated` per-repo in `/var/lib/pkm/state/<repo>.json` after first successful sync. On every subsequent sync, parse new index's `generated` field BEFORE accepting it; refuse-with-loud-error if new timestamp is older than last-seen value. Wire INDEX_MAX_AGE to actually reject indexes older than 1h (or 7-day window with warn-after-3-day soft alert). Add separate signed `Valid-Until` field. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| L-020 | Holy-Grail | Index `version` field silently accepted at any value — no schema-version refusal protects against malicious schema downgrade or future-format misparse | `pkm/repo.py:98` uses `data.get("version", 1)` with NO check that version is in supported range. If server-side schema bumps to v2 (e.g., adds `min_client_version` or restructures `packages` dict), older v1 clients silently misparse. Worse: attacker with mirror-write access (or compromised signing key during 12h revocation window per SECURITY.md:69) can publish `version: 1` indexes that lie about package metadata to clients running newer schema-aware code. There's no `min_client_version`, `schema_version`, or `signed_max_supported_client` field. Sig-algorithm-agility: trust chain is hardwired to GPG-detached-armored sigs with no negotiated `signature_format` field — migrating to sigstore/ed25519/cosign requires bumping schema, but schema has no opt-out path that lets old clients fail-closed instead of misparse. Holy-Grail because it eliminates chain's ability to safely evolve under attacker pressure. | [pkm/repo.py:98](../../pkm/repo.py#L98), [pkm/repo.py:230](../../pkm/repo.py#L230), [pkm/repo.py:455](../../pkm/repo.py#L455), [scripts/generate-repodb.py:109](../../scripts/generate-repodb.py#L109) | Add `if data.get("version") not in {1}: raise IndexFormatError(...)` to _parse_index. | L-021 | Critical | TOCTOU between SHA256 verify and tar extract — archive in `/var/cache/pkm/packages/` can be swapped between verify and read | `pkm/repo.py:313-350` `download_package()` verifies SHA256 immediately after download and returns the path. `pkm/cli.py:213-218` passes that path to `installer.install(dep_name, archive_path=dl_result)`. `pkm/installer.py:101-105` opens file via `subprocess.run(["tar", ...])` for staging extract, AGAIN at line 160-164 for deploy. Between SHA256 verify (in download_package) and FIRST tar read (in installer), and between FIRST and SECOND tar reads, file is on disk. No re-verification at either gate. Local attacker with write access to /var/cache/pkm/ (or race between concurrent pkm install calls — sqlite locking prevents concurrent DB ops but not concurrent cache writes) can swap archive AFTER verify but BEFORE extract. Two tar reads happen sequentially and read file twice — second read could be tampered version even if first was clean. | [pkm/repo.py:313-350](../../pkm/repo.py#L313), [pkm/cli.py:213-218](../../pkm/cli.py#L213), [pkm/installer.py:101-105](../../pkm/installer.py#L101), [pkm/installer.py:160-164](../../pkm/installer.py#L160) | Re-hash archive once inside installer.install AFTER opening but BEFORE either tar extract; pass expected SHA256 through from cmd_install to installer.install. | L-022 | Critical | No disaster-recovery story for VPS-side artifacts — if origin.intergenstudios.com loses disk, the signed index + ALL `_previous/` snapshots vanish together | Mirror layout at `docs/mirror/design.md:50-64` puts `current/`, `_staging-*/`, AND `_previous/` snapshots all under SAME `/home/intergen/public_html/mirror/x86_64/`. ### Lane N — Disk / partitioning capabilities

_(WC iter-3 complete 2026-05-18 ~03:30 CDT — iter-1 8 + iter-2 2 (N-009..N-010) + iter-3 9 (N-011..N-019) = 19 findings total; iter-3 surfaced 4 High (N-011 fstab drift, N-012 no min-disk-size, N-013 USB-media not excluded, N-014 no partition rollback); exhaustive)_

**Supported-shape inventory:**
- Fresh-wipe-only (single disk, full erase): yes — `disks.partition_disk()` at [disks.py:121-159](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L121); wired in UI + orchestrator
- Alongside-Windows (preserve ESP, dual-boot): half — backend primitives present (`detect_existing_esp`, `detect_shrinkable_ntfs`, `is_bitlocker_encrypted`, `shrink_ntfs`, `partition_disk_alongside`) at [disks.py:162-337](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L162), but NO frontend wiring — `state.target_disk` is the only disk variable, no mode toggle; orchestrator hard-codes `partition_disk()` at [install.py:343](../../installer/backend/install.py#L343)
- Manual partition (user-chosen layout): no — only `target_disk` (whole-disk path) is captured; no per-partition assignment surface anywhere
- LUKS encryption: no — zero references in installer/* (only mentioned in research docs as future + in signing_key_custody for offline-USB key backup)
- LVM: no — zero references in installer/*; no lvm tools in initramfs build list
- BTRFS: no — `partition_disk()` hard-codes `mkfs.ext4`; GRUB module list includes `btrfs` (incidental, dual-boot detection) but no installer path creates a btrfs root
- ZFS: no — same as BTRFS; GRUB modules list `zfs zfscrypt zfsinfo` (dual-boot detection only)
- Multi-disk (e.g., /boot on disk A, / on disk B): no — single `target_disk` field, single-disk partition map dict
- RAID / mdadm: no — zero references anywhere in installer/* or scripts/*
- Dedicated /home partition: no — `generate_fstab()` at [config.py:8-36](../../installer/backend/config.py#L8) writes ONLY root + ESP entries
- Swap partition / zram: no — `partition_disk()` creates no swap; `generate_fstab()` writes no swap line; no zram-generator config; no swap reference anywhere in installer/*
- Custom mount points: no — fstab generation is hard-coded to / + /boot/efi only

| N-003 | Medium | No swap partition / zram support — fresh-install boots with zero swap, ever | `partition_disk()` creates ESP + root only. `generate_fstab()` writes ESP + root only. | N-005 | Medium | Disk-screen filter excludes ALL disks containing `/` mount — false negatives on bind-mount / containers / nested chroot | `detect_disks()` at [disks.py:110-114](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L110) excludes any disk containing a partition mounted at "/". Intended: filter the live media. Actual: any partition mounted at "/" — including a bind mount, a chroot whose `/` is being scanned, or a Docker overlay — eliminates the parent disk. | N-009 | Medium | partition_disk() wired path lacks partprobe + udevadm settle between parted and mkfs — race against /dev/ node appearance | Fresh-wipe path at [disks.py:121-159](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L121) creates partitions via `parted mkpart` then immediately calls `mkfs.fat`/`mkfs.ext4` against derived /dev/<disk><n> paths. On real hardware kernel needs to re-read partition table + udev needs to create device nodes before mkfs tools can open them; without `partprobe` + `udevadm settle` between mkpart and mkfs, format calls can fail with "no such file or directory" or "device busy" on slow-enumerating hardware (NVMe, USB, virtio under load). Counter-example same file: `partition_disk_alongside()` at [disks.py:318-319](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L318) correctly calls `partprobe` + `udevadm settle` after its mkpart for exactly this reason ("Without these, detect_disks() can race against the new partition's /dev/ node appearing"). Wired path is missing same guard. Risk: install failures partway through partition phase on hardware exhibiting race. Reproducibility: hard (timing-dependent). | [disks.py:121-159](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L121) vs [disks.py:318-319](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L318) | After both `parted mkpart` invocations in `partition_disk()` (lines 138 EFI and 153 BIOS), insert `_run(f"partprobe {disk_path}")` followed by `_run("udevadm settle")` before `_partition_paths()` + `mkfs.*` calls. Mirror the comment from partition_disk_alongside explaining the race. | open | iter-2 @ b3eb6318: NEW |
| N-010 | Low | partition_disk() lacks pre-wipe unmount + swapoff — wipefs -a will fail if any partition on target disk is mounted | `partition_disk()` at [disks.py:131](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L131) calls `wipefs -a $disk_path` to clear existing partition table, but does not first unmount any currently-mounted partitions on that disk or swapoff any active swap partitions. `wipefs -a` will refuse to clear a disk with mounted children, returning a partial-failure exit code that surfaces as a generic "Command failed" from `_run`. Disk-screen filter at [disks.py:109-114](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L109) excludes only disks whose partition is mounted at exactly "/" — a secondary disk with /data, /backup, etc. mounted will pass the filter, then fail at wipefs step. UX-degraded; not destructive (wipefs refuses safely). | [disks.py:121-131](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L121) | Before wipefs, iterate disk.partitions and run `umount` on each .mountpoint that is non-empty, plus `swapoff` on each partition whose fstype == "swap". Sibling to N-005/C-012 — those filter problems, this is consequence of a slip-through. | open | iter-2 @ b3eb6318: NEW |

| N-011 | High | install-time and image-time fstab generators drift on mount options + swap — two paths produce two different running systems | `installer/backend/config.py:generate_fstab` writes root with `defaults` (no noatime/discard/commit interval) and ESP with `umask=0077`. `scripts/create-image.sh:155-160` writes root with `defaults,noatime` and ESP with `fmask=0077,dmask=0077`. | N-014 | High | No partition-table rollback when PHASE_PARTITION fails partway — disk left in unknown state | `install.py:344-345` runs `partition_disk()` then immediately advances `phase_completed = PHASE_PARTITION`. If `partition_disk()` raises (any mkfs/parted step at lines 131-157 of disks.py), the disk has been wipefs'd + partially repartitioned + partially mkfs'd, and orchestrator catch-block at install.py:560-574 only attempts `unmount_target` (nothing to unmount — mount happens in next phase). | N-015 | Medium | `_get_uuid` blkid call does not force fresh probe — UUID can be cached-stale immediately after mkfs | `config.py:185-191` calls `blkid -s UUID -o value <device>` to read UUID for fstab + grub-default generation. blkid maintains cache at `/run/blkid/blkid.tab` keyed by device path; a partition that previously held a different filesystem can return OLD uuid on first-call after `mkfs.ext4` if udev hasn't re-fired blkid yet. On real hardware lag is millisecond-scale but observable; on slow virtio/USB window opens to seconds. Result: fstab points at UUID that doesn't exist on disk → next boot drops to emergency shell with "can't find root by UUID". Reproducibility: rare on first install (no prior FS), routine on re-install over existing InterGenOS. | [config.py:185-191](../../installer/backend/config.py#L185), [install.py:343-403](../../installer/backend/install.py#L343) | Either (a) call `blkid -g` (garbage-collect cache) before each _get_uuid, or (b) use `blkid -p -s UUID -o value <device>` which probes directly bypassing cache. Option (b) is cleanest — works with no privileged side-effects. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| N-016 | Medium | `mkfs.ext4` uses default options — no SSD-aware tuning, no reserved-space adjustment, no discard | `partition_disk()` calls `mkfs.ext4 -L intergenos <part>` with only label flag. Defaults: 5% reserved-space for root (~5GB on 100GB disk — meaningful on small SSDs), no `-E discard` (no TRIM-during-format, wastes ~30s on large SSDs), no `-T` workload tuning. For desktop install: `-m 1` (1% reserved), `-E discard` (issues TRIM during format on SSDs). Image-time path (create-image.sh:123) has SAME minimal invocation — drift NOT present here, both paths equally underspecified. | [disks.py:145,157](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L145), [create-image.sh:123](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L123) | Define `MKFS_EXT4_OPTS = ["-m", "1", "-E", "discard,lazy_itable_init=0,lazy_journal_init=0"]` in disks.py and apply in both wired paths. lazy_itable_init=0 is important — defers full disk write at install time without it. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| N-017 | Medium | No fstrim.timer enabled — SSD performance degrades over months with no periodic discard | No fstrim.timer/service shipped or enabled anywhere. util-linux ships fstrim binary; .timer unit is part of util-linux upstream but not enabled by users.enable_services() (install.py:464) or by create-image.sh service-enable block (lines 528-549). Result: InterGenOS SSD install over 6-12 months accumulates dead blocks SSD firmware can't reclaim, write performance drops 30-50%. Affects every installed system on flash storage. Compounds with N-016. | [install.py:462-466](../../installer/backend/install.py#L462), [create-image.sh:528-549](../../scripts/create-image.sh#L528) | Add `systemctl enable fstrim.timer` to users.enable_services (installer) and to create-image.sh service-enable block. | N-018 | Medium | Zero encryption-at-rest story documented or stubbed — Holy Grail-adjacent gap | N-001 noted "LUKS encryption: no — zero references in installer/*". Holy Grail explicitly calls out "Credential handling is sacred — GNOME Keyring, never plaintext" (rule 8), which presupposes user's data at rest is not trivially extractable via dd off stolen laptop. Don't ship without addressing the question. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| N-019 | Low | `_split_partition_path` uses `rfind("p")` for nvme/mmcblk — incorrect on future device-mapper paths | disks.py:438-446 and bootloader.py:237-254 both implement disk/partition splitting. For `/dev/nvme0n1p3` → rfind("p") returns index of second "p" (correct). But for `/dev/mapper/cryptpool-root` (LUKS-mapped — N-018 future) or `/dev/loop0p1` (loop device with partitions), rfind("p") finds wrong "p". `/dev/mapper/...` never matches nvme/mmcblk branch so falls through to digit-strip path which ALSO fails on `-root` suffix. Currently unreachable (no LVM/LUKS/loop wired), but a footgun for any future device-mapper layer. | [disks.py:438-446](../../installer/backend/disks.py#L438), [bootloader.py:237-254](../../installer/backend/bootloader.py#L237) | Replace ad-hoc split with `lsblk --noheadings --raw -o PKNAME <part>` parent-lookup or `udevadm info --query=property --name=<part>`.
