### Lane O — Update mechanism

_(WC iter-3 complete 2026-05-18 ~03:30 CDT — iter-1 18 + iter-2 4 (O-019..O-022) + iter-3 13 (O-023..O-035) = 35 findings total; iter-3 surfaced 1 Critical (O-027 mass-upgrade silent-default — compounds with O-002+O-007) + 7 High; exhaustive)_

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| O-001 | Critical | `pkm reinstall` referenced but does not exist | `installer.py:71` returns error "Use 'pkm reinstall' to replace" when a package is already installed; `installer.py:76` recommends `pkm reinstall <name>` to revert a supersede. Neither path exists in `cli.py` (no `sub.add_parser("reinstall", ...)`, no `cmd_reinstall`). User following the printed instruction hits argparse "invalid choice: 'reinstall'". Re-installing or reverting a superseded package is functionally impossible without manual archive extraction. Cross-ref H-010. | [pkm/installer.py:71](../../pkm/installer.py#L71), [pkm/installer.py:76](../../pkm/installer.py#L76), [pkm/cli.py:24-95](../../pkm/cli.py#L24) | Add `reinstall` subcommand: remove existing record (force=True), un-set `superseded_by` on predecessors if applicable, then re-run install flow. Update error messages once shipped. | open | |
| O-002 | Critical | Kernel upgrade leaves system unbootable on partial failure | `pkm upgrade linux-kernel` calls `remover.remove(force=True)` BEFORE installing the new kernel (`cli.py:319-322`). The old `/boot/vmlinuz-*`, `/lib/modules/<ver>/`, and config files are deleted from the RUNNING system. If the new install fails (disk full, bad archive, DB error), the system has no kernel modules for the live kernel, depmod will not have been run, and reboot is impossible without recovery media. Even on success, no grub-mkconfig, no initramfs regen, no UKI re-sign — bootloader still points at the deleted vmlinuz. | [pkm/cli.py:312-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L312), [packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:108-113](../../packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh#L108) | Make upgrade install-new-first-then-remove-old (or skip the remove entirely when supersedes covers the version change). Add kernel-aware post-install: `depmod`, `grub-mkconfig -o /boot/grub/grub.cfg`, regenerate initramfs, re-sign UKI if SecureBoot. Refuse to upgrade `linux-kernel` while DESTDIR matches running kernel without an explicit `--allow-kernel-replace`. | open | |
| O-003 | Critical | `pkm upgrade` never executes `post_install` hooks | Every package's `build.sh` defines `post_install()` for runtime-essential tasks (depmod for linux-kernel, desktop-file registration for firefox, ca-certificates trust store, gtk-update-icon-cache, glib-compile-schemas, ldconfig, etc.). `igos-build/builder.py:640-656` runs these at BUILD time inside chroot. The pkm installer/upgrade path (`pkm/installer.py:51-241`, `pkm/cli.py:286-326`) does not source the build.sh or invoke post_install. Comment in `packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:108` even says "Post-install: runs on the live system AFTER deploy" — but nothing runs it. Result: every upgrade leaves the system in a degraded state (icons not refreshed, modules not re-resolved, CA trust stale, schemas not compiled). | [pkm/installer.py](../../pkm/installer.py), [pkm/cli.py:286](../../pkm/cli.py#L286), [igos-build/builder.py:640](../../igos-build/builder.py#L640), [packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:108](../../packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh#L108) | Ship `post_install` (and `pre_install`) hook scripts inside the .igos.tar.gz archive at a known path (e.g., `var/lib/igos/packages/<name>/.scripts/post_install.sh`). Installer extracts them to a staging dir and executes after deploy + DB commit. Define standard hook environment ($PKG_NAME, $PKG_VERSION, $OPERATION=install\|upgrade). Audit all 80+ existing post_install functions for live-system safety (some currently assume DESTDIR which won't exist at runtime). | open | |
| O-004 | Critical | Shipped `/etc/pkm/repos.conf` is INI format but parser expects JSON | `packages/core/pkm/build.sh:35-46` writes the default `repos.conf` as INI (`[intergenos-current]\nurl = https://intergenstudios.com/...`). `pkm/repo.py:147-148` does `json.load(f)`. Parse fails, exception is swallowed, code silently falls back to `DEFAULT_REPOS` (`pkm/repo.py:76-82`) which points at `https://repo.intergenos.org/x86_64/current` — a DIFFERENT host than the shipped config. Every install on a stock ISO talks to the wrong URL, the user's repo customisations are ignored, and they have no signal anything is wrong. Cross-ref H-002 and L-004. | [packages/core/pkm/build.sh:35](../../packages/core/pkm/build.sh#L35), [pkm/repo.py:143-151](../../pkm/repo.py#L143), [pkm/repo.py:76-82](../../pkm/repo.py#L76) | Pick one format and align. Recommend INI (`configparser`) per the design doc at `docs/mirror/design.md:230-231`; rewrite `_load_repos`. Add a unit test that `packages/core/pkm/build.sh`'s emitted file parses cleanly. Surface `_load_repos` parse errors as a hard warning, not silent fallback. | open | |
| O-005 | High | `cmd_upgrade` does not resolve new dependencies introduced by upgrade | When firefox 138 → 139 introduces a new `libfoo` dep, `cli.py:312-326` only downloads + installs `firefox` itself. No `repo.resolve_dependencies()` call, unlike `cmd_install` (`cli.py:204`). New deps land as missing, firefox fails to launch, user has no warning. | [pkm/cli.py:312-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L312) | Wrap each upgrade target with `resolve_dependencies(pkg, db)` against the new version's depends list; install missing ones first. Treat as one transactional unit per package upgrade. | open | |
| O-006 | High | User-modified config files silently overwritten on upgrade | `remover.py:67-83` correctly preserves modified `etc/` configs (skips `os.remove`, records in `preserved_configs`). But `cmd_upgrade` then runs `installer.install` which calls `tar -xzf ... -C /` (`installer.py:160-163`) with default tar overwrite semantics — the preserved config is replaced with the new package's stock copy. No `.pacnew` / `.dpkg-new` style three-way merge artifact is created; the user's edits are simply gone. No notice printed. | [pkm/remover.py:67-83](../../pkm/remover.py#L67), [pkm/installer.py:160-163](../../pkm/installer.py#L160) | When installing into a path that exists AND has a tracked checksum diverging from the original, write new file as `<path>.pkmnew` and emit a "configuration files changed" summary at end of upgrade. Document the resolution workflow. | open | |
| O-007 | High | No rollback / snapshot mechanism despite atomicity claim in docs | `docs/users/package-management.md:98` claims "Package upgrades are treated as atomic 'supersedes' transactions, ensuring your system is never left in a broken, half-installed state if an operation fails or loses power." Reality: supersedes atomicity (`installer.py:196-225`) is SQLite-level only. The `pkm upgrade` path does `remove` then `install` (`cli.py:319-322`) — between those two filesystem ops there is no atomicity, no snapshot, no rollback. Power loss between remove and install = no firefox at all, no recovery. No `btrfs snapshot`, no `zfs snapshot`, no A/B partition scheme, no transaction log of file moves. | [docs/users/package-management.md:98](../../docs/users/package-management.md#L98), [pkm/cli.py:319-322](../../pkm/cli.py#L319) | Either (a) implement install-new-then-remove-old ordering so worst-case is two versions coexisting briefly (FS-level closer to atomic), or (b) integrate with btrfs subvolumes / overlayfs for true transactional upgrades, or (c) walk back the docs claim. Option (a) is lowest cost for highest safety win. | open | |
| O-008 | High | No bootloader / initramfs integration on kernel package install | Even if O-002 + O-003 are fixed (kernel install order + post_install execution), `packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:108-113` only runs `depmod`. There is no UKI build (`scripts/build-uki.sh` exists for ISO builds but isn't invoked on runtime kernel install), no shim+UKI re-sign for SecureBoot. **No mkinitcpio/dracut either — both RATIFIED-AGAINST.** After `pkm upgrade linux-kernel`, the next boot will load whichever vmlinuz the existing UKI references — possibly the just-deleted one. | [packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:108-113](../../packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh#L108), [scripts/build-uki.sh](../../scripts/build-uki.sh) | **RESOLVED-VIA-D-005 framing:** Add `packages/core/linux-kernel/post_install.sh` that runs depmod, regenerates the UKI envelope (which on plain installs carries a minimal/empty initramfs; on LUKS installs carries the custom busybox-static FDE-initramfs per D-001 I-D), and signs the UKI with the host MOK key. **NOT dracut, NOT mkinitcpio — both RATIFIED-AGAINST.** Gate the sign step on presence of a host MOK or shim cert. Cross-reference Lane B for SecureBoot integration. | open (per-D-005 implementation) | |
| O-009 | Medium | `pkm upgrade` does not log `upgrade` operation type | `cli.py:286-326` calls `remover.remove` (logs `remove`) and `installer.install` (logs `install`). No row written with `operation='upgrade'` and `old_version`+`new_version` populated together. `pkm history` shows the upgrade as a remove-then-install pair — old/new linkage lost, version-bisection from history harder. The DB schema supports it (`database.py:102-103`). | [pkm/cli.py:286-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L286), [pkm/database.py:415-428](../../pkm/database.py#L415) | After successful upgrade, write a single `db.log_operation("upgrade", name, old_version=..., new_version=..., method="archive")` row. Optionally suppress the constituent remove/install rows or tag them. | open | |
| O-010 | Medium | Version comparison is string-equality, not version-aware | `cli.py:296` and `cli.py:357` both use `remote["version"] != pkg["version"]` to decide "upgradable." Treats a downgrade (repo 5.0 → installed 5.1, e.g., after a CVE rollback in repo) as upgradable. Treats `1.10` vs `1.9` as ordered by string rather than version. Treats `5.2.37-1` vs `5.2.37-2` (release bump) ambiguously since release isn't in the version string. | [pkm/cli.py:296](../../pkm/cli.py#L296), [pkm/cli.py:357](../../pkm/cli.py#L357) | Introduce a `version.py` module with a `compare(a, b) -> -1\|0\|1` (vercmp/rpmvercmp style); use `> 0` to define upgradable. Add `release` to comparison key. Surface downgrades explicitly with `--allow-downgrade`. | open | |
| O-011 | Medium | No release-channel concept; single repo per host | No support for `stable` / `testing` / `edge` channels. `repos.conf` has one stanza pointing at `current/`. Cannot pin a single package to stable while running edge globally, cannot test a beta package without switching the whole index. `docs/mirror/design.md:230-231` lists `repos.d/` drop-in as TBD. | [pkm/repo.py:76-82](../../pkm/repo.py#L76), [packages/core/pkm/build.sh:35-46](../../packages/core/pkm/build.sh#L35), [docs/mirror/design.md:230-231](../../docs/mirror/design.md#L230) | Decide channel taxonomy (single-repo vs multi-channel) per Prime Directive (user control). | O-012 | Medium | `pkm update` documentation drift (`pkm sync` vs `pkm update`) | `docs/users/package-management.md:18` instructs `sudo pkm sync` (does not exist). `docs/users/package-management.md:36-38` says `pkm update` "Compares your installed packages against the synced index and upgrades any packages with newer versions available" — that's `pkm upgrade`'s behavior, not `pkm update`. | O-016 | Low | No transaction log of FS-level operations | Even with SQLite-atomic DB updates, the FS-level tar deploy (`installer.py:160-163`) is not journaled. | O-021 | High | `pkm upgrade` silently re-writes `config_files.original_checksum` to new stock — defeats future preservation | On upgrade: `pkm/remover.py:67-83` correctly preserves user-modified etc/ file by skipping `os.remove` (file stays on disk untouched). Effect: user's edits are lost (O-006) AND DB's notion of "what the stock content was" silently ratcheted to new stock — so even if file survived once, future preservation logic compares against wrong baseline. Compounds O-006's silent overwrite with silent baseline-erasure that breaks the preservation contract going forward. | [pkm/database.py:257-260](../../pkm/database.py#L257), [pkm/remover.py:67-83](../../pkm/remover.py#L67), [pkm/installer.py:160-163](../../pkm/installer.py#L160) | When inserting config_files for a package whose path already has a row with a different package_id (supersede/upgrade case), preserve original_checksum from prior row; OR write new stock checksum to a `vendor_checksum` column and only update `original_checksum` on first install. **Iter-2 verifications @ b3eb6318:** All 18 iter-1 findings (O-001..O-018) CONFIRMED. **Additional details:** O-006 has a UPSHIFT-Critical candidate (config-file silent overwrite + DB baseline ratchet — surfaced as separate O-021); the Lane C C-004 finding (post-install hooks never fire at INSTALL time) and my O-003 (never fire at UPGRADE time) confirmed as same root cause: no hook execution layer in runtime pkm. Doc-drift in docs/users/package-management.md is broader than iter-1's O-012 captured — surfaced O-019/O-020 as siblings.

**Iter-3 NEW findings (gap-find @ b0879120):** 13 new findings — 0 Holy-Grail, 1 Critical, 7 High, 3 Medium, 2 Low.

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| O-023 | High | Zero upgrade-availability notification surface — users on stock ISO never learn updates exist | docs/users/package-management.md:9 explicitly establishes "no auto-updater on a timer" as Prime-Directive position (correct). But corollary — "user must learn of updates and run pkm upgrade themselves" — has no implementation: zero systemd timers (verified `find . -name '*.timer'` empty across whole tree), no /etc/update-motd.d/ entry, no GNOME extension, no `intergen` daemon hook, no shell-rc print, no first-boot-greeter integration, no notify-send call anywhere in pkm/. User who follows docs and runs `pkm update; pkm upgrade` weekly is well-served; user who doesn't think to ever invoke it runs CVE-vulnerable indefinitely. | [docs/users/package-management.md:9](../../docs/users/package-management.md#L9), [pkm/repo.py:85](../../pkm/repo.py#L85), [packages/core/pkm/build.sh:65-70](../../packages/core/pkm/build.sh#L65) | Ship opt-in notification surface (default-on per first-boot-greeter): (a) `/etc/update-motd.d/90-pkm-pending` runs `pkm list upgradable` + prints count + last-sync timestamp; (b) user-systemd-timer (per-user, not system) runs `pkm update` weekly and writes count to ~/.cache/pkm/pending-count for greeter/shell-rc consumption; (c) document opt-out clearly. Prime-Directive-aligned: USER is told, USER decides when to act. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| O-024 | High | `_download` has no retry, no resume support, no backoff — flaky connection = full re-download from zero | `pkm/repo.py:221-228` is singular network fetch path. Single `urllib.request.urlopen` call, hard-coded 30s timeout, no Range header for resume, no exponential backoff, no retry-after handling, no max-retry count. Multi-GB upgrade on flaky connection: drop at 95% = full re-download from byte 0. Also: when `_download` raises (lines 339-342 in download_package), the EXCEPTION path returns early WITHOUT calling `local_path.unlink()` — partial file stays on disk until next invocation triggers checksum-mismatch unlink (line 347). On disk-full + offline scenario, retry-cycle leaks partial files. | [pkm/repo.py:221-228](../../pkm/repo.py#L221), [pkm/repo.py:339-342](../../pkm/repo.py#L339) | Wrap `_download` in retry loop with exponential backoff (3 attempts, 1s/4s/16s). Send `Range: bytes=N-` header when partial dest exists with size N to resume. Wrap urlopen call in try/finally that unlinks partial dest on exception. Add `--max-retries` and `--no-resume` flags. Honor `Retry-After` header on 503. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| O-025 | High | No free-disk-space preflight before download or extraction | Zero `shutil.disk_usage` / `os.statvfs` calls anywhere in pkm/. cmd_upgrade (cli.py:312-326) downloads archive to /var/cache/pkm/packages/ then extracts to / — both can fail on disk-full mid-write with no useful error, and (per O-016) no FS-level rollback. Worst case: extracting kernel-package tar mid-way through writing /lib/modules/<ver>/ → ENOSPC → tar exits → installer.py:166-167 returns error → DB never updated → user has half a kernel module tree on disk AND old kernel already deleted (O-002). With preflight check, operation could be refused before destructive remove step. | [pkm/repo.py:313-350](../../pkm/repo.py#L313), [pkm/installer.py:95-167](../../pkm/installer.py#L95), [pkm/cli.py:312-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L312) | Add `_check_disk_space(required_bytes, mount)` helper. Sum `size + installed_size * 1.5` across upgrade queue. Refuse with clear error before any download/remove if either /var or / is below threshold. Surface as `pkm upgrade --skip-disk-check` for power-users. Pairs with O-013. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-19 via T0-5 Q6 free-disk preflight helper** (commit subject `feat(pkm): Q5+Q6 helpers — service-restart scan + free-disk preflight` names this row's Q6 design directly). Resolution path: `pkm/preflight.py` helper module added with `check_disk_space(required_bytes, mount)` + `aggregate_upgrade_requirements(queue)`; cmd_upgrade integration call-site refuses with clear error before any download or remove step if either /var or / is below the computed threshold. Pairs with O-013 cache GC per the original recommendation. | code @ e3d9a0ab |
| O-026 | High | No `pkm hold` / `pkm pin` — cannot freeze a package version while upgrading others | Searched pkm/ for hold/pin/IgnorePkg — zero results. cmd_upgrade upgrades EVERY upgradable package, or all in args.packages. Common workflows blocked: (1) "freeze nvidia until next reboot window because in-use module," (2) "freeze linux-kernel until I've validated DKMS modules build against new headers," (3) "freeze glibc at tested version pending downstream ABI investigation," (4) "freeze python3 because pinned venvs." Workaround today is `pkm upgrade <list-of-everything-except-X>` — nothing prevents accidental `pkm upgrade` from clobbering the package user wanted held. Critical given O-002 (kernel upgrade unbootable on failure). | [pkm/cli.py:286-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L286), [pkm/database.py](../../pkm/database.py) (no held column in installed schema) | Add `held` BOOLEAN column to `installed` table (default 0). Add `pkm hold <pkg>` / `pkm unhold <pkg>` / `pkm list held` subcommands. cmd_upgrade filters held packages from upgrade list with informational notice. Allow override with `--ignore-holds` for emergency security upgrades. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| O-027 | Critical | `pkm upgrade` with no args silently mass-modifies system — no confirmation, no preview, no --dry-run | pkm/cli.py:51 defines `packages` as `nargs="*"` — bare `pkm upgrade` defaults to ALL upgradable. cmd_upgrade prints summary list then immediately proceeds to remove+install each one. No `input()` / Y-N prompt, no `--yes` / `--noconfirm` flag (because there's no prompt to skip), no `--dry-run` to preview, no transactional grouping. Compounds catastrophically with O-002 (kernel-upgrade-removes-first-then-installs): a non-interactive shell script that runs `pkm upgrade` weekly can brick system on a single bad download. Compounds with O-007 (no rollback). Holy Grail Rule 10 ("when in doubt, deny") applies — silent destructive mass-operation defaults are the opposite of default-deny. Distinct from O-002 (unbootable failure mode) and O-007 (no-rollback gap) — this is the missing user-consent gate that makes the others routinely triggerable instead of edge-case-only. | [pkm/cli.py:51](../../pkm/cli.py#L51), [pkm/cli.py:286-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L286) | Refuse bare `pkm upgrade` (no args) unless `--yes` or `--all` is passed. Always require explicit confirmation summary "About to upgrade N packages totaling M MB download + K MB disk. Proceed? [y/N]" on tty stdin. Add `--dry-run` that prints planned operation graph and exits 0 without touching anything. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-19 via T0-5 Q3 confirmation gate + plan summary + Q5 restart integration** (commit subject literally cites "(O-027)" in the parenthetical). Resolution path: cmd_upgrade now requires explicit confirmation when invoked with no args; --yes flag added for non-interactive contexts; --dry-run flag added that prints planned operation graph and exits 0 without touching anything; pairs with Q5 service-restart scan for end-of-upgrade summary. Holy Grail Rule 10 (default-deny on destructive operations) applied. | code @ 528913ca |
| O-028 | Medium | `priority` field in repo config is parsed but never consulted in dedup; comment lies | `pkm/repo.py:76-82` DEFAULT_REPOS dict declares `"priority": 100`. `pkm/repo.py:251-258` `search()` does `for index in self.indexes.values(): ... if r["name"] not in seen: seen[r["name"]] = r` — first-iteration-wins. Comment on line 253 says "Deduplicate — higher priority repo wins" — false. `get_package()` likewise iterates self.indexes.values() and returns first hit. Once multi-repo lands (post-O-011), this becomes real ordering bug: third-party repo enabled with priority=10 can shadow official intergenos repo (priority=100) purely by dict-insertion order. Rule 21 applies. | [pkm/repo.py:76-82](../../pkm/repo.py#L76), [pkm/repo.py:251-258](../../pkm/repo.py#L251), [pkm/repo.py:260-267](../../pkm/repo.py#L260) | Sort self.indexes consumers by `self.repos[name].get("priority", 0)` descending before iteration in search, get_package, list_available, and (eventually) the mirror-failover loop in O-031. Add unit test. Or remove field if multi-repo permanently deferred. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| O-029 | High | No service-restart / process-reload integration after upgrading running daemons | pkm/ has zero `systemctl` / `daemon-reload` / `needrestart` references. When `pkm upgrade nginx` runs, old `nginx` PID continues executing with deleted-but-open binary inode; new binary on disk is never activated. User has no notice; `nginx -v` reports new version while `systemctl reload nginx` is required and never prompted. Same for postgresql, mariadb, redis/valkey, sshd (most dangerous — locked-out-on-bad-config scenario), avahi, NetworkManager. Standard distro practice: needrestart (Debian/Ubuntu), `dnf needs-restarting` (Fedora). InterGenOS ships nothing equivalent. Holy-Grail-tangential: a recently-patched-for-CVE binary that's never restarted is unpatched in effect. | [pkm/cli.py:286-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L286), [pkm/installer.py:51-241](../../pkm/installer.py#L51) | After successful upgrade of any package owning a file in /usr/lib/systemd/system/*.service that is currently `is-active`, emit summary "Services using upgraded binaries: nginx, postgresql, sshd. Run `sudo systemctl restart <name>` to activate new version." Optionally `pkm upgrade --restart-services` flag (with sshd exclusion-by-default to avoid lockout). | **RESOLVED 2026-05-19 via T0-5 Q5 service-restart-scan helper** (commit subject `feat(pkm): Q5+Q6 helpers — service-restart scan + free-disk preflight` names this row's Q5 design directly). Resolution path: `pkm/services.py` NEW helper -- notify-only service-restart pattern -- scans installed manifest for systemd unit files (`/usr/lib/systemd/system/*.service` + `/etc/systemd/system/*.service`) and SysV init scripts (`/etc/init.d/*`), cross-references against currently-active services via `systemctl is-active`, and prints an end-of-upgrade summary. REBOOT_TRIGGER_PACKAGES frozenset escalates to REBOOT REQUIRED for kernel/glibc/systemd/microcode/bootloader packages where userspace restart cannot resolve live-vs-on-disk divergence. Surface: `scan_manifest_for_services()` + `query_active_services()` + `classify_restart_requirement()`. CLI wiring (`pkm restart-services` + cmd_upgrade integration) authored as the consumer side per dispatch matrix. | code @ e3d9a0ab |
| O-030 | High | No `pkm upgrade --security-only` mode; index has no security/CVE metadata | cmd_upgrade treats all upgrades identically — version diff = candidate. No way to say "I want only security fixes today, defer feature updates to weekend." InterGenOS.db index schema has no `security: bool`, no `cve: [CVE-2026-NNNN, ...]`, no `severity: critical|high|medium|low`, no `previous_version_eol`. Holy-Grail rule 1 ("no security trade-offs for convenience") implies users should be able to apply security fixes quickly without committing to full system upgrade. Currently they must either upgrade everything (risk: O-002 / O-005 / O-006 / O-007 stack) or upgrade-one-by-one with hand-curated CVE knowledge. Especially relevant given MS UEFI 2011 CA deadline (2026-06-27) — security-only update paths reduce risk of bricking near hard deadline. | [pkm/cli.py:286-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L286), [pkm/repo.py:23-40](../../pkm/repo.py#L23) | Extend InterGenOS.db index schema with optional per-package `security`, `cve_ids` fields populated at repo-build time from hand-curated `docs/governance/security-advisories.yml`. Add `pkm upgrade --security-only` filtering to packages with `security=true`. | closed | iter-4 @ 2026-05-19: CLOSED via Q7 (commit `f937c9e9`) — schema fields + boolean `--security-only` filter + `scripts/generate-repodb.py` reading hand-curated `docs/governance/security-advisories.yml`. The earlier iter-3 phrasing of the proposed remediation named "upstream CVE feeds" + severity-band scoring as inputs; both were rescoped. Hand-curation is the only authoring mechanism InterGenOS currently commits to, and the filter is boolean rather than severity-banded. |
| O-031 | Medium | No mirror failover during package download — single point of failure per repo | `pkm/repo.py:313-350` `download_package` resolves package → finds its `repo` name → constructs URL from `self.repos[repo]['url']` → single `_download` call. If resolving mirror is up enough for index-sync but per-archive fetch 503s/timeouts/connection-resets, operation fails with no fallback. No `mirrorlist` concept (multiple URLs per logical repo), no try-next-mirror loop, no automatic mirror health-check. Distinct from O-011 (release channels). Especially fragile given L-001 status (binary mirror is nascent — single point of failure today is the only point). | [pkm/repo.py:313-350](../../pkm/repo.py#L313), [pkm/repo.py:76-82](../../pkm/repo.py#L76) | Extend repo stanza schema with `urls = [primary, mirror1, mirror2]` (or accept multiple comma-separated URLs in url field). `_download` walks list on retry. Add `pkm mirror-test <repo>` to measure latency/availability per URL. Pair with O-024 retry/backoff. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| O-032 | Medium | AppArmor profile changes don't auto-load — depends on per-package post_install + O-003 fix | 14 packages ship AppArmor profiles to /etc/apparmor.d/usr.* (forge, intergen-mcp, pkm, first-boot-greeter, postgresql, mariadb, nginx, lighttpd, apache-httpd, caddy, etcd, haproxy, influxdb, memcached, valkey). 12 of those have `apparmor_parser -r` in build.sh post_install. But (a) O-003 establishes post_install NEVER fires at runtime; (b) apparmor CORE package's post_install is EMPTY, so no scan-and-reload-all on apparmor install; (c) packages/core/apparmor/profiles/usr.bin.* have no individual reload step — relying on generic mechanism that doesn't exist. Fixing O-003 doesn't fix this on its own; needs generic policy "any install that adds /etc/apparmor.d/* triggers `apparmor_parser -r` on those files." | [packages/core/apparmor/build.sh:65-70](../../packages/core/apparmor/build.sh#L65), [packages/extra/postgresql/build.sh:138-139](../../packages/extra/postgresql/build.sh#L138), [packages/core/apparmor/profiles/](../../packages/core/apparmor/profiles/) | When O-003 hook framework lands, add generic post-deploy step: scan installed manifest for paths matching `etc/apparmor.d/*` and run `apparmor_parser -r` on each new/changed file. Eliminates per-package boilerplate. Holy Grail Rule 5 — apparmor on disk that doesn't enforce is no defense. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| O-033 | High | Cascade-rebuild needed on library upgrade is invisible; SONAME bump silently breaks rdeps | cmd_upgrade upgrades one package at a time, never checks `get_reverse_depends()` for upgrade target. Upgrading glibc 2.39 → 2.40 (or any SONAME-bumping library: openssl, sqlite, libxml2, icu) silently leaves 50-600+ dependents linked against old SONAME `.so` file. No SONAME-tracking in installed table, no SONAME-comparison logic in (nonexistent per O-010) version module, no warning at upgrade-time. User sees `pkm upgrade glibc` succeed, then random binaries fail with `error while loading shared libraries: libc.so.6`. Infrastructure exists (`get_reverse_depends` on database.py:386) but cmd_upgrade never uses it. | [pkm/cli.py:286-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L286), [pkm/database.py:386](../../pkm/database.py#L386) | Phase 1: at upgrade-time, call `get_reverse_depends` on each target; warn "upgrading <name> from X to Y will affect N reverse dependencies." Alternate SONAME-aware mechanisms (per-library SONAME column, ELF extraction at package-build time, refuse-on-SONAME-bump with `--allow-soname-break` override, auto-include-rdeps batch) are non-committed scope. | closed-phase-1 | iter-4 @ 2026-05-19: Phase 1 LANDED at `da304855` (`pkm.cascade.format_reverse_dep_warning` + upgrade-orchestration call site). The iter-3 phrasing's Phase 2 SONAME-aware refuse semantics were rescoped at sprint closure 2026-05-19; alternate mechanisms would require explicit operator authorization to scope a design pass. |
| O-034 | Low | DKMS / out-of-tree kernel modules not preserved across kernel upgrade | pkm/ has zero DKMS references. `packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:58-100` ships kernel + headers + `/lib/modules/<ver>/build` symlink to support DKMS builds, but pkm has no dkms-build trigger on kernel upgrade. User installs NVIDIA / VirtualBox / ZFS modules via DKMS against running kernel 6.18.10-igos; `pkm upgrade linux-kernel → 6.19.0-igos` removes old `/lib/modules/6.18.10-igos/` tree — old DKMS modules vanish — and never rebuilds for 6.19.0-igos. On reboot, NVIDIA driver / ZFS / VirtualBox is gone. Lower severity because dkms isn't shipped today, but linux-kernel build.sh already prepares for it ("supports out-of-tree module builds (DKMS, NVIDIA, VirtualBox, ZFS)" — line 71) — aspirational-stub class per Rule 21. | [packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:71](../../packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh#L71), [pkm/cli.py:286-326](../../pkm/cli.py#L286) | Either (a) ship `dkms` package and add kernel-package post_install that triggers `dkms autoinstall -k <new_kernel_ver>`, OR (b) walk back "supports DKMS" claim in linux-kernel/build.sh:71 until integration ships. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-19 via Option (b) walk-back of DKMS aspirational claim per Rule 21 (no stubs)** (commit subject literally cites "O-034 walk back DKMS aspirational claim per Rule 21"). Resolution path: `packages/core/linux-kernel/build.sh:71` line edited to remove the "(supports DKMS, NVIDIA, VirtualBox, ZFS)" out-of-tree-module promise; integration not yet shipped, so the claim was vacuous. | O-035 | Low | No GPG keyring rotation mechanism; key compromise requires shipping new pkm package via same channel | GPG_KEYRING = /etc/pkm/trusted.gpg (pkm/repo.py:74) is shipped once by packages/core/pkm/build.sh and never refreshed. No `pkm refresh-keys`, no key-expiry handling, no trust-on-update for new signing keys, no key-rotation policy doc. If S1 or S2 release-signing key is compromised, only mitigation is shipping new pkm package — through same compromised repository. Compares unfavorably to apt (`apt-key`, `signed-by`), pacman (`pacman-key --refresh-keys`), dnf (`/etc/pki/rpm-gpg/`). For a project with "Holy Grail security ONLY" posture, key-rotation is missing primitive. | [pkm/repo.py:74](../../pkm/repo.py#L74), [packages/core/pkm/build.sh:42-46](../../packages/core/pkm/build.sh#L42), [pkm/release-keys.json](../../pkm/release-keys.json) | Document key-rotation procedure in `docs/governance/signing-key-rotation.md` covering: (1) primary + standby key, (2) cross-signing chain so new key validated by old key, (3) `pkm refresh-keys` command to fetch latest trust bundle (with TOFU acceptance + manual verification), (4) revocation broadcast via repo index metadata. Required before gpg_verify flag flips on in repos.conf for production. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |

| ID | Severity | Title | Description | Code refs | Remediation plan | Status | Verified |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| P-001 | Holy-Grail | No GPL source-availability mechanism on shipped ISO | InterGenOS ships GPL'd binaries (kernel, glibc, gcc, coreutils, systemd, hundreds of others). GPLv2 §3 / GPLv3 §6 require either bundled corresponding source OR a written offer valid 3 years OR equivalent network access. The ISO ships only binaries; the design doc at `docs/research/build_system/vps_source_mirror_design_2026-04-02.md` describes `intergenstudios.com/intergenos/sources/` but the README, LICENSE, and any installed legal doc make **no written offer** and the mirror is described as a build-time source repo, not a §6d-compliant public-network source-distribution channel with the durability/access commitments GPL requires. Tip commit body lists "VPS source mirror completion" as Upcoming — i.e., not yet implemented. Risk: distributing the ISO to a single third party in current form is a textbook GPL violation. Cross-ref L-001. | [README.md:163](../../README.md#L163), [docs/mirror/design.md:1](../../docs/mirror/design.md#L1), [docs/research/build_system/vps_source_mirror_design_2026-04-02.md:12](../../docs/research/build_system/vps_source_mirror_design_2026-04-02.md#L12) | (a) Add a written offer per GPLv3 §6b to `LICENSE` / `/usr/share/doc/intergenos/COPYING.offer` shipped on ISO, OR (b) bring the `https://intergenstudios.com/intergenos/sources/` mirror live with all package source tarballs and document the §6d access promise in a top-level `SOURCES.md` + README license section, AND (c) ensure ISO ships an `/usr/share/doc/intergenos/SOURCES` text file telling the user where to find it. Block v1.0 ISO publish until one of these paths is in place. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-18 via v1.0 legal-readiness sprint** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). Resolution path: 9 core legal docs landed: SOURCES.md (GPL §6d+§6b) + TRADEMARK.md + PRIVACY.md (GDPR/CCPA) + EXPORT-NOTICE.md (ECCN 5D002) + DCO.md + AUTHORS + THIRD-PARTY-NOTICES.md (5504 lines covering 795 packages 66 licenses) + governance/license-policy + governance/fedora-shim-redistribution. | code @ 52f8d17e |
| P-002 | Critical | LFS/BLFS attribution declares CC-BY-NC-SA — incompatible with commercial distribution | `CREDITS` lines 12, 25 attribute Linux From Scratch and BLFS books under "Creative Commons Attribution-**NonCommercial**-ShareAlike 2.0." InterGenOS uses these books' methodology and quotes their build instructions extensively (BLFS database, kernel-config convergence, package selection). If the project ever moves to a commercial/sponsored distribution model — or if a user asserts "you're distributing CC-BY-NC material commercially" — the NC clause is triggered. Also the LFS book itself is CC-BY-NC-SA 3.0 today (not 2.0 — drift), and methodology/instructions arguably are not copyrightable but our derivative documentation (`docs/operations/*`, package build.sh scripts that paraphrase BLFS steps) is. Need a clean separation between "we follow LFS methodology" (uncopyrightable facts) and "we redistribute LFS prose" (CC-BY-NC-SA-bound). | [CREDITS:12](../../CREDITS#L12), [CREDITS:25](../../CREDITS#L25) | (1) Update CC-BY-NC-SA version from 2.0 → current (3.0 for LFS book, verify BLFS), (2) audit `packages/*/build.sh` and `docs/` for verbatim LFS/BLFS prose vs paraphrased methodology, (3) add a "Methodology vs. Verbatim Text" disclaimer to CREDITS stating that procedure facts are uncopyrightable and that no verbatim LFS/BLFS text is bundled into shipped binaries or distributed ISOs (only into `docs/` repo content which is itself separately-licensed). | **RESOLVED 2026-05-18 via v1.0 legal-readiness sprint** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). Resolution path: 9 core legal docs landed: SOURCES.md (GPL §6d+§6b) + TRADEMARK.md + PRIVACY.md (GDPR/CCPA) + EXPORT-NOTICE.md (ECCN 5D002) + DCO.md + AUTHORS + THIRD-PARTY-NOTICES.md (5504 lines covering 795 packages 66 licenses) + governance/license-policy + governance/fedora-shim-redistribution. | code @ 52f8d17e |
| P-003 | Critical | FDK-AAC redistribution restrictions ignored | `packages/desktop/fdk-aac/package.yml:5` declares `license: FDK-AAC`. The Fraunhofer FDK-AAC license requires patent-license fees for commercial distribution of AAC encoders/decoders that exceed certain quantity thresholds, and bars certain hardware-product distribution. Most distros (Fedora, Debian) **explicitly omit fdk-aac from main repos** for this reason and place it in non-free / RPM Fusion. InterGenOS ships it in the `desktop` tier with no patent disclaimer, no opt-in gating, no "non-free" repo separation. | [packages/desktop/fdk-aac/package.yml:5](../../packages/desktop/fdk-aac/package.yml#L5) | Either (a) move fdk-aac to an opt-in/non-free repo with clear patent-warning notice, OR (b) drop it from the default ISO entirely (most distros' choice), OR (c) document the patent posture in a `LEGAL/PATENT-NOTICE.md` and require explicit user opt-in via pkm `install-helper` pattern (the model already used for proprietary apps). v1.0 ship-blocker. | **RESOLVED 2026-05-18 via v1.0 legal-readiness sprint** (commit subject names this row in the closure list). | P-015 | Holy-Grail | ffmpeg ships `--enable-nonfree --enable-libfdk-aac` — resulting binary is NOT redistributable, license metadata is wrong | `packages/desktop/ffmpeg/build.sh:13-33` invokes `./configure --enable-gpl --enable-version3 --enable-nonfree --enable-libfdk-aac --enable-libx264 --enable-libx265 --enable-libmp3lame --enable-openssl`. FFmpeg's own documentation is explicit: `--enable-nonfree` produces a binary "with restrictions on distribution" — specifically, the FDK-AAC linkage (and OpenSSL-with-GPL combination per FFmpeg license-FAQ) makes resulting libavcodec.so and ffmpeg binary **non-redistributable, period.** `package.yml:5` declares `license: LGPL-2.1-or-later`, which is **demonstrably impossible** for this build configuration. FFmpeg project warns: "If your derived work is going to be redistributed, you'll need to drop the nonfree options." Compounds P-003 (fdk-aac patent posture) — at the binary level ffmpeg is the redistribution vector. Iter-1/2 missed because P-003 looked at fdk-aac package alone; ffmpeg build wiring was not checked. | [packages/desktop/ffmpeg/build.sh:13](../../packages/desktop/ffmpeg/build.sh#L13), [packages/desktop/ffmpeg/build.sh:16](../../packages/desktop/ffmpeg/build.sh#L16), [packages/desktop/ffmpeg/build.sh:22](../../packages/desktop/ffmpeg/build.sh#L22), [packages/desktop/ffmpeg/package.yml:5](../../packages/desktop/ffmpeg/package.yml#L5) | (a) DROP `--enable-nonfree` and `--enable-libfdk-aac` from default ffmpeg build (standard distro choice — Fedora/Debian both do this); ship separate `ffmpeg-nonfree` opt-in package via helper pattern (P-006) if needed, OR (b) accept non-redistributable status and gate ISO build to NEVER ship libavcodec.so or ffmpeg binary — implausible given desktop tier need. | P-020 | High | No PRIVACY.md / no privacy notice surface — Prime Directive holds in code, but legal posture is undocumented for jurisdictions requiring disclosure | Grep across repo for "GDPR" / "CCPA" / "privacy notice" finds 74 hits but ZERO are user-facing privacy policy or PRIVACY.md/PRIVACY_NOTICE document. Verified: no PRIVACY* file exists at root or in docs/. Substantively, intergen does NOT exfiltrate data (verified). HOWEVER: (1) GDPR Art. 13/14 requires privacy notice even for purely-local processing if data subject is in EU and ANY personal data is processed (hostname, search query, model-download manifest with timestamps all qualify). (2) CCPA §1798.130 requires "Do Not Sell" / collection-disclosure notice even for businesses that don't sell data. (3) HuggingFace download request inherently sends client-IP + User-Agent — under EU jurisdiction that's personal data crossing border to US service. (4) Default-collected systemd journal logs, intergen conversation history, pkm install logs all qualify as "personal data" under GDPR's broad definition. Iter-1/2 didn't audit privacy because Lane P was framed as "license compliance," not "regulatory compliance." | (no existing file; gap), [intergen/model_manager.py:16](../../intergen/model_manager.py#L16), [intergen/tools/web_search.py:154](../../intergen/tools/web_search.py#L154) | (1) Add `PRIVACY.md` at repo root: enumerate what's processed locally, what crosses network, user's control surface. | P-021 | High | Vendored Rust crates (Cargo.lock with 420 crates) in `packages/core/cargo-c/` carry no license inventory | packages/core/cargo-c/Cargo.lock (420 `[[package]]` entries) is dependency graph for cargo-c. Each crate listed downloaded at cargo-c build time from `registry+https://github.com/rust-lang/crates.io-index` and statically linked into resulting cargo-cbuild / cargo-cinstall binaries shipped on ISO. Static linkage means each crate's license obligations attach to final binary. Most crates.io crates are MIT/Apache-2.0 dual-licensed, but some have copyleft variants (MPL-2.0, EPL, LGPL) and BSD-3-Clause-with-advertising-clause attribution. No license inventory generated from lockfile; cargo-c's package.yml declares only its own top-level license. | [packages/core/cargo-c/Cargo.lock:1](../../packages/core/cargo-c/Cargo.lock#L1), [packages/core/cargo-c/package.yml](../../packages/core/cargo-c/package.yml) | Generate cargo-c-LICENSES.txt from lockfile via `cargo-deny` or `cargo-license` at build time, ship to /usr/share/licenses/cargo-c/THIRD-PARTY.txt. Add lockfile-driven license-extraction as generic pkm build-step hook for future Rust/Go/Node packages. Block ISO build if any "unknown" or copyleft-but-undisclosed license surfaces. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| P-022 | High | License DRIFT — `mariadb` declares `"GPL-2.0 AND LGPL-2.1"` but bundles FMT library (MIT) as build-time source artifact without inventorying it | packages/extra/mariadb/package.yml:5 declares `license: "GPL-2.0 AND LGPL-2.1"`. package.yml:13-15 adds second source entry: `fmt-12.1.0.zip` from github.com/fmtlib/fmt. fmt library is MIT-licensed and gets statically linked into MariaDB server binary via cmake's ExternalProject. Shipped mariadbd binary therefore carries MIT + GPL-2.0 + LGPL-2.1 obligations, but package.yml inventory only mentions first two. Generic class of drift wherever package.yml has multiple `source:` entries. | [packages/extra/mariadb/package.yml:5](../../packages/extra/mariadb/package.yml#L5), [packages/extra/mariadb/package.yml:13](../../packages/extra/mariadb/package.yml#L13) | (1) Update mariadb license to `"GPL-2.0 AND LGPL-2.1 AND MIT"`; (2) sweep all 794 packages for multi-source entries via yq query, cross-check each secondary source's actual license against declared compound license; (3) add pkm precommit hook flagging multi-source packages whose license field is not SPDX compound expression. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| P-023 | Medium | Bundled X.509 CA certificate in `docker/shim-build/vendor-cert/` is a build-time dev cert but has no LICENSE / README clarifying intent and not-for-shipping status | docker/shim-build/vendor-cert/intergenos-secure-boot-ca.pem (valid certificate, "InterGenOS Secure Boot CA", validity 2026-05-14 to 2028-05-13). | P-024 | Medium | No US BIS / EU dual-use export-control notice despite shipping OpenSSL + GnuPG + cryptsetup + GnuTLS + NSS strong crypto by default | InterGenOS ships at least 9 strong-cryptography packages by default: openssl, gnutls, libgcrypt, nss, nettle, gpgme, gpgmepp, gnupg2, cryptsetup. US 15 CFR Part 740.17 (TSU — encryption license exception, "publicly available source code") arguably covers most once published, but standard distro practice is to ship `LEGAL/EXPORT-NOTICE.md` that: (a) declares export classification (typically 5D002 ENC self-classified, TSU exception claimed), (b) names BIS notification reference if one was filed, (c) lists embargoed jurisdictions where user must not download. Most distros (Fedora's `legal-notice` package, Debian's /usr/share/common-licenses/, Red Hat's MRP notice) ship some such notice. None exists in InterGenOS tree. Risk is low but documenting posture is best-practice. | [packages/core/openssl/package.yml:5](../../packages/core/openssl/package.yml#L5), [packages/core/gnupg2/package.yml](../../packages/core/gnupg2/package.yml), [packages/core/cryptsetup/package.yml](../../packages/core/cryptsetup/package.yml), [packages/core/gnutls/package.yml](../../packages/core/gnutls/package.yml) | Add `docs/legal/EXPORT-NOTICE.md`: classify ISO as 5D002 ENC, claim TSU exception per 15 CFR 740.17(b)(2), enumerate strong-crypto components, list embargoed jurisdictions (current OFAC list). Mirror for EU dual-use rules. Reference in README License section. | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
| P-025 | Medium | Build-time toolchain licenses (gcc, glibc, perl, python, ruby, rust) not inventoried — non-propagating but documenting is best-practice and SBOM completeness gap | packages/core/ contains gcc-core, glibc-core, perl-core, python, ruby, rust, cargo-c, rust-bindgen, python-cryptography, python-pefile (10 build/runtime toolchain packages). The licenses of these tools do not propagate to user-program output under standard library and GCC-Runtime-Library-Exception carve-outs. But: (1) any package that statically links libstdc++ or libgcc inherits GCC RLE conditions — needs to be documented for SBOM tools; (2) Python interpreter shipped with system carries PSF-2.0 obligations on interpreter binary itself; (3) Ruby's license is bespoke and triggers attribution requirements when ruby binary is distributed. Most distros ship a `/usr/share/licenses/__BASESYSTEM__/` or equivalent. | [packages/core/gcc-core/package.yml](../../packages/core/gcc-core/package.yml), [packages/core/glibc-core/package.yml](../../packages/core/glibc-core/package.yml), [packages/core/python/package.yml](../../packages/core/python/package.yml), [packages/core/ruby/package.yml](../../packages/core/ruby/package.yml), [packages/core/rust/package.yml](../../packages/core/rust/package.yml) | Generate `docs/legal/TOOLCHAIN-LICENSES.md` distinguishing (a) toolchains shipped on ISO and user-invokable (gcc/python/perl/ruby/rust → ship their LICENSE per P-004), (b) toolchains used at build time only and not on ISO (nasm, autoconf, m4 → document but no ISO obligation). | open | iter-3 @ b0879120: NEW |
